<th>Understanding the Columns on the VDL (cont.)</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>that contain them on the right click menu option or the Due List menu option.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>IVP/IVPB Medication Tab:</strong> Column is not available for this Tab.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>IV Medication Tab:</strong> Column is not available for this Tab.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Dosage:</strong> Lists the total dosage and schedule information for the medication order.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>IVP/IVPB Medication Tab:</strong> This column is replaced by the Infusion Rate column.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>IV Medication Tab:</strong> This column is replaced by the Infusion Rate column.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Route:</strong> Also called “Med Route,” indicates how a clinician will administer the medication to the patient. For example: Intravenous, Intramuscular, Intradermal, Subcutaneous.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>This section describes the columns within the Medication Order Display Area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Next Dose Action:</strong> Replaces the previous “Admin Time” column on the Unit Dose and IVPB tabs and provides information on medication that is late and/or due for removal along with the admin date and time.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>NOTE: For non-standard schedules such as DAY@HHMM, HHMM or other odd schedules, Removal Times cannot be calculated due to the lack of a Frequency. Regardless of the Prompt for Removal in BCMA code value for the orderable item, no Removal Times will display in BCMA for these non-standard schedules. These types of schedules must be avoided for Medications Requiring Removal (MRR) orders<strong>.</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Continuous Medication Order:</strong> If a medication is late, the text is in red. If a cell in the Alert column contains the Requires Removal icon and the medication is due to be removed, the hover hint</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/034.png)Understanding the Columns on the VDL (cont.)</td>
<td><blockquote>
<p>text consists of “REMOVE” along with the removal date and time. If the next action is for it to be administered (i.e., Given), the column contains the word “DUE” and the next Admin Time as a date/time on a separate line. If the next action for a medication requiring removal is for it to be Removed, but is late, the column contains “LATE-RM” and the next Removal Time as a date/time on a separate line, with all text in red font.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Multiple Administration Times:</strong> If a Continuous-type order has multiple administration times, each administration time appears as a separate line item on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>IV Medication Tab:</strong> Column is not available for this Tab since IVs do not have administration times associated to them.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Last Action:</strong> Describes the last action taken on the orderable item and the date/time of this action. When BCMA “refreshes,” it updates medication order information, plus this column and the Status column.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Multiple Line Items:</strong> If multiple line items are displayed, the same last action time displays for each related item.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Renewed Medications:</strong> Medications renewed during the Start/Stop Time Parameters selected on the BCMA VDL, display the last action and time of the preceding order.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>IV Medication Tab:</strong> Column is not available for this Tab.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>“Unknown” Status:</strong> If an order created in BCMA CHUI Manual Medication Entry is not completed with a valid administration status, it will display as “Unknown” in the Last Action column.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Last Site:</strong> Shows the location of the last injection site for the orderable item shown, applicable to administrations</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<th>Understanding the Columns on the VDL (cont.)</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>that participate in injection site rotation. When BCMA “refreshes,” it updates this column.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>IV Medication Tab:</strong> Column is not available for this Tab.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Exceptions</p>
<p>Besides the Medication Order Display Area, the IV Medication Tab also includes the IV Bag Chronology and the IV Bag Detail display areas. Each area is described below:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>IV Bag Chronology:</strong> Lists the action taken on each IV bag, whether the bag is available, the Unique Identifier Number, and the contents of each bag.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>IV Bag Detail:</strong> Provides a history of an IV bag, such as the date and time the medication was administered, the initials of the clinician who administered the medication, any actions taken on the medication, and any comments entered by a clinician.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>

<colgroup>

</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconsorting-the-contents-of-a-column" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/035.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/036.png)Sorting the Contents of a Column</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA displays medication information in columns on the BCMA VDL. You can sort the contents of each column alphabetically, by ascending or descending order. You cannot change the order of the actual columns within the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Information in columns is actually sorted numerically, then alphabetically in the columns. On the Unit Dose VDL in Inpatient Order Mode, the default sort order upon logging in to BCMA is in ascending order based on the date/time in the Next Dose Action column, so “older” items are at the top.</p>
<p>To sort the contents of a column</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Sort By command in the Due List menu. The Sort By drop-down menu displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">s</span></strong> to display the Sort By drop-down menu. </p>
<p>Example: Sort By Drop-down Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/037.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the name of the column that you want to sort alphabetically on the BCMA VDL. The contents of the column changes accordingly.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the arrow keys to select the desired column name, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to sort the column alphabetically.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconresizing-the-columns-on-the-bcma-vdl" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/038.png)Resizing the Columns on the BCMA VDL</h3></td>
<td><p>You can quickly — and easily — resize the columns on the BCMA VDL. Here’s how.</p>
<p>To resize columns on the VDL</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Place the mouse pointer over the vertical border (line) of a Column Header. A crosshair displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Crosshair Used to Resize a Column</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/039.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Press and drag the crosshair to the right to increase the column width, or to the left to decrease the column width.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> There is a minimum size allowed for each column so you do not accidentally overlay one column onto another, and find yourself unable to access a column.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="refreshing-the-vdl" class="Subheading-Style">Refreshing the VDL</h3></td>
<td><p>You can “refresh” the BCMA VDL to ensure that the medication order information displayed is the most current received from Inpatient Medications V. 5.0. When you use this feature, BCMA “loads” active medication orders onto the BCMA VDL, and refreshes the information in the Status and Last Action columns.</p>
<p>To refresh the VDL</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/040.png)Select the Refresh command in the Due List menu. The BCMA VDL refreshes so you are receiving the most current medication order information. It also updates the information in the Status and Last Action columns.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">r</span></strong> to select the Refresh command. The BCMA VDL “refreshes” with current medication order information, and also updates the Status and Last Action columns.</p>
<p>Example: Command Used to Refresh the VDL</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/041.png)</p>
<p>— THEN —</p>
<p>(SEE NEXT PAGE)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Refreshing the VDL (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: Message When VDL Refreshing</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/042.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Notice the message that displays when you refresh the BCMA VDL, and that the Status and Last Action columns are updated once this process is complete.</p></li>
</ol></td>

<span id="_Toc199860811" class="anchor"></span>Getting Started

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="signing-on-to-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">Signing on to BCMA</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/043.png)</p></th>
<th><p>Signing on to BCMA V. 3.0 may vary slightly, as a result of how site parameters are set for your division. For example, your medical center may require that you specify your division, enter an electronic signature code, or indicate if you are working with a nursing instructor. If so, you will receive all or just a few of the associated screens shown in this section when accessing BCMA V. 3.0.</p>
<p>To sign on to BCMA</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Double-click on the BCMA icon on your desktop. BCMA displays the BCMA Splash Screen then prompts you for your VistA sign on credentials.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: BCMA Splash Screen</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/044.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Signing on to BCMA (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>To sign in using two-factor authentication (2FA) you will select the appropriate PIV credentials.</p></li>
</ol>

</ol>

<ol start="4" type="1">

</ol></th>

<td><p><span id="p58_46" class="anchor"></span>For Divisions with Nursing Students</p>
<p>If you are a nursing student, your nursing instructor must enter their Access and Verify Codes, at the Instructor Sign-On dialog box provided below before you can have full access to the patient’s VDL. BCMA will then verify that the instructor has been assigned the PSB INSTRUCTOR security key, and is a recognized nursing instructor.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If Instructor Codes are not entered, BCMA will automatically default to Read-Only mode (indicated by the “READ-ONLY” message in the title bar.) In order to administer medications, you must exit Read-Only BCMA and sign on with your instructor. For more information on using Read-Only BCMA, please refer to the chapter entitled, “Read-Only and Limited Access BCMA.”</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> An Instructor, logged on for the purpose of monitoring a Student, is not authorized to witness High Risk/High Alert administrations. If the Instructor currently logged on with a student, attempts to witness the administration of a high risk/high alert medication, the following message will display: “An instructor monitoring a student does not have authority to witness a high risk/high alert medication.”</p>
<p>To enter nursing instructor codes</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Request that your nursing instructor enter their Access and Verify Codes in the Instructor Sign-On dialog box, and press Sign On.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">Sign On</span> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

Working With Patient Records

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconopening-a-patient-recordtip-box-with-lightbulb-icon" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/054.png)Opening a Patient Record![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/055.png)</h3></th>
<th><p>Before you can administer active medications to a patient, you must open the patient record (VDL). You can also open a patient record while an existing record is still open on the screen. BCMA may prompt you to confirm any active medication orders that have not been viewed, then proceeds to close the current record.</p>
<p>To open a patient record</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the Scan Patient Wristband dialog box, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>I<strong>f the Scanner Status is “Ready,”</strong> scan the bar code on the patient’s wristband or the Veterans Health Information Card (VHIC).</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Not Ready,”</strong> click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">enable scanner</span></strong> button to enable the scanner. You are ready to scan when the Scanner Status indicator is <strong>GREEN</strong> and displays “Ready.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enable scanner</strong></span> button, press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter,</span></strong> or press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt‑b</span></strong> to enable the scanner.</p>
<p>Example: Scan Patient Wristband Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/056.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> Deceased patients cannot be opened via the Scan Patient Wristband dialog or Unable to Scan functionality. They can only be opened via Limited Access, Read-Only, and Edit Med Log.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> to return to the VDL and access the Menu Bar — without opening a patient record — and do one of the following:</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Print all reports by ward, except for the Cumulative Vitals/Measurement Report. A patient’s file must be opened to access patient-specific reports. See the chapter entitled, “Viewing and Printing BCMA Reports” for more information.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Edit the Medication Log to make changes to medication administration entries that have been created during the medication administration process. Access the Edit Med Log command from the File menu. See chapter entitled, “Editing the Medication Log” for more information.</p></li>
<li><p>Open a patient record in Limited Access Mode. See chapter entitled, “Read-Only and Limited Access BCMA” for more information.</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>If the scan is successful, skip to step #5. If you are unable to scan the patient wristband, click the unable to scan button, and perform the following actions at the Unable to Scan dialog box:</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>unable to scan</strong></span> button, press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter,</span></strong> or press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt‑u</span></strong>.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Select a Reason</strong> (required) for scanning failure from the drop-down list.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Enter a Comment</strong> (optional) that will aid your OIT staff in trouble-shooting the problem. The Comment field is limited to 150 characters.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/057.png)Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Click <span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to complete the Unable to Scan event. The Patient Select dialog box displays. Proceed to Step#3.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Patient Wristband<br />
Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/058.png)</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>At the BCMA – Patient Select dialog box, enter one of the following search criteria in the Patient Name field:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient name (Last, First)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient Social Security Number (SSN)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Rm-Bed</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Ward</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA automatically searches for the patient record(s) that match the criteria - as you are typing. You must enter at least 2 characters to initiate the search. There is no need to press ENTER. Note that the search is not case sensitive.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<td><p>Example: Patient Select Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/061.png)</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the patient you are requesting is displayed in the Patient List</strong>, click on the patient record you want to access, and click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to access the patient’s VDL. Proceed to Step #5.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to go to the Patient List. If multiple records are displayed, use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the patient record. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to access the patient’s VDL in Read-Only mode.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the patient you are requesting is not displayed in the Patient List:</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If more records are retrieved than can be displayed in the Patient List, <span class="smallcaps">scroll bars</span> will appear to allow you to scroll through the data. Scroll to the patient record, click on the patient record you want to access, and click <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> to access the patient’s VDL in Read-Only mode.</p></li>
<li><p>If records are retrieved, but you do not see the intended patient record, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #3 above.</p></li>
</ul></td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</td>
<td colspan="2"><ul>
<li><p>If you see a “No patients matching…” message, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #4 above.</p></li>
<li><p>If you see a “Too many patients matching…” message, the system found more than 100 records that matched your criteria. Re-enter more specific patient criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>The Patient Confirmation dialog box displays after a successful scan, or upon selecting a patient after documenting an Unable to Scan event. The patient’s personal data displays, such as name, SSN, date of birth, ward, room-bed, allergies, ADRs, and Patient Record Flag (PRF) assignments, if applicable.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Patient Confirmation Dialog Box<br />
(After Successful Scan)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/062.png)</p></td>

<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/063.png)Example: Patient Confirmation Dialog Box<br />
(After Unable to Scan Event)</p>
<ol start="7" type="1">

</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the patient’s record is marked as “Sensitive,” the SSN and DOB fields will be blocked out. See the section “If Patient’s Record Marked as Sensitive” for reviewing information on a sensitive record.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If any active PRF assignments exist for this patient, the <strong><span class="smallcaps">details</span></strong> button will be enabled in the Patient Flags section of the dialog box. It is strongly recommended that you click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">details</span></strong> button to view the Patient Record Flag report, especially for behavioral flags, to view information which may be critical to patient and employee safety.</p></th>

<tr class="odd">
<td>Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="8" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the information matches</strong> the data printed on the patient’s wristband:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If a confirmation checkbox displays as a result of a Unable to Scan event, check the box and confirm that you have used two acceptable forms of patient identifiers.</p></li>
<li><p>Click YES to access their VDL and to begin administering active medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the patient record is Sensitive:</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If a confirmation checkbox displays as a result of an Unable to Scan event, check the box and confirm that you have used two acceptable forms of patient identifiers.</p></li>
<li><p>Click ACCEPT then YES to access their VDL and to begin administering active medications to the patient. An entry is created automatically in a log for your Information Security Officer.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If this information does</strong> not <strong>match</strong> the data on the patient’s wristband, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel,</span></strong> and verify the patient’s identity against the information on their wristband.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>yes</strong>,</span> <span class="smallcaps"><strong>accept</strong>,</span> or <span class="smallcaps"><strong>cancel</strong></span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to access the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>If Patient’s Record Marked as “Sensitive”</p>
<p>BCMA uses the standard Patient Lookup. If a patient record is marked as “Sensitive,” you may (or may not) receive a Restricted Record Warning message. This will depend on whether you hold the security key for this type of patient record. A “Sensitive Patient” is one for whom a record exists in the DG SECURITY LOG file (#38.1) with a SECURITY LEVEL field (#2) marked as “Sensitive.”</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/064.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/065.png)Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/066.png)Example: Sensitive Patient Confirmation Dialog Box</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Every time a “Sensitive” patient record is accessed, an entry is created in a log for the Information Security Officer at your medical center. The log lists the individual who accessed the record, how they accessed the record, and for what length of time. That way, the Security Officer can monitor the patient’s privacy and make sure that “need to know” information is disseminated accordingly.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> For opening Sensitive patients during an Unable to Scan event, the checkbox must be checked to enable the Accept button. Click <strong>ACCEPT</strong> to enable the Yes button. Click <strong>YES</strong> to open the patient’s record.</p>
<p>To review information for a sensitive record</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Warning message, and click <strong>ACCEPT</strong>, which acknowledges your understanding of the security warning, Click <strong>YES</strong> to access the patient’s VDL and begin administering active medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">yes</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<ol start="9" type="1">
<li><p>Continue with the medication administration process.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p>Opening a Patient Record (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/067.png)</p></td>
<td><p>If Patient Transfer Notification Message Displays</p>
<p>BCMA displays the Patient Transfer Notification message for Inpatient orders, only, if the patient has had a movement type (i.e., usually a transfer) within the site-definable parameter, and the last action for the medication occurred before the movement, but still within the defined timeframe. You can define this parameter, the Patient Transfer Notification Timeframe, on the BCMA Site Parameters Tab of the BCMA GUI Site Parameters application</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The display of the message is dependent on the last action displayed in the “Last Action” column of the BCMA VDL. BCMA evaluates the last action performed each time the Unit Dose or IVP/IVPB Medication Tabs are refreshed.</p>
<p>To review Patient Transfer Notification message</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Patient Transfer Notification message, and click OK to return to the patient’s VDL and begin administering active medications to the patient. BCMA will determine each last action that falls within the site-specified Notification “window” and display the patient’s movement in the “Last Action” column, along with the existing last action.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/068.png)Example: Patient Transfer Notification Message</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue with the medication administration process.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconclosing-a-patient-record" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/069.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/070.png)Closing a Patient Record</h3></td>
<td><p>Once you finish administering active medications to your patient, you can close their patient record (VDL), and open another patient record. This feature is particularly useful when you need to leave the patient’s room for a few minutes, and do not want to leave their record open on your computer.</p>
<p>To close a patient record</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Close Patient Record command from the File menu. The Information message displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+f</strong></span> to display the File menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">c</span></strong> to display the Information message.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/071.png)Example: Information Message</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Information message, provided above, displays only for IV Piggyback medications since you automatically view Unit Dose orders when the BCMA VDL opens. The message lets you verify if you want to view active orders under the IVP/IVPB Medication Tab before closing the patient’s record.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">yes</span></strong> to close the current record without viewing medication orders, for the patient, on other Medication Tabs. The Patient Lookup dialog box displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Closing a Patient Record (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">no</span></strong> to view active medication orders under the Medication Tab listed in the Information message.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">yes</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA provides the “BCMA Idle Timeout” site parameter for defining the number of minutes that an idle BCMA session can stay open. Once the allowable time-out has been reached, BCMA will close. If the BCMA session displays a prompt, it will not time-out until the prompt is answered. The allowable entry for this parameter is 1 to 1440 minutes/day. The default is 30 minutes.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Toc206069022" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 3: Working with the Cover Sheet

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-1" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></th>
<th><p>Use this chapter when you need to access the BCMA Cover Sheet to display alternate views of medication data related to the selected patient.</p>
<p>This chapter describes features and functionality of the Cover Sheet, how to access the four user-selectable views, and how to manipulate the data within each view.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="what-is-the-cover-sheet" class="Subheading-Style">What is the Cover Sheet?</h3></td>
<td><p>The BCMA Cover Sheet supplements the VDL medication tabs by providing users with four alternate views of primary medication data related to the selected patient – all in a single, easy-to-use location. The Cover Sheet tab increases the amount of information available to the user by displaying data related to expired, discontinued, and future orders. Each view has a unique data set and format, and allows users to drill down to view additional order and/or IV bag details, when applicable.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet tab functions as a display tool only, and does not allow the user to edit any data, administer medications, or take action against a patient’s record. No special security key is required to access the Cover Sheet – it is available to all users that have access to the BCMA GUI application, and it is fully functional in Read-Only mode.</p>
<p>Upon opening a patient record, BCMA opens to the Unit Dose tab by default. In order to display the Cover Sheet, the user must select the Cover Sheet tab by clicking the tab to the left of the Unit Dose tab.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet supports both Inpatient Order Mode and Clinic Order Mode. While the Cover Sheet is displayed, you can switch between Order Modes. The Clinic Order Mode displays a column for Clinic location and omits the HSM column.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="features-of-the-cover-sheet" class="Subheading-Style"><br />
Features of the Cover Sheet</h3>
<h2 id="section-1"></h2></td>
<td><p>Views</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet tab provides four user-selectable views for the current patient:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Medication Overview:</strong> This is the default view. It displays all Active and Future orders, as well as orders that have Expired/Discontinued (DC'd) within the last 24 hours. This view includes all Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB, and large volume IV orders.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>PRN Overview:</strong> Displays Active and Future PRN orders, as well as PRN orders that have Expired/DC'd within the last 24 hours.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>IV Overview:</strong> Displays large volume IV bag information from Active orders, as well as from orders that have Expired/DC’d within the last 24 hours.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders:</strong></p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>When Inpatient Order Mode is selected, this view defaults to displaying all orders that have Expired/DC'd within the last 24 hours, as well as orders expiring today and tomorrow. In addition, the user can temporarily expand the display to include orders that have expired within the last 48 and 72 hours, as well as future orders expiring within 48 and 72 hours after midnight tonight.</p></li>
<li><p>When Clinic Order Mode is selected, and the Medication Overview or PRN Overview is selected, the Expired/DC'd orders sections will display orders that have Expired or have been Discontinued within the last 7 days. When the Expired/DC'd view is selected, orders will display that have Expired or have been Discontinued within the last 7 days, Today, and within the next 7 days.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Features of the Cover Sheet (cont.)</p>
<h2 id="section-2"></h2></td>
<td><p>Display Features</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Displays the Medication Overview by default.</p></li>
<li><p>Allows the user to select alternate views from a drop-down field; a table then displays the data associated with the selected view.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays data in groups that the user can expand and collapse as desired. Each group is expandable to display data or collapsible to hide data.</p></li>
<li><p>Each group within a view is named and displays the number of items within the group to the right of the group name in brackets, e.g., Active [10 Orders].</p></li>
<li><p>Each group has a header row that identifies the columns of data displayed in the group. As the user expands order and/or bag detail rows to reveal more data, appropriate headers appear to describe the data displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays up to 4 previous actions per order.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays information by order, instead of administration, as shown on the existing BCMA medication tabs.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays Active, Expired, and Discontinued (DC'd) orders, including orders Expiring Today and Expiring Tomorrow.</p></li>
<li><p>The default timeframe for displaying Expired or DC’d orders in each view is the current time minus 24 hours from the date/time the VDL is accessed, unless otherwise stated below.</p></li>
<li><p>Allows the user to temporarily expand the display to include Inpatient orders that have expired within the last 48 and 72 hours, as well as future orders expiring within 48 and 72 hours after midnight tonight. Group headings change dynamically, based on selected timeframe. When Clinic Order Mode is selected, the Expired/DC'd view displays orders that have Expired or have been Discontinued within the last 7 days, Today, and within the next 7 days</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p>Features of the Cover Sheet (cont.)</p>
<h2 id="section-3"></h2></td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Displays Future orders, i.e., any active order with a future start date.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays icons for: STAT; Order Flag; IV Order – No action taken yet; Witness required/recommended for High Risk/High Alert Administrations; Requires Removal; Hazardous to Handle; and, Hazardous to Dispose.</p></li>
<li><p>Displays icons for STAT, Order Flag, and IV Order – No action taken yet, and Witness required/recommended for High Risk/High Alert Administrations.</p></li>
<li><p>In Special Instructions column, displays message in cell: “Too much information to display. Use right-click menu to display full text” for orders containing Special Instructions / Other Print Info that exceed 180 characters. Displays this same message as hover text when hovering over a field containing Special Instructions / Other Print Info that exceed 180 characters.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The STAT icon will display for STAT, ASAP, and NOW orders only if the PRIORITIES FOR ACTIVE NOTIFY is properly set in the Inpatient Medications system parameters.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Cover Sheet tab does not display the green/white Schedule Type indicators found on the existing BCMA medication tabs (Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB, and IV).</p>
<p>Limitations by Design</p>
<ul>
<li><p>When the Inpatient Order Mode is selected, the Cover Sheet displays only Inpatient Orders. When the Clinic Order Mode is selected, the Cover Sheet displays only Clinic Orders. Each Order Mode is mutually exclusive.</p></li>
<li><p>In Inpatient Order Mode, when the Cover Sheet is accessed, the Virtual Due List Parameters and Schedule Types groups are disabled (grayed out).</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Features of the Cover Sheet (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>In Clinic Order Mode, when the Cover Sheet is accessed, the Clinic Order Date and Schedule Types groups are disabled (grayed out).</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Disabled Virtual Due List Parameters<br />
and Schedule Types</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/072.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><p>While the Cover Sheet is active, the Scanner Status is<br />
“Not Ready.” This means you cannot:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Scan a medication</p></li>
<li><p>Manually enter an IEN number</p></li>
<li><p>Edit order data</p></li>
<li><p>Take action against a patient's record</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>The IV Overview does not display IV bags for ward stock or future orders.</p></li>
<li><p>The Cover Sheet does not include printing or reporting functions.</p>
<p>Similarities to the VDL</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>While the Cover Sheet is active (any view), you can document PRN Effectiveness.</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet columns can be sorted in ascending or descending order by clicking a column header. Note that all groups within a view will sort, and whenever BCMA loads, the default sort order set by the user returns.</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet columns can be resized by placing the mouse pointer over the vertical border (line) of a column header, and dragging the crosshair to increase or decrease the column width. The column widths set by the user are saved on the Cover Sheet screen.</p></li>
<li><p>Patient Demographics can be accessed by clicking the patient information box on the Cover Sheet.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Features of the Cover Sheet (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Refresh can be used to reload Cover Sheet data.</p></li>
<li><p>Right-clicking on a Cover Sheet row will provide the following standard BCMA options:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Available Bags (for IV orders)</p></li>
<li><p>Display Order</p></li>
<li><p>Special Instructions / Other Print Info</p></li>
<li><p>Display Reason for Order Flag, if applicable</p></li>
<li><p>Med History</p>
<p>Keyboard Shortcuts</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The Cover Sheet includes several keyboard shortcuts as shown below:</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

Example: Cover Sheet Shortcut Keys

|                    |                                                                                            |
|--------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Use This Shortcut: | To Make This Occur:                                                                        |
| F2                 | Switch to Inpatient Order Mode                                                             |
| F3                 | Switch to Clinic Order Mode                                                                |
| F9                 | Display Cover Sheet tab                                                                    |
| Alt-V              | Activate Cover Sheet View drop-down list box                                               |
|                    |                                                                                            |
| Shift-Tab/Tab      | Shift focus from group to group (previous/next group) and through active fields on screen. |
| Up/Down Arrow      | Shift focus from one row to the next (previous/next row)                                   |
| Left/Right Arrow   | Expand or collapse a row, if applicable.                                                   |
| Alt-Up/Down Arrow  | Scroll entire Cover Sheet up and down                                                      |
|                    |                                                                                            |
| Shift-F9           | Expand/Collapse the first group in a view                                                  |
| Shift-F10          | Expand/Collapse the second group in a view                                                 |
| Shift-F11          | Expand/Collapse the third group in a view                                                  |
|                    |                                                                                            |
| Ctrl-Alt-V         | Show Available Bags for highlighted item                                                   |
| Ctrl-Alt-O         | Display Order for highlighted item                                                         |
| Ctrl-Alt-E         | Display Med History for highlighted item                                                   |
| Ctrl-Alt-S         | Display Special Instructions / Other Print Info                                            |

An Icon Legend is accessible via the View Menu, showing icons and indicators used on the Cover Sheet and medication tabs.

Example: Icon Legend

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/073.png)

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="cover-sheet-screen-medication-overview" class="Subheading-Style">Cover Sheet Screen: Medication Overview </h3></td>
<td><p>The Medication Overview displays and groups active, expired or discontinued (DC’d), and future orders for the current patient. The total number of orders per group displays in brackets next to each group heading. The groups are displayed top down as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Active</strong> orders are those orders with an order start date/time less than or equal to the current date/time minus the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter, and an order stop date/time greater than the current date/time.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Future</strong> orders are those orders whose start date/time is <em>greater than</em> the current date/time plus the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Expired/DC’d</strong> orders are those orders that have expired or have been discontinued within the last 24 hours for Inpatient orders, and last 7 days for Clinic orders.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/074.png)Example: View: Medication Overview (Inpatient Order Mode)

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/075.png)Example: View: Medication Overview (Clinic Order Mode)

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/076.png)

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Cover Sheet Screen: Medication Overview (cont.)</td>
<td><p>The Medication Overview provides three levels of detail for each order displayed.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>The top level displays order and next administration data, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Icons: When applicable, the following icons or indicators will display:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>STAT:</strong> (Black exclamation Point on yellow circle) displays for STAT orders.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Order Flag:</strong> (Red block) indicator displays for any flag from CPRS/ Pharmacy, with the corresponding “Reason for Flag” comment available from the right-click menu.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Override/Intervention reasons:</strong> (Yellow block) indicator displays in verified “Ver”</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Cover Sheet Screen: Medication Overview (cont.)</th>
<th><p>cell when provider overrides or pharmacist interventions are associated with an order.</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>IV Order – No action taken yet:</strong> (Question mark) Displays for large volume IV orders, where no action has been taken yet.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>High Risk/High Alert – Witness Required/Recommended: (</strong>Red exclamation point on yellow triangle) displays High Risk/High Alert medicationorders that require or recommend a witness during administration.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Requires Removal: (</strong>Black arrow on orange patch) displays when a transdermal medication requires removal.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Hazardous to Handle:</strong> (Red ‘X’ superimposed on white hand) displays when a drug, additive or solution requires use of Personal Protective Equipment (PPE).</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Hazardous to Dispose:</strong> (Red ‘X’ superimposed on lidded trash can) displays when a drug, additive or solution necessitates the user follow proper disposal procedures.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Status: the current status of the order (i.e., Active, Expired, Hold)</p></li>
<li><p>Ver: the initials of the nurse who verified the order or three asterisks (*) indicating non-nurse verified.</p></li>
<li><p>Type: the schedule type of the order (C for Continuous, O for One Time, OC for On Call, P for PRN)</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Cover Sheet Screen: Medication Overview (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/077.png)</p></td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Medication: the orderable item associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Dosage, Route: the dosage and route of the order, separated by a comma</p></li>
<li><p>Schedule: the order schedule (i.e., Q2H, BID)</p></li>
<li><p>Next Action: one of the following:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>“DUE”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action taken for active orders that have defined administration times in MM/DD@HHMM format.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>“Missed”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action taken if administration date/time exceeds the “After Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter in MM/DD@HHMM format.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>“Provider Hold”</strong> for active orders on provider hold</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Blank</strong> for PRN, On Call, and One-Time orders</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions or “Other Print Info” associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Order Stop Date: the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against this specific order, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Actions whose activity date exceeds the “Med History Days Back” site parameter will not be displayed.</p>
</blockquote></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: If the order is an IV order, then the Bag ID header and field displays, which is the unique identifier for the bag associated with this action.</p></li>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action, and the date/time of the action in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the status of the administration (i.e., Given, Held, Refused, Missing, etc.).</p></li>
<li><p>If the order has a PRN schedule type, the following headers and fields will display:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>PRN Reason:</strong> the PRN reason associated with the action</p></li>
<li><p><strong>PRN Effectiveness:</strong> the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p></li>
</ul></td>

<td><h3 id="cover-sheet-screen-prn-overview" class="Subheading-Style">Cover Sheet Screen: PRN Overview</h3></td>
<td><p>The PRN Overview displays and groups active expired or discontinued and future orders with a schedule type of PRN for the current patient. The total number of orders per group displays in brackets next to each group heading.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Actions whose activity date exceeds the “Med History Days Back” site parameter will not be displayed.</p>
<p>The groups are displayed top down as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Active</strong> orders are those orders with an order start date/time less than or equal to the current date/time minus the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter, and an order stop date/time greater than the current date/time.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Future</strong> orders are those orders whose start date/time is greater than the current date/time plus the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Expired/DC’d</strong> orders are those orders that have expired or have been discontinued within the last 24 hours for Inpatient orders, and last 7 days for Clinic orders.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<li><p><strong>IV Order – No action taken yet:</strong> (Question mark) Displays for large volume IV orders, where no action has been taken yet.</p></li>

<colgroup>

<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Cover Sheet Screen: PRN Overview (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Status: the current status of the order (i.e. Active, Hold, Expired)</p></li>
<li><p>Ver: the initials of the nurse who verified the order or three asterisks (*) indicating non-nurse verified.</p></li>
<li><p>Medication: the orderable item associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Schedule: the order schedule (i.e., Q4H PRN)</p></li>
<li><p>Dosage, Route: the dosage and route of the order separated by a comma</p></li>
<li><p>Last Given: the last administration and the date/time the action was performed for the orderable item in ACTION MM/DD@HHMM format<br />
> **NOTE:** Last Given may not be associated with this PRN order. It may be the last time the medication was given on a separate order.</p></li>
<li><p>Since Last Given: the number of hours and minutes since the last administration of the orderable item in ##d ##h ##m format. (e.g. 1d 10h 23m ago)</p></li>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions associated with the order</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/081.png)Cover Sheet Screen: PRN Overview (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p><strong>Order Start Date:</strong> the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Order Stop Date:</strong> the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against this specific order, and will contain a header and information in the following order.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action and the date/time of the action in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the status of the administration (i.e., Given, Held, Refused, Missing, etc.)</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Reason: the PRN reason associated with the action</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness: the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>The third level of the PRN Overview displays comments associated with the action and includes the following header and information.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Comment By: the initials of the person that entered the comment and the date/time the comment was entered in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The IV Overview displays and groups IV bag information on active, expired, and discontinued large volume IV orders for the current patient selected. The number of IV bags per group displays in brackets next to each group heading. The groups are displayed top down as follows:</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Cover Sheet Screen: PRN Overview (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p><strong>Infusing</strong> is any bag that is currently infusing on an active, expired, or discontinued order.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Stopped</strong> is any bag that is currently stopped on an active, expired, or discontinued order.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>All Other</strong> is any bag that is not infusing or stopped on an active order.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>

<td>The IV Overview provides two levels of detail for each bag displayed.</td>

</ul>

<td><h3 id="cover-sheet-screen-expireddcd-expiring-orders" class="Subheading-Style">Cover Sheet Screen: Expired/DC’d/ Expiring Orders</h3></td>
<td><p>The Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders functions differently, depending on whether the Inpatient Order Mode or the Clinic Order Mode is selected.</p>
<p><strong>Inpatient Orders</strong></p>
<p>By default, the Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders view in Inpatient Order Mode displays and groups expired, discontinued, and expiring orders within a 24 hour period. Using drop-down lists, the user can temporarily expand the display timeframe of this view to 48 or 72 hours in the past or future.</p>
<p>Example: Fields to Expand Display Timeframe (Inpatient Order Mode)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/085.png)</p>
<p>The specified timeframe and the total number of orders per group displays in brackets next to each group heading. The groups are displayed top down as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Expired/DC’d within last (24) Hours:</strong> those orders that have expired or have been discontinued within the last 24 hours. If the user specifies an expanded timeframe for past orders, the heading and orders will dynamically update according to the number of hours specified.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Expiring Today:</strong> those orders that have not yet expired, but will expire before midnight of the current day.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Expiring within next (24) Hours</strong> (after Midnight tonight): those orders that expire 24 hours after midnight of the current day, but before midnight of the following day (tomorrow). If the user specifies an expanded timeframe for future orders, the heading and orders will dynamically update according to the number of hours specified.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<li><p><strong>Expiring Today:</strong> those orders that have not yet expired, but will expire before midnight of the current day.</p></li>
</ul>

<td>Cover Sheet Screen: Expired/DC’d/ Expiring Orders (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Status: the current status of the order (i.e., Active, Hold, Expired)</p></li>
<li><p>Ver: the initials of the nurse who verified the order or three asterisks (*) indicating non-nurse verified.</p></li>
<li><p>Type: the schedule type of the order (C for Continuous, O for One-Time, OC for On-Call, P for PRN)</p></li>
<li><p>Schedule: the order schedule (i.e., Q2H, BID)</p></li>
<li><p>Medication: the orderable item associated with the order</p></li>

<li><p>Next Action: one of the following:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>“DUE”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action taken for active orders that have defined administration times in MM/DD@HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>“Missed”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action taken if administration date/time exceeds the After Scheduled Admin Time site parameter in MM/DD@HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>“Provider Hold”</strong> for active orders on provider hold</p></li>
<li><p>Blank for PRN, On Call, and One-Time orders</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul></td>

</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against this specific order, and includes a header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Actions whose activity date exceeds the “Med History Days Back” site parameter will not be displayed.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: If the order is an IV order, then the Bag ID header and field displays, which is the unique identifier for the bag associated with this action.</p></li>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action and the date/time of the action in MM/DD@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the status of the administration (i.e., Given, Held, Refused, Missing, etc.)</p></li>
<li><p>If the order has a PRN schedule type, the following headers and fields will display:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>PRN Reason:</strong> the PRN reason associated with the action</p></li>
<li><p><strong>PRN Effectiveness:</strong> the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p></li>
</ul>

</ol>
<ul>

<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment</p></li>
</ul></td>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="accessing-the-cover-sheet" class="Subheading-Style">Accessing the Cover Sheet</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA opens to the Unit Dose tab by default. You must select the Cover Sheet tab in order to view the Cover Sheet.</p>
<p>When a patient record is open, if the patient status is admitted, the Inpatient order mode defaults. If the patient status is not admitted, the Clinic order mode defaults.</p>
<p>To Access the Cover Sheet</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Open a patient record using any of the available methods.</p></li>
<li><p>Click on the Cover Sheet tab to display the Cover Sheet for the current patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>F9</strong></span> to display the Cover Sheet tab for the current patient.</p>
<p>Example: Cover Sheet Tab</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/090.png)</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>After a brief “Loading Cover Sheet” message, the Cover Sheet displays the default Cover Sheet view, the Medication Overview, for the current patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Accessing the Cover Sheet (cont.)</th>
<th><p>Example: Default Cover Sheet View (Inpatient Order Mode)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/091.png)</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet opens to the Medication Overview by default, for the selected Order Mode, either Inpatient or Clinic. You may select one of the four available Cover Sheet views.</p>
<p>To select a Cover Sheet View</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>From the Cover Sheet tab, click on the View drop-down list box, and then select one of the available views from the list.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt-w</strong></span> to activate the View drop-down list box, and then press any <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> key to quickly switch to another view.</p>
<p>Example: View Drop-down List Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/092.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<td><h3 id="using-the-cover-sheet" class="Subheading-Style">Using the Cover Sheet</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/093.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/094.png)</p></td>
<td><p>You can control the way data is displayed on any Cover Sheet view by using the mouse and keyboard shortcuts. By default, all groups are expanded per view, and all rows are collapsed. When the user expands or collapses data in a view, it remains that way until the user exits BCMA.</p>
<p>To Expand and Collapse Groups and Rows</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>From the Cover Sheet tab, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click on the ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/095.png) to expand a collapsed group or row.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click on the ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/096.png) to collapse an expanded group or row.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click anywhere on a row that begins with ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/097.png)or ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/098.png) to expand/collapse the group or row.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcuts:</strong> To Expand/Collapse the <u>selected</u> data row: Press the <strong><span class="smallcaps">left</span></strong> or <strong><span class="smallcaps">right</span></strong> <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> key.</p>
<p>To Expand/Collapse <u>groups</u> within a view:</p>
<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 23%" />
<col style="width: 76%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><strong><span class="smallcaps">shift-f9</span></strong></td>
<td>Expand/Collapse the first group in a view</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><strong><span class="smallcaps">shift-f10</span></strong></td>
<td>Expand/Collapse the second group in a view</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><strong><span class="smallcaps">shift-f11</span></strong></td>
<td>Expand/Collapse the third group in a view</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> These shortcuts function when data rows exist in a group.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The selected group or row expands or collapses. The following example shows a fully expanded row of data, along with the conditional headers that display.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>

<th>Using the Cover Sheet (cont.)</th>
