<span id="_Toc199860815" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 4: Administering Active Unit Dose Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-2" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></td>
<td>Use this chapter when you need to administer active Unit Dose medications to patients on your ward and in the clinic. The options and features available within the BCMA VDL apply specifically to active Unit Dose medication orders only.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconpreparing-to-administer-unit-dose-medications" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/102.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/103.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/104.png)Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications</h3></td>
<td><p>Before administering any active Unit Dose medications to a patient, review this section to learn more about the Schedule Types for Unit Dose medications that you can administer, including medication orders that display on the BCMA VDL, and how BCMA indicates “actions” taken on medications displayed on the VDL.</p>
<p>Then you will be ready to define the administration Start and Stop Times and Schedule Types of the medications that you want to display on the BCMA VDL, and to administer active Unit Dose medications to your patients.</p>
<p>Schedule Types that You Can Administer</p>
<p>You can administer medications for active Unit Dose medication orders with the Schedule Types listed below.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Continuous</strong>: A medication given continuously to a patient for the life of the order, as defined by the order Start and Stop Date/Time. Includes Fill-on-Request orders.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Fill-on-Request Orders:</strong> These are grouped, based on whether their Schedule Type is Continuous or PRN. This depends on whether the schedule contains the characters “PRN.” If BCMA does not find these characters, it looks for administration times, and places the order accordingly on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>PRN</strong>: A medication dosage given to a patient on an “as needed” basis. Includes Fill-on-Request orders.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>On-Call:</strong> A specific order or action dependent upon another order or action taking place before it is carried out.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>One-Time:</strong> A medication order given one time to a patient such as a STAT or a NOW order. This order type displays for a fixed length of time on the BCMA VDL, as defined by the order Start and Stop Date/Time.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> Each time that you open a BCMA VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass.</p>
<p>Medication Orders that Display on the VDL</p>
<p>Once a Unit Dose medication order becomes “active,” it displays on the BCMA VDL under the Unit Dose Medication Tab for the Start and Stop Date/Times and Schedule Types selected on the BCMA VDL. This status occurs once a pharmacist or nurse verifies a medication order using Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 or CPRS, provided the nurse holds the PS Nurse Verify key. This includes orders on “Hold” and any orders entered through the Unit Dose or IV package. Orders placed “On Hold” by a provider display grayed out on the BCMA VDL. You can only mark these order types as “Held,” although it is not necessary that you do so.</p>
<p>Active Unit Dose orders display under the Unit Dose Medication Tab, except for orders entered with a Medication Route of IV PUSH or IV Piggyback. (These order types display under the IVP/IVPB Medication Tab.)</p>
<p>BCMA determines <em>when</em> to display an order on the BCMA VDL by subtracting the information in the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter field from the Start Date/Time of the medication order. You can define this parameter using the Parameters Tab in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/105.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/106.png)Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Medications Available for Scanning</p>
<p>Administering Unit Dose medications to a patient involves the scanning of the patient’s medication (drug) bar code. BCMA recognizes the following number on the Unit Dose Medication Tab:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Internal Entry Number (IEN):</strong> Drug numbers provided<br />
on medication bar codes are considered a unique drug identifier by the Pharmacy. BCMA validates the bar code scanned against the IEN of DRUG file (#50) and/or the SYNONYM field (#.01) of the DRUG file (#50), to ensure that a valid number exists for the dispensed drug and strength scheduled for administration. BCMA also recognizes National Drug Code (NDC) unique identifier product numbers found on manufacturer bar code labels, which are also stored in the SYNONYM field (#.01) of the DRUG file (#50).</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Marking the Order Status/Last Action Column</p></li>
</ul>
<p>When you administer a Unit Dose medication to a patient, BCMA electronically documents the “action” taken on the medication by displaying a letter, for example a “G” (for “Given”), in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. This information also displays on the Medication Log Report and the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The Last Action column lists the “last action” taken on an orderable item and the date/time of this action, so the nurse will know when the patient last received and last had a medication requiring removal removed for any dose of a medication regardless of the Schedule Type selected. This information helps to prevent the same medication from being given to the patient from another order or schedule type.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the orderable item is the same, the Last Action column lists the last administration action.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/107.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/108.png)<br />
Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the patient has two different orders, for the same orderable item, the last administration of either of these orders displays in the Last Action column for both orders. You can view the MAH Report to determine from which order the medication was given on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a medication was not administered before to the patient, the Last Action column will not list a date/time.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Understanding the Status of a Medication Order</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Once you scan and mark a medication as Given, you cannot scan it again for the same administration time. If you do, you will receive an Error message. You can, however, change the status from “Given” to “Not Given” by using the “Undo–Given” option — provided you are the individual who originally marked it as “Given,” or you have been assigned the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>You can mark a Unit Dose medication with the following status:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Given to Not Given</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Removed to Given</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Held or Refused to Given</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Missing to Given, Held, or Refused</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> A patch marked as “Given,” displays on the BCMA VDL each time BCMA is opened — until it is marked as “Removed” — even if the order is discontinued or expires, or the patient is discharged or<br />
re-admitted to your medical center. The patch will fall off the display after the order’s stop date if the “Patch Display Duration” site parameter value is set between 7 and 14 days.</p>
<p>Information Stored by BCMA</p>
<p>BCMA stores the following information each time you administer an active Unit Dose medication to a patient:</p>
<p>Patient</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Location of the patient (i.e., bed, ward, division, clinic)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Clinician administering the medication</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Clinician who created the Medication Log Entry</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Entered date and time</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Audit information (i.e., clinician, text, date and time)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Administration date and time</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Status of the administration, such as Given, Held, Refused, Missing, or Removed (in the case of a patch)</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Orders changed using the “Undo–Given” option do not display a code (letter) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. This status appears only in the Audit Trail section of the Medication Log Report, not on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>“Cancelled” administrations are not stored in the Medication Log.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>“Unknown” Status: If an order created in BCMA CHUI Manual Medication Entry is not completed with a valid administration status, the Admin Status will be stored as null (blank), but will display as “U” (unknown) in the BCMA VDL Status column and “Unknown” in the Last Action column.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Number of minutes that the dose was given too Early or too Late to the patient</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Reason that a PRN medication was administered and the medication effectiveness</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Medication, dosage, and/or number of units given</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Any comments associated with the drug administration dose</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Injection site for medications that must be injected</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="how-bcma-validates-patient-and-medication-information" class="Subheading-Style">How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information</h3></td>
<td><p>When used as intended, BCMA serves as an excellent check-and-balance system for patients and VAMCs. The chances for errors increase when the scanning process is circumvented — entered manually — during the medication administration process. In short, here is the validation process completed by BCMA V. 3.0.</p>
<p>First Validation by BCMA</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/109.png)When you scan the bar code on a patient’s wristband, BCMA automatically verifies/validates the patient’s identity and provides important clinical information via a Confirmation dialog box and the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>Second Validation by BCMA</p>
<p>The second validation by BCMA occurs when you scan the bar code on the patient’s medication or when you use the Unable to Scan feature. During this validation process, BCMA verifies whether the medication is located in the DRUG file (#50), if the patient has an active order entered into Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 for the medication scanned, and if the dosage is correct and timely for the medication ordered. The lookup is restricted to the IEN and SYNONYM field (#.01) of the DRUG file (#50).</p>
<p>A variety of dialog boxes will display for each patient, depending on the medications scheduled for administration. (See the descriptions provided below to learn when a dialog will display on the VDL.) If the administration is successful, the patient’s VDL displays the letter “G” (for “Given) in the Status column to document that the patient received the medication as required.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the order is active, and includes more than one unit per dose, a dialog box displays so you can select and scan each unit dose scheduled for administration.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient has more than one active order for the same medication, with different schedule types, both orders display on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you give the medication outside the medication administration window — Early or Late — (as defined by a site parameter), the Medication Log dialog box displays, requiring that you complete the Comments field. The order is then logged as Early or Late in the Medication Variance Log.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a medication is scanned and marked as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you scan a medication twice for the same administration time, you will receive an Error message.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Unable to Scan Medication</p></li>
</ul>
<p>If you experience a medication scanning failure, you can select the Unable to Scan feature to administer the medication and inform your support staff of the failure, After entering a reason for the failure and an optional comment, the Medication Verification dialog displays, where you can choose one of the following options:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Verify Medication:</strong> This (default) option provides an entry field in which the user types the number from the bar code label on the medication or IV bag to verify the medication being administered to the patient. BCMA validates the entry against the order and displays the matching dispense drug or bag components. Best practice dictates that you always attempt to verify the medication first. You may retry if your entry does not result in a match.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Verify Five Rights:</strong> This option provides a method for administering a medication in the event that Verify Medication failed, or, for example, when the number on the bar code label is not readable, or there is no label. You must confirm that each of the five rights of medication administration have been physically verified (right patient, right medication, right dose, right route, right time) before you can continue the administration process.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Note:</strong> Refer to your BCMA Coordinator and site policy for guidance on the use of the Verify Five Rights option.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Verify Five Rights option is only available if the Five Rights Override Parameters are enabled for Unit Dose and IV medications in the BCMA Site Parameters application. If the Five Rights Override Parameter is turned off, the option will be grayed out and you will not be able to administer the medication. Refer to your site policies regarding how to contact pharmacy to address the problem<strong>.</strong></p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Administering_a_Patient’s" class="anchor"></span>

Administering a Patient’s Unit Dose Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconpreparing-to-administer-unit-dose-medications-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/110.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/111.png)Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications</h3></th>
<th><p>The instructions listed in this section describe how to change the Virtual Due List Parameters (Start and Stop Date/Time) and Schedule Types on the patient’s VDL, along with the process for scanning the patient’s active Unit Dose medications.</p>
<p>Viewing a Patient’s Active Unit Dose Medications</p>
<p>The “view” or active window shown below, displays the <em>first</em> time that you open BCMA and display medications under the Unit Dose Medication Tab.</p>
<p>Each time that you open a VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass. The PRN Schedule Type controls the default display of PRN medications on the BCMA VDL, and is based on the GUI BCMA Site Parameters entry for “Include Schedule Types.”</p>
<p>Using the Unit Dose Medication Tab</p>
<p>The Unit Dose Medication Tab provides an “alert light” which turns <strong>GREEN</strong> <em>only</em> when the patient has active medication orders associated to them and the admin time is within 12 hours before and 12 hours after NOW. When you click a “lit” Tab, BCMA displays the patient’s active medication orders on the BCMA VDL for your selected timeframe. This safeguard is provided, along with the Missed Medications Report, to ensure that all Unit Dose medications that are due are given to the patient in the correct dosage and on time.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/112.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/113.png)Preparing to Administer Unit Dose Medications (cont.)</th>
<th><p>Example: BCMA VDL for<br />
Active Unit Dose Medications</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/114.png)</p>
<p>Changing the Virtual Due List Parameters</p>
<p>The Virtual Due List Parameters, applicable to the Inpatient order mode, only, is the functional timeframe during which you can administer medications to a patient before or after the scheduled administration time. For many medical centers, this timeframe is defined as two hours.</p>
<p>Once you use BCMA, these Parameters become your default settings. For example, when you change the default settings for certain fields (i.e., Start and Stop Times, and Column Sort Selection) on the BCMA VDL, these settings are retained in your user parameters and become the default settings each time you log on to BCMA. You can reset these user-selected parameters to site-defined parameters using the <em>Reset User Parameters</em> [PSB USER PARAM RESET] option in CHUI BCMA.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The BCMA VDL Start and Stop Times display in one-hour increments, from the top of the nearest hour. For example, 1:15 displays as 1:00 and 1:45 displays as 2:00. You can expand the time range 12 hours before and 12 hours after NOW.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to access the Virtual Due List Parameters area and to move among the Time fields.</p>

<ol start="2" type="1">

<p>Changing Schedule Types on the VDL</p></li>
</ol>
<p>You are ready to select the Schedule Types of the active Unit Dose medications that you want to display on the BCMA VDL. You can choose all Schedule Types available or just specific ones.</p>
<p>The abbreviation for each Schedule Type is listed as follows in the Type column of the BCMA VDL:</p>
<ul>

-gui-user-manual/163.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/164.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/165.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/166.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/167.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/168.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/169.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/170.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/171.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/172.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/173.png)Preparing <td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconscanning-and-verifying-medication-information" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/176.png)Scanning and Verifying Medication Information</h3></td>

<p>To scan and verify medication information</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the patient’s VDL, first check the status of the scanner at the lower left corner of the VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>

</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Not Ready” and RED,</strong> click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">enable scanner</span></strong> button to enable the scanner, and scan the bar code on the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt‑b</span></strong> to enable the scanner.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/177.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/178.png)Example: Scanner Status and Enable Scanner button</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>If you are unable to scan the medication bar code for any reason, right-click on the administration, and select the Unable to Scan option from the right click or Due List menu. Proceed to the section entitled “<a href="#p70_74">Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication</a>.” </p></li>
</ol></td>
<td></td>

<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Continue with the medication administration process for the patient’s active Unit Dose medications.</p></li>

<p>If an Error or Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_68">If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration.</a>”</p>
<p>If an Information pop-up box displays that indicates that Special Instructions/Other Print Info apply, see the section entitled, “<a href="#administering-an-order-with-special-instructions">Administering an Order with Special Instructions</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Early/Late Medication Log dialog box displays, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_103">Administering a Medication Early</a>.”</p>
<p>If a Late Medication Log dialog box displays, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_105">Administering a Medication Late</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Error message indicates that the Drug IEN Code was not found in the DRUG file (#50), see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_69">If Drug IEN Code Not Found in Drug File.</a>”</p>
<p>If an Error message indicates that the medication has already been given or it’s not time to give it yet, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_70">If Medication Already Given or Not Time to Give Yet</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Error message indicates that no order exists for the medication that you just scanned, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_71">If No Order Exists for Medication Scanned.</a>”</p>
<p>If an Information message indicates that you attempted to take action on an administration with an unknown action status, see section entitled, “<a href="#p58_72">If User Attempts to Take Action on an Administration with an Unknown Action Status</a>.”</p></td>

<colgroup>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If an Information message indicates that you attempted to take action on an order that contains an administration with an unknown action status, see section entitled, “<a href="\l">If User Attempts to Take Action on an Order that Contains an Administration with an Unknown Action Status.”</a></p>
<p><a href="\l"><span id="p70_68" class="anchor"></span>If</a> Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is Selected</p>
<p>The Error message provided below displays when administration of a non-nurse verified order is attempted.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message, then click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<p>Example: Error Message When<br />
“Prohibit Administration” Parameter is Selected</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/181.png)</p>
<p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is Selected</p>
<p>The Warning message provided below displays when administration of a non-nurse verified order is attempted.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified and to continue the administration. All medication administration dialogs will display as appropriate to the workflow for the selected administration.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog. Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<p>Example: Warning Message When<br />
“Allow Administration with Warning” Parameter is Selected</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/182.png)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When the “Allow Administration with Warning” or “Prohibit Administration” parameter setting is selected, the resulting warning/error pop-up message will usually precede other BCMA pop-ups during the medication administration process. Exceptions to this are:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Multiple Orders for Scanned Drugs:</strong> When the user scans a medication and there are multiple administrations available within the virtual due list parameters timeframe, the Multiple Orders for Scanned Drugs dialog displays before the Non-Nurse Verified pop-up.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Site parameters for non-nurse verified orders do not affect the CPRS med order button functionality.</p></th>
</tr>

<td>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><p><span id="p58_69" class="anchor"></span>If Drug IEN Code Not Found in DRUG file (#50)</p>
<p>The Error message provided below displays when BCMA does not locate the medication Drug IEN Code or synonym in the DRUG file (#50). This occurs if the DRUG file (#50) contains two entries for the same Drug IEN Code, <em>or</em> the code is invalid.</p>
<p>This error message also displays during an Unable to Scan event, whenever the Drug IEN Code or synonym entered at the Medication Verification dialog does not match the medication on the order.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you receive this Error message more than once, contact the Pharmacy directly about the problem.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Error message, and click OK to return to the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/183.png)Example: Error Message When<br />
Drug IEN Code Not Found</p>

<li><p>Select a medication order on the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol></td>

</ol>

</ol>
<p>If No Order Exists for Medication Scanned</p>
<p>The Error message, provided below, displays if the patient does not have an order for the medication that you just scanned.</p>
<p>To review the Error message</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Error message, and then click OK to return to the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol></td>

</blockquote></li>

</blockquote></li>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconunable-to-scan-unit-dose-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/188.png)Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>Medication scanning failures may be due to several reasons. The barcode may be illegible, it may be damaged, it may be absent, the equipment may be faulty, the drug may be invalid, there may be a dose discrepancy, or the synonym may not be in our drug file. Whatever the reason, the user can select the Unable to Scan feature to document the administration as well as inform their OIT/Pharmacy staff of the problem.</p>
<p>To administer a unit dose medication using Unable to Scan</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>From the Unit Dose tab, select an administration for a unit dose order. Then select the Unable to Scan command from the right-click or the Due List menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Right Click Option</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/189.png)If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is selected</p>
<p>The Error Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! DO NOT GIVE!” displays.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message and click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is selected</p>
<p>The Warning Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! Do you want to continue?” displays.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified to continue the administration. Or, click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If Special Instructions/Other Print Info apply, the information will display in a pop-up box when the pharmacist has flagged the message to pop-up in BCMA.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the early/late medication log displays, enter a comment describing why the administration is early or late.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If it is a PRN order, the PRN Medication Log dialog box displays before the Unable to Scan dialog box if it is too soon to give the PRN medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the selected administration has multiple dispense drugs, or a unit per dose does not equal to one, continue the existing workflow as if the drug had been scanned until the Multiple Dose or Multiple/Fractional Dose dialog box displays. For orders with multiple dispense drugs or units per dose not equal to one, refer to the sections on “Administering a Multiple Dose Order” and “Administering a Fractional Dose Order.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/190.png)Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>At the Unable to Scan dialog box, verify the administration information displayed at the top of the Unable to Scan dialog box including: Medication, Scheduled Admin Time, Schedule Type, Dosage/Infusion Rate, Units Per Dose, Last Action, Bag ID, Medication Route, Special Instructions, and Dispensed Drugs/Medications/Solutions.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Dialog Box<br />
for Unit Dose Administration</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/191.png)</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select an “Unable to Scan Reason” from the drop-down list box. Selections include: Damaged Medication Label, Dose Discrepancy, No Bar Code, Scanning Equipment Failure, and Unable to Determine.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/192.png)Example: Unable to Scan Medication Reasons</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you click <strong>Cancel</strong> at any point in the Unable to Scan process, the Unable to Scan event is not logged, an email is not sent, and the “Order Administration Cancelled” message displays.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>You may enter an optional text comment. Click OK. The Medication Verification dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/193.png)Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box</p></th>
</tr>

<td>Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Notice the Verify Medication option is selected by default. To verify the medication being administered, enter the Drug IEN or National Drug Code from the medication package in the entry field. Click Submit.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the number entered matches the dispense drug being administered for the selected order, the medication, dosage, units, route and special instructions will display. Verify that the information displayed matches the order.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When entering a bar code number, remember that no letters, spaces or punctuation marks are allowed.</p>
<p>Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box<br />
(Verify Medication Option)</p>
<blockquote>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/194.png)</p>
</blockquote></td>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the number entered does not match the dispense drug being administered for the selected order:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>An “Invalid Medication – Do not Give”error message displays.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/195.png)Example: Error Message When<br />
Drug IEN Code Not Found</p>
<ul>
<li><p>If the number entered does not match, or the bar code number is not readable, or there is no label, you may select the Verify Five Rights option. Place a checkmark in each of the five checkboxes to document that the five rights of medication administration have been physically verified (right patient, right medication, right dose, right route, right time) and continue administering the medication without entering a matching bar code number.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Note:</strong> This option is only available if the Five Rights Override Parameter is enabled for unit dose medications in the BCMA Site Parameters application. If the Five Rights Override Parameter is turned off, you will not be able to administer the medication. Refer to your site policies regarding how to contact pharmacy to address the problem.</p>
<p>Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box<br />
(Five Rights Override Option)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/196.png)</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>Review the contents of the Medication Verification dialog box and perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/197.png)Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to complete the Unable to Scan process and continue with the administration. Upon completing the administration you will return to the VDL. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient. The Unable to Scan event is recorded, and a Mailman message is sent notifying OIT/Pharmacy staff of the medication bar code sanning failure.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click the <strong>Cancel</strong> button to cancel the Unable to Scan process without documenting the administration. The Unable to Scan event will not be recorded, nor will a MailMan message be sent.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>MailMan Message Sent After Medication Bar Code Scanning Failure</p>
<p>When you create a medication scanning failure entry, a MailMan message will be sent to the mail group you specified. The subject line of the message will indicate a medication scanning failure. The body of the message will contain the following information:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>User: Last name, First Name (for identifying system issues only/educational needs)</p></li>
<li><p>Date/Time of event</p></li>
<li><p>Patient: Last Name, First Name, and last four digits of patient’s Social Security Number.</p></li>
<li><p>Order Number</p></li>
<li><p>Ward Location/Room</p></li>
<li><p>Type of Bar Code issue: Medication</p></li>
<li><p>Medication</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Unit Dose orders will display dispense drug; drug IEN; dosage ordered</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>IV Orders will display: unique ID (Bag ID typed by User or Ward Stock); orderable item.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Reason for scan failure</p></li>
<li><p>User’s comment</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note</strong>: Inclusion of the last four digits of the patient’s SSN is currently allowed in VistA clinical alert messaging. If there are changes to this policy due to a future VHA directive, the format of this field is subject to change.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<table>
<colgroup>

</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-multiple-dose-order" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/198.png)Administering a Multiple Dose Order</h3></td>
<td><p>The Multiple Dose dialog box, provided below, displays when the patient’s order includes a <strong>single</strong> dispensed drug with multiple doses (variable doses) that need to be administered to the patient. The Multiple Dose dialog box provided on the next page displays when the patient has <strong>multiple</strong> dispensed drugs that need to be administered to them. You can add comments about the medication administration process to either dialog box.</p>
<p>To administer a multiple dose order</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Scan each dosage or dispensed drug for the medication that you want to administer to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>If you did not scan once for each unit listed in the Multiple Dose dialog box, the Confirmation dialog box displays. Proceed to step #2.</p></li>
<li><p>If you are unable to scan one of the units, click the Unable to Scan button next to the unit and proceed with the Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication process, as described in the <a href="#p70_74">Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication</a> section.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Multiple Dose dialog box closes automatically if you are scanning the last dosage for the medication.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering a Multiple Dose Order (cont.)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/199.png)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/200.png)Example: Multiple Dose Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/201.png)Example: Multiple/Fractional Dose Dialog Box</p>
<p>— OR —</p>
<p><strong>(See Next Page)</strong></p></th>

<th>Administering a Multiple Dose Order (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/202.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>At the Confirmation dialog box, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">back</span></strong> to scan additional units. The Multiple Dose dialog box re-displays, retaining the data entered before you clicked the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>done</strong></span> button.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">done</span></strong> after you scan all multiple dosages or multiple dispensed drugs needed. BCMA processes the information, and then displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">done</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to display the patient’s VDL.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-fractional-dose-order" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/203.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/204.png)Administering a Fractional Dose Order</h3></td>
<td><p>The Fractional Dose functionality is designed to alert you when dispensed drug dosages need to be administered to a patient in “fractional” doses, and to allow you to provide comments about this order type once administered. In short, the related dialog boxes let you document the units and the fractional portion of a dose administered to a patient.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Fractional Dose dialog box displays when the units per dose are fractional and <em>less than</em> 1.0. The Multiple/Fractional Dose dialog box displays when the units per dose is <em>greater than</em> 1.0. If you do not scan once for each unit listed in the Multiple/Fractional Dose dialog box, the Confirmation dialog box displays, requesting that you confirm the actual total units administered to the patient.</p>
<p>To administer a fractional dose order</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Scan the medication that you want to administer to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The dialog box that displays depends on the amount of the fractional dose (i.e., less than or greater than 1.0) to be administered to the patient.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/205.png)Example: Fractional Dose Dialog Box</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/206.png)Administering a Fractional Dose Order (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/207.png)Example: Multiple/Fractional Dose Dialog Box</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions, which are related to the fractional dose administered to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the fractional dose is <em>less than</em> 1.0,</strong> enter any comments about the administration (if desired), and click <strong><span class="smallcaps">done</span></strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the fractional dose is <em>greater than</em> 1.0,</strong> scan all units that you’re administering to the patient, enter any comments about the administration (if desired), and click <strong><span class="smallcaps">done</span></strong>. If all units are scanned, BCMA processes the information, and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If you did not scan once for each unit listed in the Multiple/Fractional Dose dialog box, the</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering a Fractional Dose Order (cont.)</th>
<th><p>Confirmation dialog box displays. Proceed to step #3.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>If you are unable to scan one of the units, click the Unable to Scan button next to the unit and proceed with the Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication process, as described in the <a href="#p70_74">Unable to Scan Unit Dose Medication</a> section.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>done</strong></span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/208.png)Example: Confirmation Dialog Box</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>At the Confirmation dialog box, perform one of the following actions, which are related to the fractional dose administered to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Click <span class="smallcaps">back</span> to scan additional units, if you did not scan all of the units for this dispensed drug. The Multiple/Fractional Dose dialog box re-displays, retaining the data entered before you clicked the <span class="smallcaps">done</span> button. If the fractional dose is greater than 1.0, perform step #2 again.</p></li>
<li><p>Click the <span class="smallcaps">partial</span> button to confirm the number of units that have been scanned. The Confirmation dialog box expands for you to select the number of units that have been scanned. Proceed to step #4.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>

<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/211.png)Example: Confirmation Dialog Box (Expanded)</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Select the number of units scanned that will be recorded in BCMA.</p></li>

<li><p>Selecting 2.0 indicates that 2.0 units were administered to the patient.</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> after making your selection. BCMA processes the information, records the number of units selected, and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
<li><p>Continue administering active medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>

<td><h3 id="administering-an-order-with-multiple-admin-times" class="Subheading-Style">Administering an Order with Multiple Admin Times</h3></td>
<td><p>The Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug dialog box, provided below, displays <em>only</em> if the patient’s order has multiple administration times for the medication that you scanned — using the Start and Stop time setting on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>To administer an order with multiple administration times</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the order containing the administration time that you need, and click OK. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select an order. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to accept the selection and display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>Example: Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/212.png)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If applicable, Non-Nurse Verified messages will display after an order is selected on the Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug dialog box.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>

<td><h3 id="administering-an-order-with-special-instructions" class="Subheading-Style">Administering an Order with Special Instructions</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/213.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Information messages, like the ones provided below, display when the Pharmacy answers “YES” to a question in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 about including Special Instructions in a Pop-up box after a nurse scans a medication. If the Pharmacy answers “NO” to the question, the Special Instructions <em>only</em> display in RED below the dispensed drug name in the Medication Order Display Area. You must acknowledge the message <em>before</em> administering the medication.</p>
<p>Special Instructions messages may include a sliding scale range written by the provider, so that you know how much insulin to administer to the patient, based on the patient’s blood sugar level. Other examples include when to call the doctor, when to hold the medication based on patient vitals, and when to use standard protocols.</p>
<p>The default size of the Special Instructions popup box is approximately 80 characters wide with a minimum height of 6 lines. The width cannot be changed, and the height will automatically resize to accommodate the length of the message. If the vertical height of the message exceeds the size of the screen, a vertical scroll bar displays.</p>
<p>If the total height of the administration row, including Special Instructions, is equal to or greater than 19 lines, the following message displays in place of Special Instructions (bold red text): “<strong>Too much information to display. Use right-click menu to display full text.</strong>”</p>
<p>The following methods for displaying Special Instructions are provided on all three medication tabs:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Right-click menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
<li><p>Due List Menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
<li><p>Shortcut function key (F6)</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />

<ul>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness Log</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Unable to Scan</p></li>
<li><p>Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Multiple/Fractional Dose</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The vertical height of the Special Instructions display in the above dialog boxes is 6 lines. If text exceeds 6 lines, a scroll bar and “Display Instructions” button appear, and the following message displays in bold red text: <strong>“&lt;Scroll down or click ‘Display Instructions’ for full text&gt;</strong>.” When the “Display Instructions” button is clicked, Special Instructions will display in the pop-up.</p>
<p>Following is an example of the PRN Medication Log dialog box with Special Instructions text that exceeds 6 lines.</p></th>

<td><h3 id="specifying-the-medication-quantity-and-units-given" class="Subheading-Style">Specifying the Medication Quantity and Units Given</h3></td>
<td><p>To specify medication quantity and units given to patient</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Enter the quantity and units of the medication that you are administering to the patient, and click <strong>OK</strong>. The maximum character length is 40. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/216.png)Example: Quantity and Units Dialog Box</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA will test for scanning of data into the Quantity and Units Dialog Box. The following criteria are tested and any input that matches is rejected: Integer only; a long numeric string that is out of range for an integer; an IV bag number – nnnVnn where n is a numeric digit; and number and units – nnnnnU or nnnnn U where n is a numeric digit. A single U is also rejected.</p>
<p>If a match is found for any of the first four conditions, BCMA will display the following error message.</p></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="specifying-the-injection-site-for-the-medication" class="Subheading-Style">Specifying the Injection Site for the Medication</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/220.png)</p></td>
<td><p>To assist you in rotating injection sites, an expanded “Injection Site Needed” dialog displays during administration of applicable injectable medications, showing the injection site history information detailed below. Use this important information to determine the next injection site location on the patient, based on the previous injection sites shown for the selected orderable item, and all injection sites used for the patient within the timeframe indicated.</p>
<p>When prompted for the injection site, BCMA requires that you enter the location on the patient (the site/location) where you are injecting the medication — before proceeding with the administration process.</p>
<p>To specify an injection site for the medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Select Injection Site drop-down list box, select the location where you are injecting the medication into the patient, and click OK. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select an injection “site” in the drop-down list box. Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>

<td><p>To assist you in rotating injection sites for applicable orders, the Last Site column on the VDL shows the location of the last injection site for the orderable item shown, and is only applicable to administrations that participate in injection site rotation. When BCMA “refreshes,” it updates this column.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/223.png)Example: Last Site Column</p>
<p>BCMA provides multiple ways to display the Injection Site History for administrations that participate in injection site rotation. This option is available on the Right-Click menu, Due List menu, or by using the F7 hotkey.</p></td>

<p>The Injection Site History dialog provides two tables: Previous Injection Site for this Medication Table and All Injection Sites Table. The name of the Orderable Item and the Route are shown above the top table.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The Previous Injection Sites for this Medication (up to 4) table shown at the top, lists up to the last four injection sites for the orderable item, displayed without time limits.</p></li>
<li><p>The All Injection Sites Table (within last nn hours) shown at the bottom, lists all injection site entries for the patient within the time frame (nn), specified by the BCMA Site Parameter, “Injection Site History Max Hours.” The default is 72 hours.</p></li>

<table>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconmarking-a-patch-as-removed" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/228.png)Marking a Patch As Removed</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA lets you document when you “remove” a patch (i.e., Nitroglycerin, Fentanyl, or Nicotine) from a patient. Once marked, the letters “RM” (for “Removed”) display in the Status column of the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>A patch marked as “Given” displays on the BCMA VDL each time BCMA is opened — until it is marked as “Removed” — even if the order is discontinued or expires, or the patient is discharged or<br />
re-admitted to your medical center. The patch will fall off the display after the order’s stop date if the “Patch Display Duration” site parameter value is set between 7 and 14 days. If an order (except a one-time order) has either Expired or been Discontinued and the patch has not been marked as “Removed,” an alert displays and continues to pop up until the patch is marked as “Removed.”</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The action of marking an administration “Not Given” has been replaced by “Undo,” which is applicable only to a patch marked as “Given” or “Removed.” The wording opposite the Undo status will change, depending on the current status of the patient’s medication. For example, changing a medication marked as Given to Undo will display as “Undo–Given” in the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<p>To mark a patch as Removed</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select a “patch” medication that you want to mark as “Removed” on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You cannot administer another patch to a patient, from the same order, until the previous one is marked as “Removed.” This requirement applies to all orderable items with a dosage form of Patch.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for this medication (patch).</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Marking a Patch As Removed (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark command in the drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Removed command from the drop-down menu. BCMA processes the information, and displays the letters “RM” (for “Removed”) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the Removed command.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></th>

<td><h3 id="given-patch-that-is-expired-or-discontinued" class="Subheading-Style">“Given” Patch that is Expired or Discontinued</h3></td>
<td><p>When a patch marked as Given is Expired or Discontinued</p>
<p>When a patch has been “Given” and the order (except a one-time order) then expires or is discontinued, and the patch has not been marked as “Removed,” an alert displays for Inpatient as well as Clinic Order patch administrations. The Location field, indicating INPATIENT for Inpatient administrations or the clinic name for Clinic Order administrations, displays in bold uppercase above the Medication.</p>
<p>Example: Given Patches that are Expired or Discontinued Alert</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/229.png)</p>
<p>To satisfy the alert:</p>
<p>Select OK to temporarily remove the alert &amp; continue as normal.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the <strong><span class="smallcaps">OK</span></strong> button is selected, then the status of the patch administration will remain <strong>Given</strong>, and the</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>“Given” Patch that is Expired or Discontinued (cont.)</th>
<th><p>alert will continue to pop up until the patch is marked as <strong>Removed</strong>.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Mark the patch as <strong>Removed</strong>, using the steps described in the, Marking the patch as removed section, on page 98.</p></li>
<li><p>The patch administration will be removed from the appropriate order mode, Inpatient or Clinic.</p></li>
<li><p>Enter comments as needed.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>To automatically mark a patch as Removed (cont.)</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select one of the following options:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Next:</strong> The Next button is enabled when there is more than one “Given” patch order that is expired or discontinued. You will see “Patch 1 of N,” where N is the total number of “Given” Inpatient and Clinic Order patches that are discontinued or expired for this patient. Select the Next button to display the next “Given” patch order that is expired or discontinued.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Done:</strong> The Done button is enabled when all “Given” patches that are discontinued or expired have been either “Marked Removed” or “Ignored.” Click <strong>Done</strong> to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You can manually mark a patch as “Removed” from the VDL. Select a patch medication on the VDL in either Inpatient or Clinic order mode, and then select the Mark command from the Right Click drop-down menu, then select Removed.</p></th>
</tr>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-prn-order" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/230.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/231.png)Administering a PRN Order</h3></td>
<td><p>The PRN Medication Log dialog box, provided below, displays when you administer a PRN medication to a patient. BCMA checks for an active order and displays the last four “actions” for the same orderable item (not the medication), the date/time of each action, the schedule type, the reasons that the selected PRN medication was administered to the patient, and the number of units given to the patient.</p>
<p>If you are administering a PRN medication using the Unable to Scan feature, the PRN Medication Log dialog box will display before the Unable to Scan dialog box, allowing you to determine whether it’s too soon to give the PRN medication before continuing with the Unable to Scan process.</p>
<p>The dialog box also includes the Vitals area, which can display the four previous vitals entries for each of the Vital signs listed in the area. The “+” (plus) sign, to the left of a Vital sign, expands the row to reveal additional entries. The “–” (minus) sign collapses the row to hide all but the most recent entry.</p>
<p>To administer a PRN order</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Select a Reason drop-down list box, select a site-defined reason that indicates why you are administering the PRN medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a Reason in the drop-down list box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering a PRN Order (![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/232.png)cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/233.png)Example: PRN Medication Log</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>In the Pain Score drop-down list box, select the patient’s pain score, between 0 and 10 or 99, with “0” being No Pain, “10” the Worst Imaginable, and “99” for “Unable to Respond.”</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You are prompted to enter a pain score only if your site has selected this requirement for the “Reason Medication Given PRN Answer Lists” in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Schedule area, select the check box to acknowledge that you, as the person administering the medication, have reviewed the schedule and last administration for the medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> To continue, you must check the box.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to accept your selection and return to the patient’s VDL. BCMA processes the information, and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Administering a PRN Order (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconrecording-the-effectiveness-of-a-prn-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/234.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/235.png)Recording the Effectiveness of a PRN Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>After administering a PRN medication to a patient, you can record the effectiveness of the medication for the patient and view the related information on the PRN Effectiveness List Report.</p>
<p>The PRN Effectiveness Log dialog box lists the orderable item, units given, administration date/time, reason the PRN medication was given, medication administrator, and the patient’s location in the hospital. The Vitals area can display the four previous vitals entries for each of the Vital signs listed in the area. The “+” (plus) sign, to the left of a Vital sign, expands the row to reveal additional entries. The “–” (minus) sign collapses the row to hide all but the most recent entry.</p>
<p>To record the effectiveness of a PRN medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the PRN medication on the BCMA VDL for which you want to record Effectiveness comments.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note</strong>: You can enter the Effectiveness for a PRN medication <em>only</em> if an administration has a status of “G” (for Given).</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the PRN Effectiveness command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The PRN Effectiveness Log dialog box displays with the patient’s medication information listed at the top of the box, under the Selected Administration area, and all PRN medication administrations displayed in the PRN List table.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">p</span></strong> to select the PRN Effectiveness command.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Under the PRN List table, select the medication for which you want to enter an Effectiveness comment. The “Selected Administration” area of the dialog box populates with administration information.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/236.png)Recording the Effectiveness of a PRN Medication ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/237.png)(cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a PRN medication in the list box.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Under the PRN Effectiveness Comment area, enter the effectiveness of the medication given to the patient, up to 150 characters in length. If a pain score is entered, the comment is optional.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: PRN Effectiveness Log Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/238.png)</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>In the Pain Score drop-down list box, select the patient’s pain score, between 0 and 10 or 99, with “0” being No Pain, “10” the Worst Imaginable, and “99” for “Unable to Respond.”</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You are prompted to enter a pain score only if your site has selected this requirement for the “Reason Medication Given PRN Answer Lists” in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>In the Date/Time drop-down list box, define the date/time that the pain score was taken. This</p></li>
</ol></th>
</tr>

If you entered a pain score, the text “Pain Score entered in Vitals via BCMA taken at [date/time]” and your comments will display on the Medication Log.</p></li>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-medication-early" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/239.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/240.png)Administering a Medication Early</h3></td>
<td><p>The Medication Log dialog box, provided below, is designed to “alert” you that you are administering the medication to the patient <em>before</em> the scheduled administration time. The dialog box includes the number of minutes that you are administering the medication, “before the scheduled administration time” listed on the BCMA VDL. You can add a “Comment” (free text), up to 150 characters in length.</p>
<p>To administer a medication early to a patient (only applicable to Inpatient administrations)</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Comments area of the Medication Log dialog box, specify the reason that you are administering the medication early to the patient, and click OK. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p>
<p>Example: Medication Log Dialog Box for Early Dose</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/241.png)Continue administering active Unit Dose medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>

This is based on the orderable item for the medication. Example: * NOTICE, LORAZEPAM tab was GIVEN 11 minutes ago.</p>

<td><p>The Medication Log dialog box, provided below, is designed to “alert” you that you are administering the medication to the patient after the scheduled administration time. The dialog box includes the number of minutes that you are administering the medication, “after the scheduled administration time” listed on the BCMA VDL. You can add a “Comment” (free text), up to 150 characters in length.</p>

BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>

<td><h3 id="marking-single-administration-as-held-or-refused" class="Subheading-Style">Marking Single Administration as Held or Refused</h3></td>
<td><p>You can mark single administrations, for the patient, as “Held” or “Refused” on the BCMA VDL. This feature is particularly helpful c medications. This is applicable to both Inpatient and Clinic administrations.</p>
<p>To mark single administrations as Held or Refused</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the administration you want to mark as Held or Refused.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The options available on the Mark menu will depend on the current Status and Type of medication order. PRN administrations cannot be marked as Held or Refused.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for these medications.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select Held or Refused from the Mark menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If a Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, “<a href="#p58_101">If ‘Allow Administration with Warning’ or ‘Prohibit Administration’ parameter option is selected.</a>”</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Select a Reason from the List on the Medication Log and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medications.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="marking-multiple-administrations-as-held-or-refused" class="Subheading-Style">Marking Multiple Administrations as Held or Refused </h3></td>
<td><p>You can select and mark multiple medications, for the patient, as “Held” or “Refused” on the BCMA VDL. This feature is particularly helpful for marking several administrations at once, for example, when a patient is temporarily off their ward, or if they refuse to take their medications.</p>
<p>To mark multiple medications on the VDL</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/249.png)Using <span class="smallcaps"><strong>shift+click</strong>,</span> select a range of medication orders that you want to mark with the same status on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Using <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ctrl+click</strong>,</span> individually select several medication orders that you want to mark with the same status on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you do not “select” orders on the BCMA VDL, the Mark options will be grayed out and not accessible to you. The options available to you will depend on the current Status of the medication order.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for these medications.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select Held or Refused from the Mark menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If a Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, “If ‘Allow Administration with Warning’ or ‘Prohibit Administration’ parameter option is selected.”</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Select a Reason from the List on the Medication Log and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medications.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconchanging-the-status-of-a-unit-dose-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/251.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/252.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/253.png)Changing the Status of a Unit Dose Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>Use this section when you need to change the status of a patient’s medication.</p>
<p>Once you scan and mark a medication as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time. If you do, you will receive an Error message. You can, however, change the status from “Given” to “Not Given” by using the “Undo–Given” option – provided you are the individual who originally marked it as “Given,” or you have been assigned the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>You can change a medication with the following status:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Given to Not Given</p></li>
<li><p>Removed to Given</p></li>
<li><p>Held or Refused to Given</p></li>
<li><p>Missing to Given, Held, or Refused</p></li>
<li><p>Held to Refused</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> A patch marked as “Given,” displays on the BCMA VDL each time BCMA is opened — until it is marked as “Removed” — even if the order is discontinued or expires, or the patient is discharged or<br />
re-admitted to your medical center. The patch will fall off the display after the order’s stop date if the “Patch Display Duration” site parameter value is set between 7 and 14 days.</p>
<p>To change the status of a Unit Dose medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the medication on the BCMA VDL for which you want to change the status.</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for this medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Mark options available to you will depend on the current Status of the medication order.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Changing the Status of a Unit Dose Medication (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select the command that represents the “action” that you want to take on the medication selected on the BCMA VDL. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the command that represents the “action” that you want to take on the medication selected on the BCMA VDL.</p>
