<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadding-comments-to-a-patients-medication-record" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/254.png)Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record</h3></td>
<td><p>You can add a comment (free text), up to 150 characters in length, to a patient’s medication marked as “G “(Given), “H” (Held), or<br />
“R” (for “Refused”) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. Your comments will also display in the Medication Log Report.</p>
<p>To add comments to a patient’s medication record</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the medication on the BCMA VDL to which you want to add Comments.</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Add Comment command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Medication Log dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">a</span></strong> to display the Medication Log dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Add Comment area, enter the comments that you want to associate with the medication selected on the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/255.png)Example: Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> once you’ve read your entry and are satisfied with it.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/256.png)Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Verify that your comments were entered in the patient’s record by clicking the Med Log button in the Tool Bar to access the Medication Log Report.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Medication Log with Comments Entered</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/257.png)</p>
<p>Note: You can view comments on the Medication Log Report if you select the “Audits” check box in the Include area of the Patient Medication Log dialog box. See chapter entitled, “Viewing and Printing BCMA Reports” for more information.</p></td>
</tr>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-icon-submitting-a-missing-dose-request" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/258.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/259.png)<br />
<br />
Submitting a Missing Dose Request</h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Missing Dose command or the Missing Dose button on the Tool Bar to send Missing Dose Requests directly to the Pharmacy. Your request will automatically print on a dedicated printer in the Pharmacy that your site predefined using the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application. BCMA will also send a MailMan message to a predefined mail group. If both are predefined, both will be notified.</p>
<p>BCMA V. 3.0 displays an “M” in the Status column of the BCMA VDL after you submit a Missing Dose Request to the Pharmacy. The Last Action column includes this status information after you refresh the BCMA VDL. This functionality will benefit the Pharmacy by identifying requests that have already been submitted, and by reducing the number of duplicate submissions that they receive on a daily basis.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You can mark a Missing Dose medication as “Held,” “Refused,” or “Given.” If you miss the “administration window,” you can use the <em>Manual Med Entry</em> [PSB MED LOG NEW ENTRY] option in CHUI BCMA to mark it as “Given.”</p>
<p>To submit a Missing Dose Request</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select a medication on the BCMA VDL that is considered “Missing.”</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Missing Dose command from the Right Click or Due List menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If an Error or Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, “If <a href="#p58_108">Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning.”</a></p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">i</span></strong> (not “L”) to display the Missing Dose Request dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Submitting a Missing Dose Request (cont.)</td>

<p>Example: Warning Message when submitting Missing Dose Request for Non‑Nurse Verified Administration</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/260.png)</p>

<li><p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to cancel the request.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is selected, the following error message displays.</p>
<p>Example: Error Message when submitting Missing Dose Request for Non‑Nurse Verified Administration</p>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/262.png)Example: Submitting a Missing Dose Requestto the Pharmacy (Inpatient Order)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/263.png)Example: Submitting a Missing Dose Requestto the Pharmacy (Clinic Order)</p></th>

<td><p>Example: Submitting a Missing Dose Requestto the Pharmacy (Clinic Order)</p>

<li><blockquote>
<p>In the <a href="mailto:Date@Time">Date@Time</a> Needed field, enter the day and time when you need the medication for the patient using the VA FileMan Date/Time formatting guidelines listed below. You can use a date in the future or the past.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<h3 id="date-formatting">Date Formatting</h3>
<ul>
<li><p>May 1, 2010, 01 MAY 10, 5/01/10, 050110</p></li>
<li><p>N (for NOW)</p></li>
<li><p>T (for Today)</p></li>
</ul>
<h3 id="time-formatting">Time Formatting</h3>
<ul>
<li><p>00:00 (For example, 14:00 for 2:00 p.m.)</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to move among the fields on the dialog box.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the year is omitted, the computer uses the current year. A two-digit year assumes no more than 20 years in the future, or 80 years in the past.</p></td>
</tr>

<span id="_Toc199860840" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 5: Administering Active IVP/IVPB Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-3" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></th>
<th>Use this chapter when you need to administer active IV Piggyback and intermittent syringe, <em>and</em> any Unit Dose medication with a route of IVP or IV PUSH to patients on your ward. The options and features available within the BCMA VDL apply specifically to active orders only.</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconpreparing-to-administer-ivp-or-ivpb-medications" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/269.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/270.png)Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications</h3></th>
<th><p>Before administering any active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to a patient, review this section to learn more about the Schedule Types for the medications that you can administer, including medication orders that display on the BCMA VDL, and how BCMA indicates “actions” taken on medications displayed on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>Then you will be ready to define the administration Start and Stop Times and Schedule Types of the medications that you want to display on the BCMA VDL, and to administer active IVP and IVPB medications to your patients.</p>
<p>Schedule Types that You Can Administer</p>
<p>You can administer medications for active IV Push, IV Piggyback, and intermittent syringe medication orders with the Schedule Types below.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Continuous:</strong> A medication given continuously to a patient for the life of the order, as defined by the order Start and Stop Date/Time. Includes Fill-on-Request orders.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Fill-on-Request Orders:</strong> These are grouped, based on whether their Schedule Type is Continuous or PRN. This depends on whether the schedule contains the characters “PRN.” If BCMA does not find these characters, it looks for administration times, and places the order accordingly on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>PRN:</strong> A medication dosage given to a patient on an “as needed” basis. Includes Fill-on-Request orders.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>On-Call:</strong> A specific order or action dependent upon another order or action taking place <em>before</em> it is carried out.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>One-Time:</strong> A medication order given one time to a patient such as a STAT or a NOW order. This order type displays for a fixed length of time on the VDL, as defined by the order Start and Stop Date/Time.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/271.png)Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Note: Each time that you open a VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass.</p>
<p>Medication Orders that Display on the VDL</p>
<p>In order for active IV Push or IV Piggyback medication orders to display on the IVP/IVPB Medication Tab, all medication routes associated with these orders must have the option “DISPLY ON IVP/IVPB TAB IN BCMA?” specified as “YES” in the MEDICATION ROUTES file (#51.2). BCMA then displays the orders that fall within the Start and Stop Date/Times and Schedule Types selected on the VDL.</p>
<p>Orders that typically display on the IVP/IVPB tab include active Unit Dose orders with a medication route of IV PUSH, and the IV order types listed below:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>“Piggyback”</p></li>
<li><p>“Syringe,” with the “INTERMITTENT SYRINGE?” prompt set to “YES”</p></li>
<li><p>“Chemotherapy,” with the “CHEMOTHERAPY TYPE:” prompt set to “Piggyback” or “Syringe” and the “INTERMITTENT SYRINGE?” prompt set to “YES”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>An “active” status occurs once a pharmacist or a nurse verifies a medication order using Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 or CPRS. This includes orders on “Hold” and any orders entered through the Unit Dose or IV package. Orders placed “On Hold” by a provider display grayed out on the BCMA VDL. You can only mark these order types as “Held,” although it is not necessary that you do so.</p>
<p>BCMA determines <em>when</em> to display an order on the BCMA VDL by subtracting the information in the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter field from the Start Date/Time of the medication order. You can define this</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/272.png)Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>parameter using the Parameters Tab in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<p>Medications Available for Scanning</p>
<p>Administering IV Push and IV Piggyback medications to a patient involves the scanning of the patient’s medication (drug) bar code, which was applied by the Pharmacy. BCMA recognizes the following numbers on the IVP/IVPB Medication Tab.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Internal Entry Number (IEN):</strong> Drug numbers provided<br />
on medication bar codes are considered a unique drug identifier by the Pharmacy. BCMA validates the bar code scanned against the IEN of DRUG file (#50) and/or the SYNONYM field (#.01) of the DRUG file (#50), to ensure that a valid number exists for the dispensed drug and strength scheduled for administration. A drug entry may contain multiple synonyms, which may include National Drug Code (NDC) and manufacturer bar code numbers.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Unique Identifer Number:</strong> This number is generated when the Pharmacy prints a bar code label for an IV bag. It is designed to communicate which IVs have been manufactured by the Pharmacy. This number displays in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Ward Stock Number:</strong> This number is generated when you use a “Ward Stock” item to complete an IV medication order because the IV bag is not available from the Pharmacy (with a Unique Identifier Number). When you scan the Bar Code number on the bag, BCMA generates a Ward Stock number (with a “WS”) that also displays on the Medication Log. You must scan every Additive and Solution for the Ward Stock item. When you do, BCMA then searches for a match to the Bar Code number in any of the active IV orders displayed on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><p>Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/273.png)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/274.png)</p></th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> If an IV bag is administered using Unable to Scan – Create WS, or Unable to Scan – Five Rights Override, BCMA generates a Ward Stock Number for the bag.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Most Pharmacies use a combination of bar codes to identify drug products at the point of administration.</p>
<p>Marking the Order Status/Last Action Column</p>
<p>When you administer an IV Push or IV Piggyback medication to a patient, BCMA electronically documents the “action” taken on the medication by displaying a letter, for example, a “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. This information also displays on the Medication Log Report and the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The Last Action column lists the “last action” taken on an orderable item (not the medication), and the date/time of this action, so the nurse will know when the patient last received any dose of a medication or last had a medication removed for medications requiring removal regardless of the Schedule Type selected This information helps to prevent the same medication from being given to the patient from another order or schedule type.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>If the orderable item is the same, the Last Action column lists the last administration action.</p></li>
<li><p>If the patient has two different orders for the same orderable item, the last administration of either of these orders displays in the Last Action column for both orders. You can view the MAH Report to determine the order in which medications were given and removed for medications requiring removal on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
<li><p>If a medication was not administered before to the patient, the Last Action column will not list a date/time.</p>
<p>Understanding the Status of a Medication Order</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Once you scan and mark a medication as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time. If you do, you will receive an Error message. You can,</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>however, change the status from “Given” to “Not Given” by using the “Undo–Given” option – provided you are the individual who originally marked it as “Given,” or you have been assigned the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>Understanding the Status of a Medication Order</p>
<p>Once you scan and mark a medication as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time. If you do, you will receive an Error message. You can, however, change the status from “Given” to “Not Given” by using the “Undo–Given” option – provided you are the individual who originally marked it as “Given,” or you have been assigned the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>You can mark an IV Push or IV Piggyback medication with the following status:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Given to Not Given</p></li>
<li><p>Held or Refused to Given</p></li>
<li><p>Missing to Given, Held, or Refused</p></li>
<li><p>Held to Refused</p>
<p>Information Stored by BCMA</p></li>
</ul>
<p>BCMA stores the following information each time you administer an active IV Push or IV Piggyback medication to a patient:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Patient</p></li>
<li><p>Location of the patient (i.e., bed, ward, division, or clinic)</p></li>
<li><p>Clinician administering the medication</p></li>
<li><p>Clinician who created the Medication Log Entry</p></li>
<li><p>Entered date and time</p></li>
<li><p>Audit information (i.e., clinician, text, date and time)</p></li>
<li><p>Administration date and time</p></li>
<li><p>Status of the administration, such as Given, Held, Refused, or Missing</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p>Orders changed using the “Undo–Given” option do not display a code (letter) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. This status appears only in the Audit Trail section of the Medication Log Report, not on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
<li><p>“Cancelled” administrations are not stored in the Medication Log.</p></li>
<li><p>“Unknown” Status: If an order created in BCMA CHUI <em>Manual Medication Entry</em> is not completed with a valid administration status, the Admin Status will be stored as null (blank), but will display as “U” (unknown) in the BCMA VDL Status column and “Unknown” in the Last Action column.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>IV Additive (strength), IV Solution (volume), and/or number of units given</p></li>
<li><p>Number of minutes that the dose was given too Early or too Late to the patient</p></li>
<li><p>Reason that a PRN medication was administered and the medication effectiveness</p></li>
<li><p>Medication, dosage, and/or number of units given</p></li>
<li><p>Any comments associated with the drug administration dose</p></li>
<li><p>Injection site for medications that must be injected</p></li>
<li><p>Last Injection Site, for administrations that participate in injection site rotation.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconhow-bcma-validates-patient-and-medication-information" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/275.png)How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information</h3></td>
<td><p>When used as intended, BCMA serves as an excellent check-and-balance system for patients and VAMCs. The chances for errors increase when the scanning process is circumvented — entered manually — during the medication administration process. In short, here is the validation process completed by BCMA V. 3.0.</p>
<p>First Validation By BCMA</p>
<p>When you scan the bar code on a patient’s wristband, BCMA automatically verifies/validates the patient’s identity, and provides important clinical information via a Confirmation dialog box and the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>If you experience a wristband scanning failure, you can select the Unable to Scan feature at the Scan Patient Wristband dialog box. After entering a reason for the failure and an optional comment, you can perform a patient lookup and confirm their identity on the Confirmation dialog box before opening the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>Second Validation By BCMA</p>
<p>The second validation by BCMA occurs when you scan the bar code on the patient’s medication or when you use the Unable to Scan medication feature. During this validation process, BCMA verifies whether the medication IEN Code is located in the DRUG file (#50) or has a valid Unique Identifier Number, if the patient has an active order entered into Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 for the medication scanned, and if the dosage is correct and timely for the medication ordered. The lookup is restricted to the Unique Identifier Number only in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0.</p>
<p>A variety of dialog boxes will display for each patient, depending on the medications scheduled for administration. (See the examples provided below.) If the administration is successful, the patient’s VDL displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that the patient received the medication as required.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p>If the order is active, and includes more than one unit per dose, a dialog box displays so you can select and scan each unit dose scheduled for administration.</p></li>
<li><p>If a patient has more than one active order for the same medication, with different schedule types, both orders display on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
<li><p>If you give the medication outside the medication administration window — Early or Late — (as defined by a site parameter), the Medication Log dialog box displays, requiring that you complete the Comments field. The order is then logged as Early or Late in the Medication Variance Log.</p></li>
<li><p>If a medication is scanned and marked as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time.</p></li>
<li><p>If you scan a medication twice for the same administration time, you will receive an Error message.</p>
<p>Unable to Scan Medication</p></li>
</ul>
<p>If you experience a medication scanning failure, you can select the Unable to Scan feature to administer the medication and inform your support staff of the failure. After entering a reason for the failure and an optional comment, the Medication Verification dialog displays, where you can choose one of the following options:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Verify Medication:</strong> This (default) option provides an entry field in which the user types the number from the bar code label on the medication or IV bag to verify the medication being administered to the patient. BCMA validates the entry against the order and displays the matching dispense drug or bag components. Best practice dictates that you always attempt to verify the medication first. You may retry if your entry does not result in a match.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>How BCMA Validates Patient and Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p><strong>Verify Five Rights:</strong> This option provides a method for administering a medication in the event that Verify Medication failed, or, for example, when the number on the bar code label is not readable, or there is no label. You must confirm that each of the five rights of medication administration have been physically verified (right patient, right medication, right dose, right route, right time) before you can continue the administration process.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Refer to your BCMA Coordinator and site policy for guidance on the use of the Verify Five Rights option.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Verify Five Rights option is only available if the Five Rights Override Parameters are enabled for Unit Dose and IV medications in the BCMA Site Parameters application. If the Five Rights Override Parameter is turned off, the option will be grayed out and you will not be able to administer the medication. Refer to your site policies regarding how to contact pharmacy to address the problem.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="p42_111" class="anchor"></span>

Administering a Patient’s IVP/IVPB Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="preparing-to-administer-ivp-or-ivpb-medications" class="Subheading-Style">Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/276.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/277.png)</p></th>
<th><p>The instructions listed in this section describe how to change the Virtual Due List Parameters (Start and Stop Date/Time) and Schedule Types on the patient’s VDL, along with the process for scanning the patient’s active IV Push, IV Piggyback, and intermittent syringe medications.</p>
<p>Viewing a Patient’s Active IVP/IVPB Medications</p>
<p>The “view” or active window shown below, displays when you select the IVP/IVPB Medication Tab on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>Each time that you open a VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass. The PRN Schedule Type controls the default display of PRN medications on the BCMA VDL, and is based on the GUI BCMA Site Parameters entry for “Include Schedule Types.”</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The IVP/IVPB Medication Tab provides an “alert light” which turns <strong>GREEN</strong> <em>only</em> when the patient has active medication orders associated to them and the admin time is within 12 hours before and 12 hours after NOW. When you click a “lit” Tab, BCMA displays the patient’s active medication orders on the BCMA VDL — for the selected timeframe only. This safeguard is provided, along with the Missed Medications Report, to ensure that all IV Push, IV Piggyback, and intermittent syringe medications that are due are given to the patient in the correct dosage and on time.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.) ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/278.png)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA VDL for Active IV Push and IV Piggyback Medications</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/279.png)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Medication Order Display Area includes the Medication/Solutions and Infusion Rate columns.</p>
<p>Changing the Virtual Due List Parameters</p>
<p>The BCMA VDL Parameters is the functional timeframe during which you can administer Inpatient medications to a patient before or after the scheduled administration time. For many medical centers, this timeframe is defined as two hours.</p>
<p>Once you use BCMA, these Parameters become your default settings. For example, when you change the default settings for certain fields (i.e., Start and Stop Times, and Column Sort Selection) on the BCMA VDL, these settings are retained in your user parameters and become the default settings each time you log on to BCMA. You can reset these user-selected parameters to site-defined parameters using the <em>Reset User Parameters</em> [PSB USER PARAM RESET] option in CHUI BCMA.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The BCMA VDL Start and Stop Times display in one-hour increments, from the top of the nearest hour. For example, 1:15 displays as 1:00 and 1:45 displays as 2:00. You can expand the time range 12 hours before and 12 hours after NOW.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/280.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/281.png)Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>To change the Virtual Due List Parameters</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the patient’s VDL, select the Start and Stop Times in the Virtual Due List Parameters area. The BCMA VDL automatically refreshes and displays active medications for the newly selected administration window.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to access the Virtual Due List Parameters area and to move among the Time fields.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/282.png)Example: VDL Parameters Area on VDL (When Inpatient Order Mode is Selected)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/283.png)Example: VDL Parameters Area on VDL (When Clinic Order Mode is Selected)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Now you are ready to select the Schedule Types of IV Push or IV Piggyback medications that you want to display on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>Changing Schedule Types on the VDL</p></li>
</ol>
<p>You are ready to select the Schedule Types of the active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications that you want to display on the BCMA VDL. You can choose all Schedule Types available, or just specific ones.</p>
<p>The abbreviation for each Schedule Type is listed as follows in the Type column of the BCMA VDL:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>C (for Continuous)</p></li>
<li><p>P (for PRN)</p></li>
<li><p>OC (for On-Call)</p></li>
<li><p>O (for One-Time)</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/284.png)Preparing to Administer IVP or IVPB Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Each time that you open a VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass.</p>
<p>To select Schedule Types that display on the VDL</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Schedule Types area of the BCMA VDL, select the check boxes that apply to the types of medication orders that you want to display on the BCMA VDL for the patient. You may select all of the check boxes or just specific ones.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If a checkbox is selected for a Schedule Type that you do</strong> <em>not</em> <strong>want displayed,</strong> click on it to deselect it.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You can turn off the automatic display of PRN medication orders when the BCMA VDL is first opened by deselecting the PRN check box in the “Include Schedule Types” area of the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to access the Schedule Types area and the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to move among the Schedule Types. Use the Spacebar to select a Schedule Type.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/285.png)Example: Schedule Types Area of VDL</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Now you are ready to scan the patient’s active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconscanning-and-verifying-medication-information" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/286.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/287.png)Scanning and Verifying Medication Information</h3></td>
<td><p>Now you are ready to scan (and verify) the patient’s active IV Push and IV Piggyback medications and to officially begin the medication administration process.</p>
<p>To scan and verify medication information</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the patient’s VDL, scan the bar code on the patient’s medication. BCMA processes the scan and displays screens related to the medication order. If unable to scan, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_141">Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication</a>.”</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the medication bar code is missing or unreadable, right-click on the medication to select the Drug IEN Code command or the Available Bags command from the Right Click drop-down menu, and to display the IEN Code or Unique Identifier Number.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue with the medication administration process for the patient’s active IV Push or IV Piggyback medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If an Error or Warning message indicates that the order is non-nurse verified, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_123">If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is Selected</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Information pop-up box displays that indicates that Special Instructions/Other Print Info apply, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_157">Administering an Order with Special Instructions / Other Print Info</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Early Medication Log dialog box displays, see the section entitled, “<a href="\l">Administering a Medication Early.”</a></p>
<p>If a Late Medication Log dialog box displays, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_173">Administering a Medication Late</a>.”</p>
<p>If an Error message indicates that the Drug IEN Code was not found in the DRUG file (#50) or the Unique Identifier number was not located, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_125">If Drug IEN Code Not Found in DRUG file (#50) or Unique Identifier Number Not Located</a>.”</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</th>
<th><p>If an Error message indicates that the medication has already been given, or it’s not time to give it yet, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_70">If Medication Already Given or Not Time to Give Yet</a>.”</p>
<p><strong>If an Error message indicates that no order exists for the medication that you just scanned, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_71">If No Order Exists for Medication Scanned.”</a></strong></p>
<p>If no bags are available for the medication displayed on the BCMA VDL, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p42_126">If No Bags Available for Medication Displayed on the VDL</a>.”</p>
<p>If IV Parameters fields set to “Warning” <em>and</em> a field is edited in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_127">If IV Parameters Fields Set to “Warning” and Field Edited in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0.”</a></p>
<p>If the “OTHER PRINT INFO:” prompt is edited in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0, see the section entitled, “If “<a href="#p58_128">OTHER PRINT INFO:”</a> prompt is edited.”</p>
<p>If the user attempts to take action on an IVP/IVPB administration with an Unknown Action status, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_129">If User Attempts to Take Action on an Administration with an Unknown Action Status.”</a></p>
<p><strong>If the user attempts to take action on an IVP/IVPB order that contains an administration with an unknown action status, see the section entitled, “<a href="#p58_130">If User Attempts to Take Action on an Order that Contains an Administration with an Unknown Action Status.”</a></strong></p></th>
</tr>

<td><p><span id="p58_123" class="anchor"></span>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is Selected</p>
<p>The Error message provided below displays when administration of a non-nurse verified order is attempted.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message, then click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<p>Example: Error Message When “Prohibit Administration” Parameter is Selected</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/288.png)</p>
<p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is Selected</p>
<p>The Warning message provided below displays when administration of a non-nurse verified order is attempted.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified and to continue the administration. All medication administration dialogs will display as appropriate to the workflow for the selected administration.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog. Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p></td>

<tr class="odd">
<td>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: Warning Message When “Allow Administration with Warning” Parameter is Selected</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/289.png)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When the “Allow Administration with Warning” or “Prohibit Administration” parameter setting is selected, the resulting warning/error pop-up message will usually precede other BCMA pop-ups during the medication administration process. Exceptions to this are:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Ward Stock Bags:</strong> When the user scans bag components into the Ward stock dialog thus creating a ward stock bag, BCMA will not match the list of components to the order until the user selects <strong>OK</strong>. At that time, if the order is not nurse-verified, the Non-Nurse Verified pop-up will then display.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Multiple Orders for Scanned Drugs:</strong> When the user scans a medication and there are multiple administrations available within the virtual due list parameters timeframe, the Multiple Orders for Scanned Drugs dialog displays before the Non-Nurse Verified pop-up.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Site parameters for non-nurse verified orders do not affect the CPRS med order button functionality.</p></td>
</tr>

<td><p><span id="p58_125" class="anchor"></span>If Drug IEN Code Not Found in DRUG file (#50) or Unique Identifier Number Not Located</p>
<p>The Error message, provided below, displays when BCMA does not locate the Drug IEN Code in the DRUG file (#50), <em>or</em> the Unique Identifier Number is not located. This occurs if the DRUG file contains two entries for the same Drug IEN Code, <em>or</em> the code/number is invalid.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you receive this Error message more than once, contact the Pharmacy directly about the problem.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Error message, and click <strong>OK</strong> to return to the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to return to the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/290.png)Example: Error Message When Drug IEN Code or Unique Identifier Number Not Located</p>

<li><blockquote>
<p>Select a medication order on the patient’s VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>

<li><p>Proceed to the Edit Med Log option to resolve the status of the administration.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> For information on using the Edit Med Log option, please refer to the chapter entitled, “Editing the Medication Log.”</p></td>

<td>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><p><span id="p58_130" class="anchor"></span>If User Attempts to Take Action on an Order that Contains an Administration with an Unknown Action Status</p>
<p>The informational message, provided below, displays if the user starts to administer or take action on an order in which one of the administrations associated with that order has an “Unknown” status. The user can choose to acknowledge the message and proceed with the administration or cancel the action.</p>
<p>To review the Error message</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Error message, and perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To continue with the administration, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To cancel the administration without saving, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong>. To resolve the status of the associated administration, use the Edit Med Log option.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong></span> or <span class="smallcaps"><strong>cancel</strong></span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to access the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> For information on using the Edit Med Log option, please refer to the chapter entitled, “Editing the Medication Log.”</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/295.png)Example: Information Message for Unknown Action Status with Option to Continue Administration</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>

<col style="width: 30%" />

<col style="width: 0%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconunable-to-scan-ivpivpb-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/296.png)Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication</h3></td>
<td colspan="2"><p>In the event of a medication scanning failure, you can use the Unable to Scan feature to administer IV Push and IV Piggyback medications. Since IV Push orders that display on the IVP/IVPB tab are treated as unit dose orders, the Unable to Scan IVP medication process is essentially the same as for unit dose medications. IV Piggyback orders displayed on the IVP/IVPB tab may be administered through the Unable to Scan option if the bags are labeled and sent from Pharmacy or via the Unable to Scan – Create WS option if the bag is to be administered as a Ward Stock.</p>
<p>To administer an IVP/IVPB medication using Unable to Scan</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>From the IVP/IVPB tab, select an administration for an IVP/IVPB order. Then select the Unable to Scan command from the right-click or the Due List menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Unable to Scan – Create WS is disabled and not applicable to IVP orders.</p>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Right Click Option for IV Push Administration</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/297.png)</p>
<p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is selected</p>
<p>The Error Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! DO NOT GIVE!” displays.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message and click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is selected,</p>
<p>The Warning Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! Do you want to continue?” displays.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified to continue the administration. Or, click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>If applicable, the Other Print Info message displays. Review the Information message and click <strong>OK</strong> to continue.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/298.png)Example: Other Print Info Message</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>From the Unable to Scan dialog box, verify the administration information displayed at the top of the Unable to Scan dialog box including: Medication, Scheduled Admin Time, Schedule</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
<td></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>Type, Dosage/Infusion rate, units Per Dose, Last Action, Bag ID, Medication Route, and Dispensed Drugs/Medications/Solutions.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Dialog Box for IV Push Administration</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/299.png)</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select an “Unable to Scan Reason” from the drop-down list box. Selections include: Damaged Medication Label, Dose Discrepancy, No Bar Code, Scanning Equipment Failure, and Unable to Determine.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<th>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/300.png)Example: Unable to Scan Medication Reasons</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you click <strong>Cancel</strong> at any point in the Unable to Scan process, the Unable to Scan event is not logged, an email is not sent, and the “Order Administration Cancelled” message displays. Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to return to the VDL</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>You may enter an optional text comment. Click <strong>OK</strong>. The Medication Verification dialog box displays with the Verify Medication option selected by default.</p></li>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/301.png)Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box (Verify Medication Option)</p></th>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To verify the IVP medication being administered, enter the Drug IEN or the National Drug Code from the medication package into the entry field.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To verify the IVPB medication being administered, enter the bag number that is printed on the label into the entry field.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When entering the IEN or NDC number, remember that no letters, spaces, or punctuation marks are allowed.</p>
<ol start="7" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong>Submit</strong>.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the number entered matches the dispense drug being administered for the selected order, the medication, dosage, units, route and special instructions will display. Verify that the information displayed matches the order. For IVPB orders, the IV bag components Confirmation dialog box displays, confirming the additives and solutions.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/302.png)Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box (Verify Medication Option)</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the number entered does not match the dispense drug being administered for the selected order:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>An “Invalid Medication – Do not Give” error message displays. Click OK to return to the Medication Verification dialog box. You may reenter the bar code number to try again.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/303.png)Example: Error Message When Drug IEN Code Not Found</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the number entered does not match, or the bar code number is not readable, or there is no label, you may select the Verify Five Rights option. Place a checkmark in each of the five checkboxes to document that the five rights of medication administration have been physically verified (right patient, right medication, right dose, right route, right time) and continue with the medication administration without entering a matching bar code number for the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Note:</strong> This option is only available if the Five Rights Override Parameter is enabled for unit dose medications in the BCMA Site Parameters application. If the Five Rights Override Parameter is turned off, you will not be able to administer the medication. Refer to your site policies regarding how to contact pharmacy to address the problem.</p>
<p>Example: Medication Verification Dialog Box (Verify Five Rights Option) )</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/304.png)</p></td>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="8" type="1">
<li><p>Review the contents of the Medication Verification dialog box and perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to continue with the administration. The Quantity and Units dialog box displays for IVP orders.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click the <strong>Cancel</strong> button to cancel the Unable to Scan process without documenting the administration. The Unable to Scan event will not be recorded, nor will a MailMan message be sent.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/305.png)Example: Quantity and Units Dialog Box</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA will test for scanning of data into the Quantity and Units Dialog Box. The following criteria are tested and any input that matches is rejected: Integer only; a long numeric string that is out of range for an integer; an IV bag number – nnnVnn where n is a numeric digit; and number and units – nnnnnU or nnnnn U where n is a numeric digit. A single U is also rejected.</p>
<p>If a match is found for any of the first four conditions, BCMA will display the following error message.</p>
<p>Example: Quantity and Units Error Message</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/306.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 32%" />
<col style="width: 67%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/307.png)Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If ‘U’ or ‘u’ is entered, BCMA will display the following error message.</p>
<p>Example: Quantity and Units Error Message</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/308.png)</p>
<ol start="9" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>If applicable, enter the quantity and units of the medication that you are administering to the patient and click <strong>OK</strong>. The Injection Site Selection dialog box displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Injection Site Selection Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/309.png)</p></td>

<td>Unable to Scan IVP/IVPB Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Note:</strong> See note concerning “<a href="#p68_161"><strong>Expanded Injection Site Needed Dialog</strong></a>” for selecting the patient’s injection site from the Expanded Injection Site Needed Dialog Box.</p>
<ol start="10" type="1">
<li><p>In the Injection Site Selection drop-down list box, select the location where you are injecting the medication into the patient.</p></li>
<li><p>Click OK to complete the Unable to Scan process and return to the VDL. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient. The Unable to Scan event is recorded, and a MailMan message is sent notifying OIT/Pharmacy staff of the medication bar code scanning failure.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>MailMan Message Sent After Medication Bar Code Scanning Failure</p>
<p>When you create a medication scanning failure entry, a MailMan message will be sent to the mail group you specified. The subject line of the message will indicate a medication scanning failure. The body of the message will contain the following information:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>User: Last name, First Name (for identifying system issues only/educational needs)</p></li>
<li><p>Date/Time of event</p></li>
<li><p>Patient: Last Name, First Name, and last four digits of patient’s Social Security Number.</p></li>
<li><p>Order Number</p></li>
<li><p>Ward Location/Room</p></li>
<li><p>Type of Bar Code issue: Medication</p></li>
<li><p>Medication</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Unit Dose orders will display dispense drug; drug IEN; dosage ordered</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<td><h3 id="administering-an-order-with-multiple-admin-times-1" class="Subheading-Style">Administering an Order with Multiple Admin Times</h3></td>
<td><p>The Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug dialog box, provided below, displays <em>only</em> if the patient’s order has multiple administration times for the medication that you scanned — using the Start and Stop time setting on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>To administer an order with multiple administration times</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the order containing the administration time that you need, and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select an order. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to accept the selection and display the patient’s VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/320.png)Example: Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug Dialog Box</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Non-Nurse Verified messages will follow this dialog after an order is selected.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-an-order-with-special-instructions-other-print-info" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/321.png)Administering an Order with Special Instructions / Other Print Info</h3></td>
<td><p>Information messages, like the ones provided below, display when the Pharmacy answers “YES” to a question in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 about including Special Instructions in a Pop-up box after a nurse scans a medication. If the Pharmacy answers “NO” to the question, the Special Instructions <em>only</em> display in RED below the dispensed drug name in the Medication Order Display Area. You must acknowledge the message <em>before</em> administering the medication.</p>
<p>Special Instructions messages may include a sliding scale range written by the provider, so that you know how much insulin to administer to the patient, based on the patient’s blood sugar level. Other examples include when to call the doctor, when to hold the medication based on patient vitals, and when to use standard protocols.</p>
<p>The title bar of the Special Instructions pop-up box reflects the type of information contained in the dialog, Special Instructions or Other Print Info. The default size of the Special Instructions / Other Print Info pop-up box is approximately 80 characters wide with a minimum height of 6 lines. The width cannot be changed, and the height will automatically resize to accommodate the length of the message. If the vertical height of the message exceeds the size of the screen, a vertical scroll bar displays.</p>
<p>If the total height of the administration row including Special Instructions / Other Print Info is equal to or greater than 19 lines, the following message displays in place of Special Instructions (bold red text): “<strong>Too much information to display. Use right-click menu to display full text.</strong>”</p>
<p>The following methods for displaying Special Instructions / Other Print Info are provided on all three medication tabs:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Right-click menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
<li><p>Due List Menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering an Order with Special Instructions / Other Print Info (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p>Shortcut function key (F6)</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The following dialog boxes display Special Instructions / Other Print Info:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness Log</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Unable to Scan</p></li>
<li><p>Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Multiple/Fractional Dose</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The vertical height of the Special Instructions / Other Print Info display in the above dialog boxes is 6 lines. If text exceeds 6 lines, a scroll bar and “Display Instructions” button appear, and the following message displays in bold red text: “<strong>&lt;Scroll down or click ‘Display Instructions’ for full text&gt;.</strong>” When the “Display Instructions” button is clicked, Special Instructions/Other Print Info will display in the pop-up.</p>
<p>Following is an example of the Unable to Scan dialog box with Special Instructions text that exceeds 6 lines.</p></th>
</tr>

</ol>

The following criteria are tested and input that matches is rejected: Integer only; a long numeric string that is out of range for an integer; an IV bag number – nnnVnn where n is a numeric digit; and number and units – nnnnnU or nnnnn U where n is a numeric digit. A single U is also rejected.</p></td>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="specifying-the-injection-site-for-the-medication-1" class="Subheading-Style">Specifying the Injection Site for the Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>The Injection Site Selection dialog box, provided below, displays when an IV Push or IV Piggyback medication is injectable and when “PROMPT FOR INJ. SITE IN BCMA” is specified as “YES” in the MEDICATION ROUTES file (#51.2) for a particular route other than Intramuscular, Intradermal, or Subcutaneous. When prompted for the injection site, BCMA requires that you enter the location on the patient (the site/location) where you are injecting the medication — <em>before</em> proceeding with the administration process.</p>
<p>To specify an injection site for the medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Injection Site Selection drop-down list box, select the location where you are injecting the medication into the patient, and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information, and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select an injection “site” in the drop-down list box. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p>
<p>Example: Injection Site Selection Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/328.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/329.png)Specifying the Injection Site for the Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p><span id="p68_161" class="anchor"></span><strong>Note:</strong> At some facilities, pharmacists may choose to finish certain injectable medication orders (such as concentrated Insulin or Haldol) as an intermittent syringe, so that the medication will be drawn up in pharmacy and packaged with a patient and order specific label. This results in non-IV route injections displaying on the IVP/IVPB tab. When one of these orders is administered, the expanded Injection Site Needed dialog displays along with a required acknowledgement of the route. In addition, the injection site will display in the Last Site column for these administrations.</p>
<p>When you administer orders on the IVP/IVPB tab with a medication route of Intramuscular, Intradermal, or Subcutaneous, an expanded “Injection Site Needed” dialog displays showing injection site history and requiring acknowledgement of the medication route prior to selecting the injection site location. Use this important information to determine the next injection site location on the patient, based on the previous injection sites shown for the selected orderable item, and all injection sites used for the patient within the timeframe indicated.</p>
<p>To specify an injection site for the medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the lower left of the dialog, a checkbox is displayed with the statement: “I acknowledge this medication to be administered via route: _______.” The medication route is displayed in bold uppercase red text. Confirm the statement by checking the checkbox.</p></li>
<li><p>In the Select Injection Site drop-down list box, select the location where you are injecting the medication into the patient, and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Specifying the Injection Site for the Medication (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> The OK button remains disabled until the checkbox is checked, and an injection site is selected.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select an injection “site” in the drop-down list box. Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to activate the <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> button, and press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

(invoked from IVP/IVPB tab)

> **NOTE:** The above dialog only displays from the IVP/IVPB tab.

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icondisplaying-the-injection-site-for-the-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/331.png)Displaying the Injection Site for the Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>To assist you in rotating injection sites for applicable orders, the Last Site column on the VDL indicates the location of the last injection site for the orderable item shown, and is only applicable to administrations that participate in injection site rotation. When BCMA “refreshes” it updates this column.</p>
<p>Example: Last Site Column</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/332.png)</p>
<p>BCMA provides multiple ways to display the Injection Site History for administrations that participate in injection site rotation. This option is available on the Right-Click men, Due List menu, or by using the F7 hotkey.</p>
<p>Example: Right-Click Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/333.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Displaying the Injection Site for the Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/334.png)Example: Due List Menu</p>
<p>The Injection Site History Dialog provides two tables: Previous Injection Site for this Medication Table and All Injection Sites Table. The name of the Orderable Item and the Route are shown above the top table.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The Previous Injection Sites for this Medication Table (up to 4) shown at the top lists up to the last four injection sites for the orderable item, displayed without time limits.</p></li>
<li><p>The All Injection Sites Table (within last nn hours) shown at the bottom, lists all injection site entries for the patient within the time frame (nn) specified by the BCMA Site Parameter, “Injection Site History Max Hours.” The default is 72 hours.</p></li>
<li><p>The following data are displayed in each table: Date Time, Medication (Orderable item name), Dosage Given, Route, and Injection Site sorted in reverse date/time order.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Note: If no data exists for the table, the message “&lt;&lt;No data to display&gt;&gt;” appears.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-prn-order-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/336.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/337.png)Administering a PRN Order</h3></td>
<td><p>The PRN Medication Log dialog box, provided below, displays when you administer a PRN medication to a patient. BCMA checks for an active order, and displays the last four “actions” for the same orderable item (not the medication), the date/time of each action, the schedule type, the reasons that the selected PRN medication was administered to the patient and the number of units given to the patient.</p>
<p>The dialog box also includes the Vitals area, which can display the four previous vitals entries for each of the Vital signs listed in the area. The “+” sign, to the left of a Vital sign, expands the row to reveal additional entries. The “-” sign collapses the row to hide all but the most recent entry.</p>
<p>To administer a PRN order</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Select a Reason drop-down list box, select a site-defined reason that indicates why you are administering the PRN medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a Reason in the drop-down list box.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/338.png)Example: PRN Medication Log Dialog Box</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering a PRN Order (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>In the Pain Score drop-down list box, select the patient’s pain score, between 0 and 10 or 99, with “0” being No Pain, “10” the Worst Imaginable, and “99” for “Unable to Respond.”</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You are prompted to enter a pain score only if your site has selected this requirement for the “Reason Medication Given PRN Answer Lists” in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to accept your selection and return to the patient’s VDL. BCMA processes the information, and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></th>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconrecording-the-effectiveness-of-a-prn-medication-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/339.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/340.png)Recording the Effectiveness of a PRN Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>After administering a PRN medication to a patient, you can record the effectiveness of the medication for the patient and view the related information on the PRN Effectiveness List Report.</p>
<p>The PRN Effectiveness Log dialog box lists the orderable item, units given, administration date/time, reason the PRN medication was given, medication administrator, and the patient’s location in the hospital. The Vitals area can display the four previous vitals entries for each of the Vital signs listed in the area. The “+” sign, to the left of a Vital sign, expands the row to reveal additional entries. The “-” sign collapses the row to hide all but the most recent entry.</p>
<p>To record the effectiveness of a PRN medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the PRN medication on the BCMA VDL for which you want to record Effectiveness comments.</p></li>
<li><p>Select the PRN Effectiveness command from the Due List menu. The PRN Effectiveness Log dialog box displays with the patient’s medication information listed at the top of the box, under the Selected Administration area, and all PRN medication administrations displayed in the PRN List table.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">p</span></strong> to select the PRN Effectiveness command.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Double-click on the PRN Effectiveness Activity to document ALL PRN medication orders needing effectiveness comments.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Under the PRN List table, select the medication for which you want to enter an Effectiveness comment. The “Selected Administration” area of the dialog box populates with administration information.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a PRN medication in the list box.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/341.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/342.png)Recording the Effectivness of a PRN Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Under the PRN Effectiveness Comment area, enter the effectiveness of the medication given to the patient, up to 150 characters in length. If a pain score is entered, the comment is optional.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/343.png)Example: Entering an Effectiveness Comment for a Selected PRN Medication</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>In the Pain Score drop-down list box, select the patient’s pain score, between 0 and 10 or 99, with “0” being No Pain, “10” the Worst Imaginable, and “99” for “Unable to Respond.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You are prompted to enter a pain score only if your site has selected this requirement for the “Reason Medication Given PRN Answer Lists” in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>In the Date/Time drop-down list box, define the date/time that the pain score was taken. The information cannot be before the administration time or after the current system time.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadministering-a-medication-early-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/344.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/345.png)Administering a Medication Early</h3></td>
<td><p>The Medication Log dialog box, provided below, is designed to “alert” you that you are administering the medication to the patient before the scheduled administration time. The dialog box includes the number of minutes that you are administering the medication, “before the scheduled administration time” listed on the BCMA VDL. You can add a “Comment” (free text), up to 150 characters in length.</p>
<p>To administer a medication early to a patient (only applicable to Inpatient administrations)</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Comments area of the Message Log dialog box, specify the reason that you are administering the medication early to the patient, and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays the letter “G” (for “Given”) in the Status column to document that you administered the medication to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/346.png)Example: Medication Log Dialog Box for Early Dose</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV Push or IV Piggyback medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<td><p><strong>Note:</strong> If the medication has been already given within the last 120 minutes, whether administered in Inpatient or Clinic order mode, a notice displays in the message box, indicating how long ago the medication was given. This is based on the orderable item for the medication. Example: * NOTICE, FUROSEMIDE INJ, SOLN was GIVEN 13 minutes ago.</p>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconchanging-the-status-of-an-ivp-or-ivpb-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/351.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/352.png)Changing the Status of an IVP or IVPB Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>Use this section when you need to “mark” (change) the status of a patient’s medication.</p>
<p>Once you scan and mark a medication as “Given,” you cannot scan it again for the same administration time. If you do, you will receive an Error message. You can, however, change the status from “Given” to “Not Given” by using the “Undo–Given” option – provided you are the individual who originally marked it as “Given,” or you have been assigned the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>You can mark a medication with the following status:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Given to Not Given</p></li>
<li><p>Held or Refused to Given</p></li>
<li><p>Missing to Given, Held, or Refused</p></li>
<li><p>Held to Refused</p></li>
</ul>
<p>To change the status of an IVP or IVPB medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the medication on the BCMA VDL for which you want to change the status (take an action on).</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for this medication.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Held and Refused IV bags as well as IV bags marked as Missing Dose can be set to the infusing state via scanning and via the Unable to Scan process.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Mark options available to you will depend on the current Status of the medication order.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select the command that represents the “action” that you want to take on the medication selected on the BCMA VDL. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/353.png)

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadding-comments-to-a-patients-medication-record-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/354.png)Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record</h3></td>
<td><p>You can add a comment (free text), up to 150 characters in length, to a patient’s medication marked as “G” (Given), “H” (Held), or<br />
“R” (Refused) in the Status column of the BCMA VDL. Your comments will also display in the Medication Log Report.</p>

</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">a</span></strong> to display the Medication Log dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Add Comment area, enter the comments that you want to associate with the medication selected on the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/355.png)Example: Medication Log Dialog Box</p>

</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p></td>

<td><h3 id="marking-single-administration-as-held-or-refused-1" class="Subheading-Style">Marking Single Administration as Held or Refused</h3></td>
<td><p>You can mark single administrations, for the patient, as “Held” or “Refused” on the BCMA VDL. This feature is particularly helpful when a patient is temporarily off their ward, or if they refuse to take their medications.</p>
<p>To mark single administrations as Held or Refused</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the administration you want to mark as Held or Refused.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The options available on the Mark menu will depend on the current Status and Type of medication order. PRN administrations cannot be marked as Held or Refused.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for these medications.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select Held or Refused from the Mark menu.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p>If a Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, <a href="#p70_180">“If ‘Allow Administration with Warning’ or ‘Prohibit Administration’ parameter option is selected</a>.”</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select a Reason from the List on the Medication Log and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medications.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
