<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconmarking-multiple-administrations-as-held-or-refused" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/361.png)Marking Multiple Administrations as Held or Refused </h3></td>
<td><blockquote>
<p>You can select and mark multiple medications, for the patient, as “Held” or “Refused” on the BCMA VDL. This feature is particularly helpful for marking several administrations at once, for example, when a patient is temporarily off their ward, or if they refuse to take their medications.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>To mark multiple medications on the VDL</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Using <span class="smallcaps"><strong>shift+click</strong>,</span> select a range of medication orders that you want to mark with the same status on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Using <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ctrl+click</strong>,</span> individually select several medication orders that you want to mark with the same status on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you do not “select” orders on the BCMA VDL, the Mark options will be grayed out and not accessible to you. The options available to you will depend on the current Status of the medication order.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for these medications.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select Held or Refused from the Mark menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If a Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, “<a href="#p58_160">If ‘Allow Administration with Warning’ or ‘Prohibit Administration’ parameter option is selected</a>.”</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Select a Reason from the List on the Medication Log and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Marking Multiple Administrations as Held or Refused (cont.)</td>
<td><p>column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medications.</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IVP/IVPB medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If “Allow Administration with Warning” or “Prohibit Administration” parameter option is selected</p>
<p>Example: Warning Message when Marking Multiple Non‑Nurse Verified Administrations as Held or Refused</p>
<ul>
<li><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/362.png)Click <strong>OK</strong> to continue the selected action. The Medication Log with Held or Refused reasons will display as appropriate to the workflow for the selected action.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to return to the VDL.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-icon-submitting-a-missing-dose-request-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/363.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/364.png)<br />
<br />
Submitting a Missing Dose Request</h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Missing Dose command or the Missing Dose button on the Tool Bar to send Missing Dose Requests directly to the Pharmacy. Your request will automatically print on a dedicated printer in the Pharmacy that your medical center predefined using the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application. BCMA will also send a MailMan message to a predefined mail group. If both are predefined, both will be notified.</p>
<p>BCMA V. 3.0 displays an “M” in the Status column of the BCMA VDL after you submit a Missing Dose Request to the Pharmacy. The Last Action column includes this status information after you refresh the BCMA VDL. This functionality will benefit the Pharmacy by identifying requests that have already been submitted, and by reducing the number of duplicate submissions that they receive on a daily basis.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You can mark a Missing Dose medication as “Held," “Refused,” or “Given.” If you miss the “administration window,” you can use the <em>Manual Med Entry</em> [PSB MED LOG NEW ENTRY] option in CHUI BCMA to mark it as “Given.”</p>
<p>To submit a Missing Dose Request</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select a medication on the BCMA VDL that is considered “Missing.”</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Missing Dose command from the Right Click or Due List menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If an Error or Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, <a href="#p70_181">“If “Allow Administration with Warning” or “Prohibit Administration” parameter option is selected</a>.”</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press ALT+D to display the Due List menu, and press i (not “L”) to display the Missing Dose Request dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>

<span id="_Toc199860875" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 6: Working with IV Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-4" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></td>
<td>Use this chapter when you need to administer active large-volume IV and continuous syringe medications to patients on your ward. The options and features available within the BCMA VDL apply specifically to active IV medication orders only.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="preparing-to-administer-iv-medications" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/373.png)Preparing to Administer IV Medications</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/374.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Before administering any active IV medications to a patient, review this section to learn more about the medication orders that display on the BCMA VDL, the different display areas for the IV Medication Tab, and how BCMA indicates “actions” taken on IV bags displayed in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>Then you will be ready to administer active IV medications to your patients.</p>
<p>Schedule Types that You Can Administer</p>
<p>The Schedule Types area of the BCMA VDL is grayed out for IV medications since they are not applicable to these types of medications.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Each time that you open a VDL (i.e., patient record), BCMA defaults to the Unit Dose Medication Tab and the Schedule Types of Continuous, One-Time, and On-Call already selected. This occurs even if you change the Schedule Types or Medication Tab during a medication pass. The PRN Schedule Type controls the default display of PRN medications on the BCMA VDL, and is based on the GUI BCMA Site Parameters entry for “Include Schedule Types.”</p>
<p>Start and Stop Times for IV Medications</p>
<p>The Virtual Due List Time Parameters area of the BCMA VDL is grayed out since administration times are not used for large-volume IV or continuous syringe medications.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IV Medicat![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/375.png)ions (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Medication Orders that Display on the VDL</p>
<p>Once a large-volume IV or continuous syringe medication order becomes active, it displays on the BCMA VDL under the IV Medication Tab. This includes all active IV medication types listed below:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Admixture</p></li>
<li><p>Hyperal</p></li>
<li><p>“Syringe,” with the “INTERMITTENT SYRINGE?” prompt set to “NO”</p></li>
<li><p>“Chemotherapy,” with the “CHEMOTHERAPY TYPE:” prompt set to “Admixture” or “Syringe,” and the “INTERMITTENT SYRINGE?” prompt set to “NO”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>An “active” status occurs once a pharmacist or a nurse verifies a medication order using Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 or CPRS. This includes orders on “Hold” and any orders entered through the IV package. Orders placed “On Hold” by a provider display grayed out on the BCMA VDL. You can only mark these order types as “Held,” although it is not necessary that you do so.</p>
<p>BCMA determines <em>when</em> to display an order on the BCMA VDL by subtracting the information in the “Before Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter field from the Start Date/Time of the medication order. You can define this parameter using the Parameters Tab in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If an IV medication order becomes expired or discontinued while an IV bag is Infusing or Stopped, the order will continue to display on the BCMA VDL until you mark the IV bag as “Completed.”</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IV Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Medications Available for Scanning</p>
<p>Administering IV medications to a patient involves the scanning of the patient’s medication (drug) bar code, which was applied by the Pharmacy. BCMA recognizes the following numbers on the IV Medication Tab.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Internal Entry Number (IEN):</strong> Drug numbers provided on medication bar codes are considered a unique drug identifier by the Pharmacy. BCMA reviews the SYNONYM field (#.01) of the DRUG file (#50), after a medication bar code is scanned, to ensure that a valid number exists for the dispensed drug and strength scheduled for administration.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Unique Identifier Number:</strong> This number is generated (with a “V”) for IV medications when the Pharmacy prints a bar code label for an IV bag. It is designed to communicate which IVs have been manufactured by the Pharmacy. This number displays in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Ward Stock Number:</strong> This number is generated when you use a “Ward Stock” item to complete an IV medication order because the IV bag is not available from the Pharmacy (with a Unique Identifier Number). When you scan the Bar Code number on the bag, BCMA generates a Ward Stock number (with a “WS”) and displays this number in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL. You must scan every Additive and Solution for the Ward Stock item. When you do, BCMA then searches for a match to the Bar Code number in any of the active IV orders displayed on the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If an IV bag is administered using Unable to Scan – Create WS, or Unable to Scan – Five Rights Override, BCMA generates a Ward Stock Number for the bag.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Most Pharmacies use a combination of bar codes to identify drug products at the point of administration.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IV Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>IV Bag Chronology Display Area on the VDL</p>
<p>Unlike Unit Dose, IV Push, and IV Piggyback medications, large-volume IV or continuous syringe medications administered under the IV Medication Tab display the status (and related icon) in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL opposite the Unique Identifier Number or Ward Stock Number. The display area lists IV bags labeled by the Pharmacy and any Ward Stock bags that you have created. This information also displays on the Medication Log Report and the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The examples provided below show the various “actions” that you can take on an IV bag (or the status that you can mark an IV bag), and the related icons in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/376.png)Example: Ward Stock IV Bag with Status of “Infusing”</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/377.png)Example: IV Bag with Other Possible Statuses</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/378.png)

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Administer IV Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Understanding the Status of a Medication Order</p>
<p>You can change a large volume IV or continuous syringe medication with the following status:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Available to Infusing, Missing, Held, or Refused</strong></p></li>
<li><p><strong>Infusing to Stopped or Completed</strong></p></li>
<li><p><strong>Stopped to Infusing, Completed, Missing, Held, or Refused</strong></p></li>
<li><p><strong>Missing to Infusing, Held, or Refused</strong></p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NOTE</strong>: Status changes may be made by use of medication bar code scanning, as well as Unable to Scan, Take Action on Bag, or Mark menu options.</p>
<p><span id="p70_233" class="anchor"></span>Meds on Patient Indicators</p>
<p>Three separate indicators display on the VDL to the left of BCMA Clinical Reminders, in a group entitled “Meds on Patient,” when the patient has currently Infusing IV’s, Stopped IV’s, or Patches that are not removed. The indicators are applicable to active Inpatient or Clinic orders of if there is action that can be taken on an active, Expired, and/or Discontinued order.</p>
<p>See the section entitled “Meds on Patient Indicators” for more information.</p>
<p>Information Stored by BCMA</p>
<p>BCMA stores the following information each time you administer an active large-volume IV medication to a patient:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Patient</p></li>
<li><p>Location of the patient (i.e., bed, ward, division, or clinic)</p></li>
<li><p>Clinician administering the medication</p></li>
<li><p>Clinician who created the Medication Log Entry</p></li>
<li><p>Entered date and time</p></li>
<li><p>Audit information (i.e., clinician, text, date and time)</p></li>
<li><p>Administration date and time</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Preparing to Administer IV Medications (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Status of the administration, such as Available, Infusing, Stopped, Completed, Held, Refused, or Missing</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>“Cancelled” administrations are not stored in the Medication Log.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>IV Additive (strength), IV Solution (volume), and/or number of units given</p></li>
<li><p>Infusion (flow) rate</p></li>
<li><p>Any comments associated with the drug administration dose</p></li>
<li><p>Injection site for the medications</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewing-a-patients-active-iv-medications" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/379.png)Viewing a Patient’s Active IV Medications </h3></td>
<td><p>The “view” or active window shown below, displays when you select the IV Medication Tab on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>The IV Medication Tab provides an “alert light” which turns <strong>GREEN</strong> <em>only</em> when the patient has active medication orders associated to them. When you click a “lit” Tab, BCMA displays the patient’s active medication orders on the BCMA VDL. This safeguard is provided to ensure that all large-volume IV medications that are due are given to the patient in the correct dosage and on time.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Discontinued and expired orders, with a Stop Date/Time greater than 72 hours from NOW, will not display on the BCMA VDL even if an Infusing or Stopped bag exists on the order.</p>
<p>Example: BCMA VDL for Active IV Medications</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/380.png)</p>
<p>Take a few minutes to get better acquainted with the various elements comprising the display areas of the BCMA VDL for IV medications.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/381.png)

Example: Elements Comprising the Display Areas for IV Medications

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/382.png)

<span id="_Toc61251601" class="anchor"></span>Administering IV Bags with Unique ID Number

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="how-bcma-validates-iv-bags-with-unique-identifier-numbertip-box-with-lightbulb-icon" class="Subheading-Style">How BCMA Validates IV Bags with Unique Identifier Number![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/383.png)</h3></th>
<th><p>When you scan the bar code on a patient’s IV bag, BCMA verifies whether the IV bag has a valid Unique Identifier Number, and if the patient has an active order entered into Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 for the bag scanned.</p>
<p>A variety of dialog boxes will display for a patient, depending on the IV bag scheduled for administration. (See the descriptions provided below to learn when a dialog will display on the VDL.) If the administration is successful, the patient’s VDL displays the word “Infusing” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL opposite the Unique Identifier Number that you just scanned.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you scan a new IV bag, and have not marked the previous IV bag as “Completed,” BCMA displays a message.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the IV PARAMETERS fields in the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application are set to “Warning,” and an IV field is edited in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0, a Warning message displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If no order exists for the medication scanned, the medication has already been given, it’s not time to give it yet, or the Unique Identifier Number is not located, an Error message displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If no IV bags are available for the medication displayed on the BCMA VDL, an Information message displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>If you experience a scanning failure while administering an IV bag with a Unique Identifier Number labeled by your Pharmacy, you can select the Unable to Scan feature to infuse the IV bag and inform your support staff of the failure. After entering a reason for the failure and an optional comment, the Medication Verification dialog displays, where you can choose one of the following options:</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>How BCMA Validates IV Bags with Unique Identifier Number (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p><strong>Verify Medication:</strong> This (default) option provides an entry field in which the user types the Unique Identifier Number from the bar code label on the IV bag to verify the medication being administered to the patient. BCMA validates the entry against available bags on the order and displays the bag components. Best practice dictates that you always attempt to verify the medication first. You may retry if your entry does not result in a match.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> It is vital that you type the Unique Identifier Number from the IV bag label in your hand, not the number you see in the IV Bag Chronology in the BCMA VDL.</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Verify Five Rights:</strong> This option provides a method for administering an IV bag in the event that Verify Medication failed, or, for example, when the number on the bar code label is not readable, or there is no label. You must confirm that each of the five rights of medication administration have been physically verified (right patient, right medication, right dose, right route, right time) before you can continue the administration process.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Refer to your BCMA Coordinator and site policy for guidance on the use of the Verify Five Rights option.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Verify Five Rights option is only available if the Five Rights Override Parameters are enabled for Unit Dose and IV medications in the BCMA Site Parameters application. If the Five Rights Override Parameter is turned off, the option will be grayed out and you will not be able to administer the medication. Refer to your site policies regarding how to contact pharmacy to address the problem<strong>.</strong></p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconscanning-and-verifying-medication-information" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/384.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/385.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/386.png)Scanning and Verifying Medication Information</h3></td>
<td><p>Now you are ready to scan (and verify) the patient’s active IV bags to officially begin the medication administration process.</p>
<p>To scan and verify IV bag with Unique Identifier Number</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the patient’s VDL, first check the status of the scanner at the lower left corner of the VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Ready” and</strong> GREEN, scan the bar code of one of the patient’s available IV bags. (The Pharmacy generates the Unique Identifier Number when they print labels for the bag.).</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Not Ready” and RED</strong>, click the <span class="smallcaps">enable scanner</span> button to enable the scanner, and scan the bar code on the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt‑b</span></strong> to enable the scanner.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/387.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/388.png) Example: Scanner Status and Enable Scanner button</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are unable to scan the medication bar code for any reason, right-click <strong>on the IV order</strong>, and select the Unable to Scan option from the right click or Due List menu. Proceed to the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_351">Unable to Scan IV Medication</a>.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message then click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/392.png)</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is Selected</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The warning message provided below displays when administration of a non-nurse verified order is attempted.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified and to continue the administration. All medication administration dialogs will display as appropriate to the workflow for the selected administration.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog. Click <strong>OK to a</strong>cknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> C<strong>he</strong>ck your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p></td>

<tr class="odd">
<td>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/393.png) (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: Warning Message When Allow Administration with Warning Parameter is Selected</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/394.png)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When the “Allow Administration with Warning” or “Prohibit Administration” parameter setting is selected, the resulting warning/error pop-up message will usually precede other BCMA pop-ups during the medication administration process. Exceptions to this are:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Ward Stock Bags:</strong> When the user scans bag components into the Ward stock dialog thus creating a ward stock bag, BCMA will not match the list of components to the order until the user selects <strong>OK</strong>. At that time, if the order is not nurse-verified, the Non-Nurse Verify pop-up will then display.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Currently Infusing IV Bags:</strong> When attempting to scan a new bag while an existing bag is currently infusing, the user must complete the infusing bag before the Non-Nurse Verify pop-up displays.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Site parameters for non-nurse verified orders do not affect the CPRS med order button functionality.</p>
<blockquote>
<p><span id="p58_180" class="anchor"></span><strong>If Unique Identifier Number Not Located</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Error message, provided below, displays when BCMA does not locate the Unique Identifier Number. This occurs if the Unique Identifier Number is invalid.</p>
<p>This error message also displays during an Unable to Scan event, whenever the IV bag Unique Identifier Number entered at the Medication Verification dialog does not match an available bag on the IV order.</p></td>
</tr>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconunable-to-scan-iv-medication" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/404.png)Unable to Scan IV Medication</h3></td>
<td><p>If you experience a scanning failure while trying to administer an IV medication, you can use the Unable to Scan option or the Unable to Scan – Create WS option.</p>
<p>It is important to note that the Unable to Scan options are only available at the order level on the IV tab, meaning you must select an order before selecting the Unable to Scan command. You cannot select Unable to Scan or Unable to Scan – Create WS for a particular bag in the IV Bag Chronology window.</p>
<p>To administer an IV medication using Unable to Scan</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the IV tab, select an IV order that you want to administer. Then select the Unable to Scan command from the right-click or the Due List menu. The Unable to Scan dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If an existing IV bag is already infusing for the selected order, BCMA will prompt you to complete the Infusing IV bag.</p>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan Right Click Option</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/405.png)If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is selected</p>
<p>The Error Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! DO NOT GIVE!” displays.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Unable to Scan IV Medication (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message and click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is selected</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Warning Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! Do you want to continue?” displays.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified and to continue the administration or click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>If applicable, the Other Print Info box displays. Review the Information message and click <strong>OK</strong> to continue.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Other Print Info Box</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/406.png)At the Unable to Scan dialog box, verify the administration information displayed at the top of the box, including: Medication, Dosage/Infusion rate, Medication Route, Other Print Info, and Dispensed Drugs/Medications Solutions.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="changing-the-status-of-an-iv-bag" class="Subheading-Style">Changing the Status of an IV Bag</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/418.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Use this section when you want to change the status of an IV bag from the Pharmacy from “Infusing” to “Stopped” or “Completed” or from “Stopped” to “Infusing” or “Completed.”</p>
<p>To change the status of an IV bag from the Pharmacy</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Scan the Unique Identifier Number for the IV bag, from the Pharmacy, for which you want to change the status. BCMA processes the scan and displays the Scan IV dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>In the IV Bag Chronology window, select the IV bag that you want to take action on, then select the Take Action on Bag command from the right-click or Due List menu. The Scan IV dialog box displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Take Action on Bag command</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/419.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Changing the Status of an IV Bag (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/420.png)Example: Scan IV Dialog Box for Scanned Unique Identifier Number</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>In the Action drop-down list box, select the “action” that you want to take on the IV bag that you just scanned.</p></li>
<li><p>In the Comment area, enter the comments that you want to associate with the action just taken on the IV bag.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>. BCMA marks the IV bag as “Infusing,” “Stopped” or “Completed” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Meds on Patient Indicators display to the left of BCMA Clinical Reminders when the patient has any Infusing IV’s, Stopped IV’s or Patches that are not removed for Inpatient and Clinic orders. See the section entitled, <a href="#p70_233">“Meds on Patient Indicators.”</a></p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Changing the Status of an IV Bag (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/421.png)Example: IV Bag Marked As Completed in IV Bag Chronology Display Area of VDL</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Continue administering active IV medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Toc61251621" class="anchor"></span>

Administering Ward Stock Items

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="how-bcma-validates-ward-stock-items" class="Subheading-Style">How BCMA Validates Ward Stock Items</h3></th>
<th><p>When you scan the bar code on a Ward Stock Item, BCMA recognizes that it is a number other than a Unique Identifier Number. BCMA then displays the Ward Stock dialog box, requiring you to scan every Additive and Solution associated with the order on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>If you are unable to scan one or more Ward Stock items, you can use the Unable to Scan—Create WS command. After documenting the reason for the scanning failure and an optional comment, BCMA then displays the Ward Stock dialog, where you can type the IEN or National Drug Code number of every Additive and Solution associated with the order on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p>After you complete the scanning (or Unable to Scan) process, you then select the injection site where you are administering the medication on the patient. BCMA marks the Ward Stock Item (IV bag) as “Infusing” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL. Unlike IV bags, which display with a “V” in the Unique Identifier Number, Ward Stock Items display with a “WS” and a system-assigned Unique Identifier Number.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconscanning-and-verifying-medication-information-1" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/422.png)Scanning and Verifying Medication Information</h3></th>
<th><p>Now you are ready to scan (and verify) the patient’s Ward Stock Items, and to officially begin the medication administration process.</p>
<p>To scan and verify Ward Stock Item with an IEN</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>At the patient’s VDL, first check the status of the scanner at the lower left corner of the VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Ready” and GREEN</strong>, scan the bar code on the Ward Stock Item. BCMA processes the scan and displays the Ward Stock dialog box.).</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the Scanner Status is “Not Ready” and RED,</strong> click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">enable scanner</span></strong> button to enable the scanner, and scan the bar code on the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/423.png) Example: Scanner Status and Enable Scanner button</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/424.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/425.png)Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>If applicable, the Other Print Info pop-up box displays. Review the Information message and click <strong>OK</strong> to continue.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/426.png)Example: Other Print Info Pop-up Box</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are unable to scan one or more Ward Stock components for any reason, right-click on the Ward Stock order, and select the Unable to Scan option from the right click or Due List menu. Proceed to the section entitled, “<a href="#p70_367">Unable to Scan IV Medication–Ward Stock</a>.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><p>At the Ward Stock dialog box, scan <strong>each</strong> Additive and Solution for the Ward Stock Item that you want to administer to the patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/427.png)Example: Ward Stock Dialog Box for Scanned Ward Stock Item</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Scanning and Verifying Medication Information (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>When finished scanning the related Additives and Solutions, click <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong>.</span> BCMA processes the information, and searches for a “match” (order) on the BCMA VDL. If multiple orders match, it then displays the Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug dialog box, provided below.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to display the Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug dialog box.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/428.png)Example: Multiple Orders for Scanned Drug Dialog Box</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If an existing IV bag is already infusing for the selected order, BCMA will prompt you to complete the Infusing IV bag.</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Prohibit Administration” is selected</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Error Message: “Order NOT Nurse-Verified! DO NOT GIVE!” displays.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the message and click <strong>OK</strong> at the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL without administering the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge that the order has not been nurse verified and to continue the administration or click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Check your site policy to determine the correct workflow for verifying the order in CPRS.</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>Select the order related to the Additives and Solutions that you just scanned, and then click <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong>.</span> The Injection Site Selection dialog box displays.</p></li>

</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>

<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>. BCMA marks the IV bag as “Infusing,” “Stopped” or “Completed” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p></li>

<span id="_Toc199860889" class="anchor"></span>Administering a Patient’s IV Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="administering-an-order-with-other-print-infotip-box-with-lightbulb-icon" class="Subheading-Style">Administering an Order with Other Print Info![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/446.png)</h3></th>
<th><p>Information messages, like the ones provided below, display when the Pharmacy answers “YES” to a question in Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 about including Other Print Info in a Pop-up box after a nurse scans a medication. If the Pharmacy answers “NO” to the question, Other Print Info <em>only</em> displays in RED below the dispensed drug name in the Medication Order Display Area. You must acknowledge the message after administering the medication.</p>
<p>For example, Other Print Info may include information on titrating an IV, when to call the doctor, when to hold the medication based on patient vitals, and when to use standard protocols.</p>
<p>The default size of the Other Print Info popup window is approximately 80 characters wide with a minimum height of 6 lines. The width cannot be changed, and the height will automatically resize to accommodate the length of the message. If the vertical height of the message exceeds the size of the screen, a vertical scroll bar displays.</p>
<p>If the total height of the administration row, including Other Print Info, is equal to or greater than 19 lines, the following message displays in place of Other Print Info (bold red text): “Too much information to display. Use right-click menu to display full text.”</p>
<p>The following methods for displaying Other Print Info are provided on all three medication tabs:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Right-click menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
<li><p>Due List Menu option entitled “Special Instructions / Other Print Info.”</p></li>
<li><p>Shortcut function key (F6)</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Administering an Order with Other Print Info (cont.)</td>
<td><p>The following dialog boxes display Other Print Info:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness Log</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Unable to Scan</p></li>
<li><p>Medication Log</p></li>
<li><p>Scan IV</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The vertical height of the Other Print Info display in the above dialog boxes is 6 lines. If text exceeds 6 lines, a scroll bar and “Display Instructions” button appear, and the following message displays in bold red text: “&lt;Scroll down or click ‘Display Instructions’ for full text&gt;.” When the “Display Instructions” button is clicked, Other Print Info will display in the pop-up.</p>
<p>Following is an example of the Scan IV dialog box with Other Print Info text that exceeds 6 lines.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Administering an Order with Other Print Info (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: Scan IV Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/447.png)</p>
<p>To review Other Print Info from the Pharmacy</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Review the Information message from the Pharmacy, and then click <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> to return to the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue the medication administration process.</p>
<p>Example: Other Print Info Pop-up Box</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/448.png)Continue administering active IV medications to the patient.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconmarking-an-iv-bag-as-held-or-refused" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/449.png)Marking an IV Bag as Held or Refused</h3></td>
<td><p>Use this section when you need to “mark” an IV bag listed as “Available” or “Missing Dose” to “Held” or “Refused.” The action taken on the IV bag displays in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> You can mark an IV bag that is on “Hold” to “Held,” although it is not necessary that you do so unless required by your medical center.</p>
<p>To mark an IV bag as Held or Refused</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the IV bag in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL that you want to mark as “Held” or “Refused.”</p></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select the Mark command from the Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays, with the “actions” available for the IV bag selected in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>In the Action drop-down list box, select the action that represents how you want to “mark” the IV bag selected in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the command that represents the “action” that you want to take on the IV bag selected on the BCMA VDL.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Held and Refused IV bags as well as IV bags marked as Missing Dose can be set to the Infusing state via scanning and via the Unable to Scan process. The “Take Action on Bag” option is not available for Held or Refused IV bags.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Marking an IV Bag as Held or Refused![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/450.png) (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/451.png)Example: Selecting a Reason for Marking an IV Bag as Held or Refused</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Specify a reason, from the drop-down list box, why you are changing the status of the IV bag selected on the BCMA VDL. BCMA processes the information, and then lists the “action” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Marking an IV Bag as Held or Refused (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/452.png)Example: An IV Bag Marked as Held on the VDL</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Continue administering active IV medications to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconadding-comments-to-a-patients-medication-record-2" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/453.png)Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record</h3></td>
<td><p>You can add a comment (free text), up to 150 characters in length, to a patient’s IV medication marked as “Infusing,” “Stopped,” “Completed,” “Held,” or “Refused” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL. Your comments will also display in the Medication Log Report.</p>
<p>To add comments to a patient’s medication record</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select an IV bag in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL that you want to add Comments.</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Add Comment command from the Due List menu. The Medication Log dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">a</span></strong> to display the Medication Log dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Add Comment area, enter the comments that you want to associate with the medication selected on the BCMA VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/454.png)Example: Medication Log Dialog Box</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/455.png)Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> once you’ve read your entry and are satisfied with it. Your comment is displayed in the IV Bag Detail window.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to continue.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/456.png)<strong>Example: IV Bag Detail with Comments Entered</strong></p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Verify that your comments were entered in the patient’s record by clicking the Med Log button in the Tool Bar to access the Medication Log Report.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/457.png)Example: Medication Log with Comments Entered</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

| Adding Comments to a Patient’s Medication Record (cont.) | Note: You can view comments on the Medication Log Report if you select the “Audits” check box in the Include area of the Patient Medication Log dialog box. See the chapter entitled, "[Viewing and Printing BCMA Reports](#p70_455)” for more information. |

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icon-marking-single-administration-as-held-or-refused" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/458.png)<br />
<br />
Marking Single Administration as Held or Refused</h3></td>
<td><p>You can mark an Available or Stopped IV Bag as Held or Refused from the IV Bag Chronology window. This feature is particularly helpful when a patient is temporarily off their ward, or if they refuse to take their medications.</p>
<p>To mark single administrations as Held or Refused</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the IV Bag you want to mark as Held or Refused.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The options available on the Mark menu will depend on the current Status and Type of medication order. PRN administrations cannot be marked as Held or Refused.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select the Mark command from the Right Click or Due List menu. The Mark drop-down menu displays with the “actions” available for these medications.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+d</strong></span> to display the Due List menu, and press <strong><span class="smallcaps">m</span></strong> to display the Mark drop-down menu.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select Held or Refused from the Mark menu.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p>If a Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see section entitled, “<a href="#p70_385">If ‘Allow Administration with Warning’ or ‘Prohibit Administration’ parameter option is selected.</a><strong>”</strong>.</p>
</blockquote>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select a Reason from the List on the Medication Log and click <strong>OK</strong>. BCMA processes the information and displays a letter in the Status column of the BCMA VDL to document the action taken on the medications.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icon-submitting-a-missing-dose-request" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/462.png)<br />
<br />
Submitting a Missing Dose Request</h3></td>
<td><p>You can submit a Missing Dose request on an available IV Bag, as well as a bag marked Held or Refused. You can use the Missing Dose command or the Missing Dose button on the Tool Bar to send Missing Dose Requests directly to the Pharmacy. Your request will automatically print on a dedicated printer in the Pharmacy that your medical center predefined using the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application. BCMA will also send a MailMan message to a predefined mail group. If both are predefined, both will be notified.</p>
<p>BCMA V. 3.0 displays the words “MISSING DOSE” in the IV Bag Chronology display area, opposite the related Unique Identifier Number, after you submit a Missing Dose Request to the Pharmacy. This functionality will benefit the Pharmacy by identifying requests that have already been submitted, and by reducing the number of duplicate submissions that they receive on a daily basis.</p>
<p>To submit a Missing Dose Request</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select an IV bag, in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL that is considered “Missing.”</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Missing Dose command from the Due List menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p>If an Error or Warning message indicates that the order is not nurse verified, see the section entitled, <a href="#p58_220">“If Non-Nurse Verified Orders Site Parameter “Allow Administration with Warning” is selected.”</a></p>
</blockquote></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/463.png)

<colgroup>

<p><strong>Note:</strong> You cannot submit a Missing Dose Request for an IV bag marked as “Complete” in the IV Bag Chronology display area of the BCMA VDL. You can, however, change the status from Missing to Held or Refused. IV bags marked as Missing Dose can be set to the Infusing state via scanning and via the Unable to Scan process.</p>

</ol>
<h3 id="date-formatting-2">Date Formatting</h3>
<blockquote>
<p>February 15, 2013, 15 FEBRUARY 13, 2/15/13, 021513</p>
<p>N (for NOW)</p>
<p>T (for Today)</p>
</blockquote>
<h3 id="time-formatting-2">Time Formatting</h3>
<blockquote>
<p>00:00 (For example, 14:00 for 2:00 p.m.)</p>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to move among the fields on the dialog box.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the year is omitted, the computer uses the current year. A two-digit year assumes no more than 20 years in the future, or 80 years in the past.</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><blockquote>
<p>In the Reason field, click once on the drop-down arrow to display pre-defined reasons why you are sending this request to the Pharmacy.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a Reason in the drop-down list box.</p></td>

<span id="_Toc338337096" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 7: Administering a Patient’s High Risk/High Alert Drugs

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="preparing-to-witness-high-riskhigh-alert-drugs" class="Subheading-Style">Preparing to Witness High Risk/High Alert Drugs</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/471.png)</p></th>
<th><p>BCMA provides functionality that allows the nurse to easily identify high risk/high alert medications that require/recommend a witness on the VDL and Cover Sheet, and prompts for witness credentials within the administration workflow.</p>
<p>The Icon ![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/472.png) appears in the “Alert” column on the Cover Sheet, Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB and IV tabs to alert the user that a High Risk/High Alert medication is to be administered, requiring/recommending a second signature from licensed personnel. When your cursor hovers over the icon, the following text displays: “High Risk/High Alert – Witness Required/Recommended.”</p>
<p>The witness provides an independent double check for a high risk/high alert medication in BCMA and is automatically prompted for their credentials before the medication is administered and allowed to add an optional comment to the patient record. The witness name, the date/time witnessed, and the optional witness comment are stored in the Medication Log.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/473.png)Local site policy dictates which High Risk/High Alert medications are to be marked as “Recommended to witness” versus “Required to witness” in BCMA. Sites should carefully consider which High Risk/High Alert medications are marked as “Recommended to witness,” as those medications will be allowed to be administered without a witness in BCMA. Conversely, High Risk/High Alert medications that are marked as “Required to witness” must be administered with an authorized witness, and cannot be documented as Given or Infusing without the witness.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Preparing to Witness High Risk/High Alert Drugs (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Your nursing and pharmacy staff will work together to assign a Witness HR Order Codes in the Drug file at the orderable item level to control whether a witness is required or recommended for a particular medication and the impact on the workflow. The four qualifying codes are as follows:</p>
<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 19%" />
<col style="width: 80%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><strong>Code</strong></th>
<th><strong>Witness Required/Recommended</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Code 0/Null:</td>
<td>Not a High Risk/High Alert drug (default)</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Code 1:</td>
<td>High Risk/High Alert – Not required to witness in BCMA (Pharmacy use only)</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Code 2:</td>
<td>High Risk/High Alert – Recommended to witness in BCMA</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Code 3:</td>
<td>High Risk/High Alert – Required to witness in BCMA</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

> **NOTE:** All drugs flagged with a Code 2 or Code 3 will display the High Risk/High Alert icon and hover text in BCMA, and will display the witness sign-on prompt within the administration workflow.

Example: Hover Text on the Cover Sheet

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/474.png)

Example: Hover Text on the VDL

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/475.png)

The BCMA Witness Sign-On Dialog is displayed last in the administration workflow, just before the Give/Infuse action. The following administration information is displayed at the top of the dialog:

- Medication (Orderable Item)
- Scheduled Admin Time
- Schedule Type
- Dosage/Infusion Rate
- Units Per Dose
- Last Action, if applicable
- Bag ID or N/A
- Quantity and Units Documented, if applicable
- Medication Route
- Special Instructions/Other Print Info
- Dispense Drugs/Medications/Solutions

The following information displays at the bottom of the Witness Sign-On dialog in a group entitled “Witness Sign-On.”

- Witness Access Code field
- Witness Verify code field
- If Witness is recommended, the following message displays: “This drug is a High Risk/High Alert medication that recommends a second signature from licensed personnel for administration.”

If Witness is required, the following message displays: “This drug is a High risk/High Alert medication that requires a second signature from licensed personnel for administration.”

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="witnessing-high-riskhigh-alert-drugs-when-a-witness-is-required" class="Subheading-Style">Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Required</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/476.png)</p></td>
<td><p><strong>To Administer High Risk/High Alert Medications When a Witness is Required</strong></p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>When a medication is flagged with a Code 3 (Required to Witness), identify and obtain your witness, and have them perform the independent double check, according to your local site policy for High Risk/High Alert administrations.</p></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>At the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog, your witness should review the administration information and enter their Access and Verify codes.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The prompt for changing the user’s Verify code is not supported.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>The witness can enter an optional comment, up to 150 characters in length, and click <strong>OK</strong>.</p></li>
<li><p>The witness must click <strong>OK</strong> to complete the administration or click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” confirmation dialog, then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>If the Witness Sign-On Credentials are valid:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>You are returned to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The administration is marked as “Given” or “Infusing.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The High Risk/High Alert Drug code values for each medication/additive/solution are included in the order. The Witness IEN, Date/Time, Optional Comment and Witness HR Order Code (the highest value of all High Risk/High Alert Drug code values in the order), are determined and stored. The “Witnessed?” flag is set to a value of Yes, indicating the administration was witnessed.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Required (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA – Initial Witness Sign-On Dialog for a High Risk/High Alert Administration when Witness is Required</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/477.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If previously prompted for Quantity and Units, the BCMA Witness Sign dialog will display the Quantity and Units to be administered.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Required (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA – Witness Sign-On Dialog With Quantity and Units Display for a High Risk/High Alert Administration when Witness is Required</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/478.png)</p>
<p>If the Witness Sign-On credentials are invalid:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>An Error message will display, based on the reason the credentials were not validated. Click <strong>OK</strong> to clear the error and return to the BCMA Witness Sign‑On Dialog.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> See section entitled “<strong>Error Messages for Witness Validation</strong>” for all witness sign-on error messages.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The administration workflow will not continue until the witness enters a valid Access and Verify code and has authority to be a witness.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To cancel the administration, click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog, then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Required (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If Witness Sign-On credentials are blank:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Error message: “An authorized witness must sign on before you are able to administer this High Risk/High Alert medication” and the OK button displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Information Message when User Attempts to Proceed without Authorized Witness Access and Verify Codes</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/479.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to clear the error and return to the BCMA Witness Sign‑On Dialog to retry.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The administration will not continue until the witness enters a valid Access and Verify code and has authority to be a witness.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To cancel the administration, click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” dialog, then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="witnessing-high-riskhigh-alert-drugs-when-a-witness-is-recommended-and-witness-is-provided" class="Subheading-Style">Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Recommended and Witness is Provided </h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/480.png)</p></td>
<td><p><strong>To Administer High Risk/High Alert Medications When a Witness is Recommended and Witness is Provided</strong></p>
<p>If witness is provided:</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>When a medication is flagged with a Code 2 (Recommended to Witness,) identify and obtain your witness, and have them perform the independent double check, according to your local site policy for High Risk/High Alert administrations.</p></li>
<li><p>At the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog, your witness should review the administration information and enter their Access and Verify codes.</p></li>
<li><p>The witness may enter an optional comment, up to 150 characters in length.</p></li>
<li><p>The witness selects one of the following:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to complete the administration, or</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” confirmation dialog. Click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>If the Witness Sign-On Credentials are valid:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>You are returned to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The administration is marked as “Given” or “Infusing.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The High Risk/High Alert Drug code values for each medication/additive/solution are included in the order. The Witness IEN, Date/Time, Optional Comment and Witness HR Order Code (the highest value of all High Risk/High Alert Drug code values in the order), are determined and stored. The “Witnessed?” flag is set to a value of Yes, indicating the administration was witnessed.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The prompt for changing the user/s Verify Code is not supported.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Recommended and Witness is Provided (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA Witness Sign-On Dialog for a High Risk/High Alert Administration when Witness is Recommended</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/481.png)</p>
<p>If the Witness Sign-On credentials are invalid:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>An error message will display, based on the reason the credentials were not validated. Click <strong>OK</strong> to clear the error and return to the BCMA Witness Sign‑On Dialog.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> See section entitled “<strong>Error Messages for Witness Validation</strong>” for all witness sign-on error messages.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert medications that are flagged as recommended to witness, if you have a witness available, the credentials entered must be valid.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To cancel the administration, click <strong>Cancel</strong> to display the “Order Administration Cancelled” confirmation dialog, then click <strong>OK</strong> to acknowledge the cancellation and to return to the VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="witnessing-high-riskhigh-alert-drugs-when-a-witness-is-recommended-but-not-provided" class="Subheading-Style">Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Recommended, but Not Provided</h3></td>
<td><p><strong>To Administer High Risk/High Alert Medications When a Witness is Recommended but Not Provided</strong></p>
<p>If no witness is provided:</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>When a medication is flagged with a Code 2 (Recommended to Witness,) at the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog, leave the Access and Verify codes blank and click <strong>OK</strong>.</p></li>
<li><p>The warning message: “You are attempting to administer a High Risk/High Alert drug without the presence of an authorized witness. Actions taken will be recorded in the audit log. Do you want to continue WITHOUT A WITNESS?” displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/482.png)<strong>Example: Warning Message when Attempting to Administer a High Risk/High Alert Drug Without Witness</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>No</strong> to return to the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog to enter witness credentials.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>Yes</strong> to return to the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog and acknowledge the message.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>The Access Code and Verify Code fields are grayed out, and the <strong>OK</strong> button is disabled.</p></li>
</ul></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs When a Witness is Recommended, but Not Provided (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA Witness Sign On Dialog with Acknowledgement of Administering a High Risk/High Alert Medication without a Witness</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/483.png)</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Read the acknowledgement message: “I acknowledge that I am administering this High Risk/High Alert medication without the presence of an authorized witness” and check the box. The OK button is enabled only after the acknowledgment checkbox is completed.</p></li>
<li><p>Enter an optional comment, up to 150 characters in length.</p></li>
<li><p>Select one of the following:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to complete the administration and return to the VDL. The administration is marked as “Given” or “Infusing.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>

<td><h3 id="error-messages-for-witness-validation-when-witnessing-high-riskhigh-alert-drugs" class="Subheading-Style">Error Messages for Witness Validation When Witnessing High Risk/High Alert Drugs</h3></td>
<td><p>Error Messages for Witness Validation:</p>
<p>BCMA authenticates witness credentials based on the witness’ access and verify codes, security keys, and primary and secondary menu options. The conditions are checked in the sequence specified below, such that if more than one condition is applicable to the witness, the first matching condition will determine the error message displayed.</p>
<p>If the Witness Access and Verify Codes are not valid</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The error message “Invalid Witness sign-on” displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to clear the error and return to the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Error Message when Witness Credentials are Not Valid</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/484.png)</p>
<p>If the witness is a student holding the PSB STUDENT Key and is attempting to witness for self or any other user</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The error message: “A student does not have authority to witness a High Risk/High Alert administration” displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>OK</strong> to clear the error and return to the BCMA Witness Sign-On dialog.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/485.png)Example: Error Message when Student User Attempts to Sign On as Witness</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</blockquote></li>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="witness-information-stored-in-the-med-log-report" class="Subheading-Style">Witness Information Stored in the Med Log Report</h3></td>
<td><p><strong>Med Log Report</strong></p>
<p>The Medication Log report stores witness information for high risk/high alert medication administrations, including the witness name, date/time witnessed and optional witness comment, if the user selects to include comments on the Witness sign-on dialog. The witness information is captured in the Comments and Audits sections of the Medication Log.</p>
<p>If you choose to exclude comments from the report, the report will not display witness sign-on information or witness comments.</p>
<p>If you select to “Include Comments” on the Medication Log Report dialog, the following witness information appears in the body of the report:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations (marked as Recommended or Required) that are witnessed: Witness Last Name, Witness First Name, Witnessed Date@Time, and Optional Comment.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations marked as Recommended to witness, that are <u>not</u> witnessed: “Witnessed?: No” and Optional Comment.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations that are marked as Given, then later marked as Undo Given, prior witness information and any witness comments are removed from the body of the Med Log report.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>If you select “Include Audits” on the Med Log Report dialog, the following witness information is included in the Audits section of the report:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations marked as Required (3) that are witnessed, the following is printed in the Audits section:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS DATE/TIME Set to” ‘[WITNESSED DATE@TIME]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESSED BY Set to” ‘[WITNESS LAST NAME, FIRST NAME]’</p>
</blockquote></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Witness Information Stored in the Med Log Report (cont.)</td>
<td><blockquote>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG Set to” ‘[WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESSED?” Set to” ‘[WITNESSED?]’</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For high risk/high alert administrations marked as Recommended (2) to witness that are witnessed, the following is printed in the Audits section:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS DATE/TIME Set to” ‘[WITNESSED DATE@TIME]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESSED BY Set to” ‘[WITNESS LAST NAME, FIRST NAME]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG Set to” ‘[WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESSED?” Set to” ‘[WITNESSED?]’</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations marked as Recommended (2) to witness, that are <u>not witnessed</u>, the following is printed in the Audits section:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>Witnessed?:” NO</p>
<p>[Required COMMENT] (on line below witness name, aligned with witness name)</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS HR ORDER.</p>
<p>FLAG Set to” ‘[WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG]’</p>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESSED? Set to” ‘[WITNESSED?]’</p>
<p>Example Audit entries:</p>
<p>10/15/12 01:32 GN Field: WITNESS HR ORDER FLAG Set to 'RECOMMEND WITNESS-HIGH RISK/ALERT'.</p>
<p>10/15/12 01:32 GN Field: WITNESSED? Set to 'NO'.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>For High Risk/High Alert administrations marked as Required (3) or Recommended (2) to witness that were witnessed, then later marked as Undo Given, the following is printed in the Audits section:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>[DATE TIME][USER INITIALS] “Field: WITNESS DATE/TIME deleted.”</p>
</blockquote></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Toc338337083" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 8: Administering Active Clinic Order Medications

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 28%" />
<col style="width: 71%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icondisplaying-clinic-orders-in-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/496.png)Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA</h3></th>
<th><p>BCMA displays clinic orders on the Cover Sheet, Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB and IV tabs. You may select between two mutually exclusive “Order Modes.” See the following Inpatient/Clinic Order Mode Indicators Table for an explanation of possible display combinations.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/497.png)Inpatient/Clinic Order Mode Indicators Table</p>
<p>Viewing a Patient’s Clinic Order Medications</p>
<p><strong>When Patient Status is Admitted</strong></p>
<p>The system selects a default order mode based on the patient admission status when the patient record is opened. If the patient is admitted to a ward, BCMA selects the Inpatient order mode. An indicator displays next to the Inpatient order mode, showing green, when active</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 28%" />
<col style="width: 71%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/498.png)</p></td>
<td><p>inpatient orders exist for the patient and/or an action can be taken on an expired or discontinued order or white when no active clinic orders exist.</p>
<p>When the Inpatient order mode is selected, the Order Mode indicator shows Inpatient orders exist, and the Virtual Due List Parameters section displays.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/499.png)<strong>Example: Inpatient Order Mode Selected</strong></p>
<p>When Patient Status is Not Admitted</p>
<p>If the patient status is not admitted, the system defaults to the Clinic order mode. An indicator displays next to the Clinic order mode, showing green when active clinic orders exist for the patient or white when no active clinic orders exist.</p>
<p>When Clinic mode is selected, the order mode indicator shows Clinic orders exist, and the Clinic Order Date area replaces the Virtual Due List Parameters area on the screen. Only clinic medication orders display on the Cover Sheet, Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB and IV tabs.</p>
<p><strong>Example: Clinic Order Mode Selected</strong></p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/500.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</td>
<td><p>In the Clinic order mode, the column entitled “Clinic” displays the clinic name associated with the order on the Cover Sheet, Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB and IV tabs. The HSM column is removed from the Unit Dose tab. “Location” is blank for patients that are not admitted.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/501.png)Example: Clinic Column</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If “AUTO-DC IMO ORDERS?” is set to “Yes” in the CLINIC DEFINITION (#53.46) file when a Clinic patient is admitted, Active Unit Dose and IVP/IVPB Clinic orders are discontinued, at which point they will not display on the VDL, except for Expired/Discontinued Patch orders that display for the number of days defined by the “Patch Display Duration” parameter or until removed by a nurse.</p>
<p>If “AUTO-DC IMO ORDERS?” is set to “No” in the CLINIC DEFINTION (#53.46) file, when a Clinic patient is admitted, Unit Dose and IVP/IVPB Clinic orders will remain displayed on the VDL in Clinic Order Mode.</p>
<p>Displaying Clinic Orders on the Cover Sheet</p>
<p>When Clinic order mode is selected, only Clinic Orders are displayed on the Medication Overview, PRN Overview, IV Overview, and Expired/DC’d/Expiring view of the Cover Sheet. When Clinic order mode and Cover Sheet are selected, the Clinic order date, calendar, navigation arrows, and Today button are disabled. When Clinic order mode is selected and focus goes from the Cover Sheet back to a medication tab (UD, IVP/IVPB), the Clinic order date field, Today button, and navigation arrows are re-enabled, and the previous date selected is active.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/502.png)Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If you switch between Inpatient and Clinic order mode while on the cover sheet tab, the Medication Overview view displays as the initial default view. If you select Medication Overview or PRN Overview, orders that have expired or have been discontinued within the last 7 days are displayed in the Expired/DC’d orders section.</p>
<p>Example: Clinic Mode and Cover Sheet (Medication Overview)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/503.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
