<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</td>
<td><p>If you select the Expired/DC’d/Expiring orders view, orders that have expired or have been discontinued within the last 7days are displayed in the Expired/DC’d orders section. Orders expiring within the next 7 days are displayed in the Expiring within next 7 days orders section.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/504.png)Example: Clinic Mode and Cover Sheet (Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The system ignores the parameters for Allowable Time Limits (Before Scheduled Admin Time and After Scheduled Admin Time) when displaying clinic orders on the cover sheet.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Orders associated with outpatient clinics, that are not technically “Clinic Orders,” will display in the Inpatient Order Mode in BCMA. Clinic Orders display within the Clinic Order Service in the Orders tab in CPRS.</p>
<p>The following BCMA Clinic Order definitions only apply to the BCMA VDL, not the Cover Sheet:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>ACTIVE ORDERS only display in BCMA Clinic order mode, if the order is active relative to TODAY, meaning the Order Start Date must be less than or equal to TODAY, and the Order Stop Date must be greater than or equal to TODAY.</p></li>
<li><p>FUTURE ADMINISTRATIONS only display in BCMA Clinic order mode for an ACTIVE ORDER, as defined above, for a date in the future, only if the schedule and admin time matches the selected Clinic Order Date. You can take an action on a future Administration on an ACTIVE ORDER.</p></li>
<li><p>PAST ADMINISTRATIONS only display in BCMA Clinic order mode for an ACTIVE ORDER, as defined above, for a date in the past, only if the schedule and admin</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Displaying Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>time matches the selected Clinic Order Date. You can take an action on a PAST ADMINISTRATION on an ACTIVE ORDER.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>FUTURE ORDERS should never display in BCMA Clinic order mode since the order start date is greater that TODAY and you cannot take an action on a FUTURE ORDER.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="administering-clinic-orders-in-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">Administering Clinic Orders in BCMA</h3></td>
<td><p>You can access the BCMA VDL to view and administer clinic medications that are due each day. You can see active clinic orders that were due prior to today so that you can administer medications to a patient who arrives late for an appointment. You can also see active clinic orders that are due after today, so that you can administer medications to a patient who arrives early for an appointment.</p>
<p>You can access all features of the cover sheet for either clinic orders or inpatient orders, and then switch between inpatient and clinic orders while displaying the cover sheet.</p>
<p>The Clinic Order Date defaults to today’s date, regardless of whether there are active orders to be administered today. If no active clinic orders display on the Unit Dose or the IVP/IVPB tabs for the selected date and/or selected schedule types, the following message displays on the VDL: “There are no administrations to display, based on your current Clinic Order Date and/or Schedule Type selections.”</p>
<p>Display Alerts</p>
<p>The following alerts pertain to clinic order administrations and display in the Medication Log dialog prior to administration:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>An alert displays on the Medication Log dialog, requiring a comment, if you attempt to administer a clinic medication on a day other than the scheduled day.</p></li>
<li><p>An alert, “You are about to give a medication that is scheduled for &lt;Future Date&gt;” in bold text in the Medication Log dialog message box, if you attempt to administer a clinic medication for a future administration of an active order. A comment is required before you are allowed to continue.</p></li>
<li><p>An alert, “You are about to give a medication that was scheduled for &lt;Past Date&gt;” in bold text in the Medication Log dialog message box if you attempt to administer a clinic medication for a past</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Administering Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>administration of an active order. A comment is required before you are allowed to continue.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>An alert also displays on the Medication Log dialog, if you attempt to administer a medication (Orderable Item) that was already given within the last 120 minutes, whether the medication was given in Inpatient or Clinic order mode.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The parameters for Allowable Time Limits (Before Scheduled Admin Time and After Scheduled Admin Time) are ignored when displaying and administering clinic orders on the VDL, meaning that alerts are not displayed when clinic orders are administered early or late.</p>
<p>To Administer Clinic Orders in BCMA</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>In the Clinic Order Date area on the Unit Dose and IVP/IVPB tabs of the BCMA VDL, select a single clinic date to display, using the left and right arrows in the pop-up calendar. Or you can click the drop-down arrow to the right of the date to display the calendar pop-up.</p></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p>When you open a patient record, the Clinic Order date defaults to TODAY.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/505.png)Example: Clinic Order Date Selection</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Administering Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/506.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/507.png)</p></td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>A “Today” button allows you to return to today’s date while in Clinic order mode. The button is enabled when the Clinic Order Date is set to a date other than today’s date, and you have selected the Unit Dose or IVP/IVPB tab. It is disabled when the Clinic Order Date is set to today’s date.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>Example: Clinic Order “Today” Button</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/508.png)</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>After a date is selected, all active Clinic Orders for the patient are displayed for a 24 hour period on the selected date (0001 to 2359), based on the Clinic Order’s start date, stop date, schedule, and admin times.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clinic orders, for which the Order Start Date/Time is in the future, do not display on the VDL.</p>
<p>Once a date is selected, and orders that are due are displayed, the administration workflow continues, such that you can scan the medication to be given or use Unable to Scan functionality.</p>
<p>Actions taken (Status) on non-PRN clinic order administrations on PREVIOUS or FUTURE DATES remain displayed on the VDL, as long as the order is still active, even after refresh.</p>
<p>After you refresh, the “Given” status of all PRN clinic orders (administered TODAY, administered on PREVIOUS dates, or administered on FUTURE dates) is cleared.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

| Administering Clinic Orders in BCMA (cont.) | Note to BCMA Coordinators: The system excludes Unable to Scan data logging functionality when BCMA Clinic Orders are administered. Clinic patients may be retrieved using Unable to Scan functionality in the GUI, but Unable To Scan events for retrieval of clinic patients are not logged. Clinic medications may be administered using Unable to Scan functionality in the GUI, but Unable To Scan events for administration of medications are not logged. Unable to Scan Detailed and Summary reports only include data for Inpatient administrations. |
|---------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconworking-with-large-volume-iv-clinic-orders" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/509.png)Working with Large Volume IV Clinic Orders</h3></td>
<td><p>You can see all available IV bags on active IV orders for both Inpatient and Clinic orders to infuse, monitor or take action on the bags as needed.</p>
<p>IV bags on active clinic orders for bags that have not been completed, display on the VDL until they are marked as completed. IV bags on Expired/Discontinued Clinic orders that have not been completed, display on the VDL for a maximum of 7 days or until they are marked as completed.</p>
<p><strong>When you are in the Clinic order mode and select the IV tab:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Clinic Order Date Selection field, navigation arrows, and Today button are disabled, as date selection and navigation are not applicable to large volume IV orders.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Active IV Clinic orders display based on the order’s start date/time and stop date/time.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Expired IV Clinic orders no longer display unless the bag is still infusing or stopped.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>You may complete infusing IV bags on expired orders, regardless of whether they were infused in a Clinic or an Inpatient location.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Clinic order IV bags only display on Expired/Discontinued IV Clinic orders if an IV bag on the order is Stopped or Infusing for a maximum of 7 days, or until you complete them.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>You may infuse or take action on bags on active IV orders and on Expired/Discontinued IV orders in both Clinic and Inpatient order modes.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If “AUTO-DC IMO ORDERS?” is set to “Yes” in the CLINIC DEFINITION (#53.46) file, when a Clinic patient is admitted:</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>Active IV Clinic orders are discontinued.</p></li>
</ul></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconlast-action-and-prneffectiveness-for-clinic-orders" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/510.png)Last Action and PRN/Effectiveness for Clinic Orders</h3></td>
<td><p>You can verify that the last action taken on a particular administration reflects the status and date acted on that medication, whether the action was taken in an inpatient ward or in a clinic.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The Last Action column on the Unit Dose and IVP/IVPB tabs is updated to reflect the action taken and date/time of the action on that orderable item, whether the action was taken in an inpatient ward or in a clinic.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Last Action Column on VDL</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/511.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The Last Given calculation and date are updated on the PRN Medication Log dialog to reflect the last date/time the orderable item was given and the elapsed time since it was last given, whether last given in an inpatient ward or in a clinic.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Last Given Calculation and Date/time Given on PRN Med Log</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/512.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><p>You will see the date and time a PRN medication was last given, including the calculation of time elapsed, whether the medication was given in an inpatient ward or in a clinic.</p></li>
<li><p>All pending PRN administrations that need effectiveness documentation, whether given in an inpatient ward or in a clinic, are displayed on the PRN Med Log.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="meds-on-patient-indicators" class="Subheading-Style">Meds on Patient Indicators</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/516.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Three separate indicators display on the VDL to the left of BCMA Clinical Reminders, in a group entitled “Meds on Patient,” when the patient has currently Infusing IV’s, Stopped IV’s, or Patches that are not removed. The indicators are applicable to active Inpatient or Clinic orders or if there is action that can be taken on an active, Expired, and/or Discontinued order.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When Meds on Patient Indicators display, you may need to switch tabs or order mode to find Infusing IVs, Stopped IVs or Patches on which action can be taken.</p>
<p>The Infusing IV indicator displays the words “Infusing IV’s” in red bold text, only when there is one or more active, expired, and/or discontinued Infusing IV on the patient, in either Clinic or Inpatient order mode.</p>
<p>Example: Infusing IV Indicator</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/517.png)</p>
<p>The Stopped IV indicator displays the words “Stopped IVs” in red bold text, only when there is one or more active, expired, and/or discontinued Stopped IVs on the patient, in either Clinic or Inpatient order mode.</p>
<p>Example: Stopped IV Indicator</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/518.png)</p>
<p>The Patches indicator displays the word “Patches” in red bold text, only when there are one or more active, Expired, and/or Discontinued patches that are not removed from the patient, in either Clinic or Inpatient order mode.</p></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconpatch-administrations-expired-or-discontinued" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/522.png)Patch Administrations Expired or Discontinued</h3></td>
<td><p>You can view clinic patch administrations as well as inpatient patch administrations that are expired or discontinued on the VDL.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The system displays both clinic and inpatient patch administrations in the “Given Patches that are Expired or Discontinued” popup on the VDL.</p></li>
<li><p>The count (Patch # of #) is updated to include the total number of patch administrations in the “Given Patches that are Expired or Discontinued” popup and whether they are clinic or inpatient.</p></li>
<li><p>The Location (Ward name or Clinic name) where the patch was administered in the facility is displayed above the medication in the popup. The word “INPATIENT” is displayed for ward-based administrations, and the clinic name is displayed for clinic based administrations in bold uppercase.</p></li>
<li><p>When you select “Mark Removed,” the system marks the patch administration “Removed” from the appropriate order mode (Clinic or Inpatient).</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The BCMA site parameter “Patch Display Duration” applies to patches administered in both Inpatient and Clinic order modes. If “AUTO-DC IMO ORDERS?” is set to “Yes” in the CLINIC DEFINITION (#53.46) file, when a Clinic patient is admitted, Expired/Discontinued orders remain displayed in Clinic order mode for the number of days defined by the “Patch Display Duration” parameter, or until removed by a nurse. If “AUTO-DC IMO ORDERS?” is set to “No” in the CLINIC DEFINTION (#53.46) file, when a Clinic patient is admitted, any existing patch orders display in Clinic order mode.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewing-and-printing-clinic-order-reports" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/524.png)Viewing and Printing Clinic Order Reports</h3></td>
<td><p>A variety of reports displaying Clinic Order data are available.</p>
<p>Some reports separate Inpatient data from Clinic order data. These reports are referred to as “Mutually Exclusive” reports. Other reports always include both Inpatient data and Clinic order data. These reports are referred to as “Combined” reports.</p>
<p>Mutually Exclusive Reports</p>
<p>Mutually Exclusive reports include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Admin Times Report</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Due List Report</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Missed Meds Report</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Cover Sheet Reports</strong></p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>You may run these reports for either Inpatient or Clinic orders for a single patient. You may also run these same reports for Clinic orders, only, for all patients in one or more selected Clinics. BCMA remembers the last order mode you were in, Inpatient or Clinic, so that when you run reports without a patient selected, the correct order mode defaults.</p>
<p>If you select the Print by “Clinic” option, you may select one or more clinics to include in the reports. See the “<a href="#p70_195">Mutually Exclusive Reports – Select Clinics Functionality</a>” section.</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>If a patient record is open:</strong></p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The report dialog Print by selection always defaults to “Patient.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you select the “Inpatient” order mode on the VDL, the report dialog Include Orders selection defaults to “Inpatient Orders.” The Print by selection defaults to “Patient,” Print by “Ward” is enabled, and Print by “Clinic” is disabled.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />

</blockquote></li>
</ul>

</ul>

</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you choose “Inpatient Orders” for the Include Orders selection, the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward.”</p>

<p>The inpatient nurse can run a PRN Effectiveness report that combines both inpatient and clinic data for a single patient to help document PRN effectiveness for medications administered in the Clinic. The clinic nurse, likewise, can</p></td>

<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/529.png)Viewing and Printing Clinic Order Reports (cont.)</td>
<td><p>document PRN effectiveness for medications administered in the Clinic. The clinic nurse, likewise, can document PRN effectiveness for medications administered in the Ward.</p>
<p>Each report dialog contains the following message: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.”</p>
<p>The Print by “Clinic” option is disabled since selecting clinics is not allowed when printing these combined reports.</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>If a patient record is open:</strong></p></li>

</ul>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/531.png)</p></td>

<tr class="even">
<td>Viewing and Printing Clinic Order Reports (cont.)</td>
<td><p>The header of all reports displays the wording: “Includes Inpatient and Clinic Orders.”</p>
<p><strong>MAH Report</strong></p>
<p>The Inpatient nurse may print this report by ward or by patient. The Clinic nurse will print this report by patient.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Date column lists three asterisks (*) to indicate that a medication is not due. This information is also noted in the Legend at the bottom of the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The report also includes information about when an order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” by a provider, and the order Start and Stop Date/Time for the medication.</p>
<p><strong>MAH Report for a Single Patient</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient has Inpatient orders, the header “INPATIENT ORDERS” is printed, followed by a list of all of the patient’s Inpatient orders in two groups:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>Continuous Unit Dose and IV orders</p>
<p>PRN, STAT, and One-Time orders</p>
<p>The word “INPATIENT” is displayed above the Order Start Date for each medication administered in an inpatient ward.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient has Clinic Orders, the header “CLINIC ORDERS” is printed, followed by a list of all of the patient’s Clinic orders in two groups:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>Continuous Unit Dose and IV orders</p>
<p>PRN, STAT, and One-Time orders</p>
<p>The Clinic name is displayed above the Order Start Date for each medication administered in a clinic.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Within each group, the orders are sorted alphabetically by medication name.</p>
<p>A combined legend prints at the end of the report, containing nurse initials for both Inpatient and Clinic administrations, if applicable.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing and Printing Clinic Order Reports (cont.)</td>
<td><p>The word “Location” displays above the “Start Date” in the left hand column header.</p>
<p>Example: MAH Report for Single Patient</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Because of its length, this report is in two (2) screens</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/532.png)<em>MAH Report: Screen 1</em></p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/533.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/534.png)<em>MAH Report: Screen 1 (Continued)</em></p>
<p><strong>MAH Report for a Selected Ward or Nurse Unit</strong></p>
<p>All patients assigned to the selected ward or nurse unit are printed as a series of single patient reports as described above for a single patient.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td>Viewing and Printing Clinic Order Reports (cont.)</td>
<td><p><strong>Med Log Report</strong></p>
<p>The Inpatient nurse may print this report by ward or by patient-almost always by patient. If no patient is selected, the report defaults to by Ward, then the nurse can select one patient on the ward (typical).</p>
<p>The Clinic nurse will print this report by patient.</p>
<p>The Medication Log report displays the Inpatient Ward name (where the medication was administered) above the Start Date for each medication administered in an inpatient ward.</p>
<p>The report displays the Clinic name (where the medication was administered) above the Start Date for each medication administered in a clinic. The report displays the word “Location” above the “Activity Date” in the left hand column header.</p>

<p>Mutually Exclusive Reports – Select Clinics Functionality</p>
<p>You will be able to select one or more clinics for clinic-based mutually exclusive reports by specifying a search prefix entry for your division/location that searches from the beginning of the clinic name, and a search text entry that searches within the clinic name to filter the list of available clinics to a more manageable list.</p>
<p>When you select the “Clinic Orders” option in the Include Orders section of the report dialog, the “Select Clinics” button allows you to print reports by clinic.</p>
<p>To Print Reports by Clinic</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong>Select Clinics</strong> to display the Clinic Selection dialog.</p></li>
<li><p>Enter search criteria in the “Enter Search Prefix” field and click <strong>Search</strong> (example: AL – Albany), and/ or</p></li>
<li><p>Enter a clinic name in the “Enter Search Text” field (example: DERM) and click <strong>Search.</strong></p></li>
<li><p>Select the clinic by clicking on it or use Shift-Click or Ctrl-click to select multiple clinics to include in the report.</p></li>
<li><p>Click <strong>Add</strong>, and the selected clinics move to the Selected Clinics box.</p></li>
<li><p>Click OK, and the data in the Selected Clinics window will be used for the report, and the number of clinics selected will be reflected on the requesting report dialog.</p></li>
</ol></th>
</tr>
</thead>

<span id="_Toc220742764" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 9: Read-Only and Limited Access BCMA

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-5" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></td>
<td><p>Use this chapter when you need to access BCMA in a Read-Only mode to view the VDL and run reports, or in a Limited Access mode, when you want to access BCMA and are not at the patient’s bed side.</p>
<p>This chapter describes what BCMA Read-Only and Limited Access is, the various ways to access each mode, and how to open a patient record in Read-Only or Limited Access mode.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 0%" />
<col style="width: 67%" />
<col style="width: 1%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="2"><h3 id="what-is-read-only-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">What is Read-Only BCMA?</h3></td>
<td colspan="2"><p>Read-Only BCMA provides non-medication administering users the ability to access the BCMA application without performing any actions against a patient’s medical record. The Read-Only functionality outlined here extends access to BCMA data to other end users at VAMCs. Each site will determine which of its users will have access to BCMA in a Read-Only mode.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Read-Only users cannot access or make changes to the BCMA GUI Site Parameter application, nor can they serve as a witness for High Risk/High Alert administrations.</p>
<p>Features Not Available in Read-Only BCMA</p>
<p>When a user with Read-Only access is logged on, the following features will <u>not</u> be available:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Administration of a medication via Scan Medication Bar Code. While a Read-Only user is signed-on to BCMA, the Scanner Status displays as “Not Ready” and the Enable Scanner button is not available.</p></li>
<li><p>Modification of any administration via Unable to Scan functionality. The modification of any administration via Unable to Scan functionality will not be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Edit Med Log option. The Edit Med Log option is disabled in BCMA Read-Only mode.</p></li>
<li><p>CPRS Med Order button. The entry of an order via the CPRS Med Order button will not be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Mark option. Modification of any administration via any Mark option will not be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Add Comment option. Adding a comment to an administration via any Add Comment option will not be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Missing Dose Request. Submission of a Missing Dose Request via any Missing Dose option will not be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Modification of any Ward Stock administration. The Take Action on Bag option will not be available.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>What is Read-Only BCMA? (cont.)</td>
<td colspan="2"><ul>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness comment. The entry of a PRN Effectiveness comment via the PRN Effectiveness Log dialog will not be available.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The following example shows a sample patient record being viewed in Read-Only BCMA. Note the “READ-ONLY” message in the title bar, and the tool bar buttons that are unavailable display as grayed-out. In addition, the Scanner Status displays as “Not Ready” and the Enable Scanner button is not available.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/544.png)Example: BCMA Read-Only VDL</p>
<p>The following example shows how menu options that are unavailable in Read-Only BCMA display as grayed-out.</p></td>
<td></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>What is Read-Only BCMA? (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/545.png)Example: BCMA Read-Only VDL Due List Menu</p>
<p>Features Available in Read-Only BCMA</p>
<p>When a user with Read-Only access is logged on, the following features <u>will</u> be available:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Inpatient Order Mode and Clinic Order Mode are available in Read-Only BCMA.</p></li>
<li><p>The Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB, and IV medication tabs will display the patient’s Virtual Due list.</p></li>
<li><p>The medication administration right-click menu will allow access to the Display Order, Med History, PRN Effectiveness, and Available Bags options.</p></li>
<li><p>Patient demographics will be available by performing a mouse click on the patient demographics box.</p></li>
<li><p>The ability to view Allergies from the Allergies button will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Virtual Due List Parameters and Schedule Types selections will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>BCMA Clinical Reminders will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>All options within the File, View, Reports, Tools, and Help menus will be available except for Edit Med Log.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>What is Read-Only BCMA? (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>BCMA Patient Record Flag functionality will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Within the Due List menu, only Display Order, Med History, PRN Effectiveness, Sort By, and Refresh will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>All BCMA reports will be available, by patient and by ward.</p></li>
<li><p>When a user with Read-Only access opens the PRN Effectiveness Log dialog, they will be limited to viewing the PRN List table, Med History, and Order Detail for a select PRN administration.</p></li>
<li><p>On the IV medication tab within the IV Bag Chronology tree view, the user will be able to expand and collapse the tree view, but will not be able to take action on any item in the tree view.</p></li>
<li><p>The Cover Sheet tab is available and fully functional in Read-Only mode.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="accessing-readonly-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">Accessing Read‑Only BCMA</h3></td>
<td><p>This section describes the three methods for accessing BCMA in Read-Only mode, and provides instructions for signing on to Read-Only BCMA.</p>
<p>Methods to access BCMA in Read-Only Mode</p>
<ul>
<li><p>If you are a user who is assigned the PSB READ ONLY security key, you can only access BCMA in the Read-Only mode. Users who are assigned the PSB READ ONLY security key cannot administer medications, nor can they use BCMA in Limited Access mode. The PSB READ ONLY security key overrides all other BCMA security keys.</p></li>
<li><p>If you are a nursing student with the PSB STUDENT security key, and access BCMA without an instructor present, BCMA defaults to Read-Only mode. In order to administer medications, you must exit BCMA and sign on with your instructor.</p></li>
<li><p>If you are a user who does not hold the PSB READ ONLY security key, you now have an additional option to retrieve a patient record in Read-Only mode by selecting the Open (Read-Only) command from the File menu (see the following example.) For instance, this feature allows a clinician to view the patient’s record and run reports—without inadvertently making changes to medication administration data. Upon closing the Read-Only patient record, BCMA reverts back to the mode that was originally enabled with the user’s security key.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Open (Read-Only) Option on File Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/546.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Accessing Read‑Only BCMA (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> All users, including users who are assigned the PSB READ ONLY security key, will be required to have the PSB GUI CONTEXT – USER secondary menu option.</p>
<p>To sign on to Read-Only BCMA</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>To sign in using two-factor authentication (2FA) you will select the appropriate PIV credentials.</p></li>
</ol>

<p>Enter your PIV PIN.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/548.png)Example: Enter PIV PIN</p></th>

<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/549.png)</p></td>
<td><ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are a user with Read-Only access to BCMA, enter your VistA signon credentials. The system will verify that you have been assigned the PSB READ ONLY security key.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are a nursing student, enter your VistA signon credentials. The system will verify that you have been assigned the PSB STUDENT security key. Click cancel at the Instructor Sign-on dialog box. BCMA automatically defaults to Read-Only mode.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>When sign-on is complete, “READ-ONLY” will display in the title bar, and the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box displays. Proceed to the next section for instructions on opening a patient record in Read-Only BCMA.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconusing-readonly-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/551.png)Using Read‑Only BCMA</h3></td>
<td><p>To Open a Patient Record in Read-Only BCMA</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are signed on as a Read-Only user (including a nursing student without an instructor):</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box is displayed, proceed to step #2 to access a patient record.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the BCMA VDL is displayed, select the Open Patient Record command from the File menu. The BCMA - Patient Select dialog box displays. Proceed to step #2 to access a patient record.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+f</strong></span> to display the File menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">o</span></strong> to display the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are a user who does <u>not</u> hold the PSB READ ONLY security key, and you want to open a patient record in Read-Only mode, select the Open (Read-Only) command from the File menu. The BCMA - Patient Select dialog box displays. Proceed to step #2 to access a patient record.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+f</strong></span> to display the File menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">r</span></strong> to display the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you are signed on as a Read-Only user and you <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> out of the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box, only BCMA ward‑specific reports will be available.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />

<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><p>Using Read‑Only BCMA (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/552.png)</p></th>
<th><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>At the BCMA – Patient Select dialog box, enter one of the following search criteria in the Patient Name field:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient name (Last, First)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient Social Security Number (SSN)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Rm-Bed</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Ward</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA automatically searches for the patient record(s) that match the criteria in the Patient Name field – as you are typing. You must enter at least 2 characters to initiate the search. There is no need to press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>. Note that the search is not case-sensitive.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the patient you are requesting is displayed in the Patient List,</strong> click on the patient record you want to access, then click <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> to access the patient’s VDL in Read-Only mode.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to go to the Patient List, then if multiple records are displayed, use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the patient record. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to access the patient’s VDL in Read-Only mode.</p>
<p>Example: BCMA – Patient Select Dialog box Search by SSN</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/553.png)</p></th>

</blockquote></li>

<li><p>If records are retrieved, but you do not see the intended patient record, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>
<li><p>If you see a “No patients matching…” message, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #4 above.</p></li>
<li><p>If you see a “Too many patients matching…” message, then the system found more than 100 records that matched your criteria. Re-enter more specific patient criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>

<table>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="what-is-limited-access-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">What is Limited Access BCMA?</h3></td>
<td><p>Limited Access BCMA provides medication administering users the ability to access the BCMA application without being at the patient’s bed side. Active, discharged, and deceased patient records can be opened in Limited Access mode without scanning or using Unable to Scan.</p>
<p>Features Not Available in Limited Access BCMA</p>
<p>When a user logs on and selects Open (Limited Access) from the File menu, the following features will <u>not</u> be available:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Administration of a medication via scanning.</strong> The scanner status remains in a Not Ready state whenever a patient record is opened in BCMA Limited Access mode.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Administration of a medication via Unable to Scan functionality.</strong> The Unable to Scan and Unable to Scan-Create WS options will be disabled.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Modification of any IV or Ward Stock administration.</strong> Unable to Scan, Unable to Scan-Create WS, and Take Action on Bag options will be disabled.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Marking a patch as Removed.</strong> The option to mark a patch as Removed will be disabled.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Use of the CPRS Med Order button.</strong> The entry of an order via the CPRS Med Order button will be disabled.</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The following example shows a sample patient record being viewed in Limited Access BCMA. Note the “LIMITED ACCESS” message in the title bar, and the tool bar buttons that are unavailable display as grayed-out. In addition, the Scanner Status displays as “Not Ready” and the Enable Scanner button is not available.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>What is Limited Access BCMA? (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Example: BCMA Limited Access VDL</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/557.png)</p>
<p>The following example shows how menu options that are unavailable in Limited Access BCMA display as grayed-out.</p>
<p>Example: BCMA Limited Access VDL Due List Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/558.png)</p></td>
</tr>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>What is Limited Access BCMA? (cont.)</td>
<td><p>Features Available in Limited Access BCMA</p>
<p>When a user logs on and selects Open (Limited Access) from the File menu, the following features <u>will</u> be available:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Inpatient Order Mode and Clinic Order Mode are available in Limited Access BCMA.</p></li>
<li><p>The Unit Dose, IVP/IVPB, and IV medication tabs will display the patient’s Virtual Due list.</p></li>
<li><p>The Edit Med Log option will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Patient demographics will be available by performing a mouse click on the patient demographics box.</p></li>
<li><p>The ability to view Allergies from the Allergies button will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Virtual Due List Parameters and Schedule Types selections will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>All options within the File, View, Reports, Tools, and Help menus will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>BCMA Patient Record Flag functionality will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>All BCMA reports will be available, by patient and by ward.</p></li>
<li><p>Within the Due List menu, all options will be available except for Unable to Scan, Unable to Scan – Create WS, and Take Action on Bag.</p></li>
<li><p>Submission of a Missing Dose Request via any Missing Dose option will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Adding a comment to an administration via any Add Comment option will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Marking appropriate administrations as Held or Refused will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>Marking a Given administration as Undo Given will be available.</p></li>
<li><p>The ability to document PRN Effectiveness will be available through the right click menu, Due List menu and via BCMA Clinical Reminders.</p></li>
<li><p>The Cover Sheet tab is available and fully functional in Limited Access BCMA.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="accessing-limited-access-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">Accessing Limited Access BCMA</h3></td>
<td><p>This section describes the method for accessing BCMA in Limited Access mode.</p>
<p>Methods to access BCMA in Limited Access Mode</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The Open (Limited Access) option is available on the File Menu; all users, except for those users with the PSB READ ONLY security key, can select the Open (Limited Access) option.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+f</span></strong> to display the File menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">l</span></strong> to access Open (Limited Access).</p>
<p>Example: Open (Limited Access) Option on File Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/559.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconusing-limited-access-bcma" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/560.png)Using Limited Access BCMA</h3></td>
<td><p>To Open a Patient Record in Limited Access BCMA</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you are accessing BCMA in the Limited Access mode:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box is displayed, proceed to step #2 to access a patient record.</p></li>
<li><p>If the BCMA VDL is displayed, select the Open Patient Record command from the File menu. The BCMA - Patient Select dialog box displays. Proceed to step #2 to access a patient record.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>alt+f</strong></span> to display the File menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">l</span></strong> to display the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you are accessing BCMA in the Limited Access mode and you <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> out of the BCMA - Patient Select dialog box, only BCMA ward‑specific reports will be available.</p>
<p>Example: Limited Access BCMA with Patient Select Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/561.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Using Limited Access BCMA (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>At the BCMA – Patient Select dialog box, enter one of the following search criteria in the Patient Name field:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient name (Last, First)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Patient Social Security Number (SSN)</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Rm-Bed</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Ward</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA automatically searches for the patient record(s) that match the criteria in the Patient Name field – as you are typing. You must enter at least 2 characters to initiate the search. There is no need to press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>. Note that the search is not case-sensitive.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>If the patient you are requesting is displayed in the Patient List,</strong> click on the patient record you want to access, then click <span class="smallcaps">ok</span> to access the patient’s VDL in Limited Access mode.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to go to the Patient List, then if multiple records are displayed, use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to select the patient record. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> button, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to access the patient’s VDL in Limited Access mode.</p>
<p>Example: BCMA – Patient Select Dialog box Search by SSN</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/562.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>

<li><blockquote>
<p>If the patient you are requesting is not displayed in the Patient List:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>If more records are retrieved than can be displayed in the Patient List, scroll bars will appear to allow you to scroll through the data. Scroll to the patient record, click on the patient record you want to access, then click <strong>OK</strong> to access the patient’s VDL in Limited Access mode.</p></li>
<li><p>If records are retrieved, but you do not see the intended patient record, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>
<li><p>If you see a “No patients matching…” message, re-enter your patient search criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>
<li><p>If you see a “Too many patients matching…” message, then the system found more than 100 records that matched your criteria. Re-enter more specific patient criteria, as indicated in step #2 above.</p></li>
</ul>

<span id="_Toc58129747" class="anchor"></span>

Chapter 10: Editing the Medication Log

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-6" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></th>
<th><p>Use this chapter when you need to edit a specific medication administration entry that has been created during the medication administration process. Using this option, you can even perform a patient lookup to complete edits to past medications, even after the patient has been discharged or deceased.</p>
<p>This chapter describes how to use the Edit Med Log option in GUI BCMA for editing a patient’s medication log. It is divided into two sections—Accessing the Edit Med Log Option and Using the Edit Med Log Option.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="accessing-the-edit-med-log-option" class="Subheading-Style">Accessing the Edit Med Log Option</h3></td>
<td><p>You can access the Edit Med Log option for an open patient record on the screen, or from a blank BCMA screen. This section describes how to access the Edit Med Log option and how to change the administration date.</p>
<p><strong>Notes:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><p>You can only edit a medication entry for an order that you have administered unless you hold the PSB MANAGER Security key. With this key, you can also edit other user’s medication entries. BCMA tracks all edits, which you can include on the Medication Log Report by selecting the “Audits” option when requesting a report.</p></li>
<li><p>The Edit Med Log option is also available while using Limited Access mode.</p></li>
<li><p>The Edit Med Log option is <u>not</u> available for users with the PSB READ ONLY security key, or when users open a patient record in Read-Only mode. For more information, please refer to Chapter 8, “Read-Only and Limited Access BCMA.”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>To access the Edit Med Log option</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Edit Med Log option from the File menu.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/566.png)Example: Edit Med Log Option</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+f</span></strong> to display the File menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">e</span></strong> to display the Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box or the Patient Select dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Accessing the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you have an open patient record on the VDL, the Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box displays the current patient’s medications that were administered today. Proceed to step #5 to change the Administration Date if necessary.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Edit Med Log Administration Selection Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/567.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/568.png)If no patient record is currently open on the VDL, the Patient Select dialog box displays. Enter the patient’s Social Security Number (SSN), patient’s name (last,first with no spaces), Rm-Bd, or Ward. Proceed to step #3.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The system automatically searches for patient records that match your search criteria as it is being entered. For example, if you enter a partial name or SSN, it searches for records that match your entry.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select the patient name from the Patient Select dialog box and click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>. The Patient Confirmation dialog box then displays.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />

<th><p>Example: Edit Med Log Patient Select Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/569.png)</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>At the Patient Confirmation dialog box, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the patient lookup is correct, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">yes</span></strong>. The Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box then displays.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the patient lookup is incorrect, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> and repeat steps #2-3 to select another patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If any active PRF assignments exist for this patient, the <strong><span class="smallcaps">details</span></strong> button will be enabled in the Patient Flags section of the dialog box. It is strongly recommended that you click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">details</span></strong> button to view the Patient Record Flag report, especially for behavioral flags, to view information which may be critical to patient and employee safety.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to activate the <span class="smallcaps"><strong>yes</strong></span> or <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> button, and then press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>enter</strong></span> to continue.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Accessing the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/570.png)Example: Patient Confirmation Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/571.png)Example: Edit Med Log Administration Selection Dialog Box</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>The Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box displays all of the medications administered for the selected patient for the date shown. By default, it displays medications that were administered today. To change the date, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>In the date field, type a valid date and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>. Valid date formats include NOV 24 2010, 24 NOV 10, 11/24/10, or 112410.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Accessing the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/572.png)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/573.png)</p></td>
<td><p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> or <strong><span class="smallcaps">shift-tab</span></strong> to move among the different areas of the dialog box.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Use the left or right <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> buttons on either side of the date field to display medications administered on the previous or next day.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> button to display a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date on the calendar. Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to close the calendar.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Edit Med Log option does not allow access to future dates. See example below for other calendar options</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/574.png)Example: Date Selection Calendar</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>After selecting a medication administration date, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the administered medication(s) you intend to edit is displayed, proceed to the next section “Using the Edit Med Log Option.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If no medications were administered on the date you selected, BCMA displays a “No Meds Found!” message. Repeat step #5 to select another date..</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><h3 id="using-the-edit-med-log-option" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/575.png)Using the Edit Med Log Option</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/576.png)</p></td>
<td><p>This section describes how to edit a patient’s medication log using the Edit Med Log option. You edit the Admin Status, Action Date/Time, Injection Site (if applicable), and PRN Reason and Effectiveness (if applicable). You can edit the Dispensed Drug, Units Given, and Units for Unit Dose orders only. You may also add a Dispensed Drug if needed.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Every field on the Edit Med Log dialog box is audited and displays on the Medication Log Report when you select the “Audits” option.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Witness information captured during High Risk/High Alert administrations is not displayed, nor available for editing in the Edit Med Log feature.</p>
<p>After you have selected the desired administration date, the Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box displays the patient’s name, Social Security Number (SSN) and the following data for medications administered on that date:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Type:</strong> Schedule Types, such as C for Continuous, OC for On-Call, O for One-Time, and P for PRN.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Medication:</strong> Name of the orderable item.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Status:</strong> Displays the administration status information for a medication, such as Given, Refused, Held, Removed, Missing Dose, Infusing, Stopped, Complete, and Unknown.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Action Date/Time:</strong> Displays the date and time of the last action taken on the medication.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Int:</strong> Displays the initials of the individual who documented the last action.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/577.png)Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/578.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/579.png)</p></th>
<th><p>Example: Edit Med Log Administration Selection Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/580.png)</p>
<p>To edit an administered medication</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>From the Edit Med Log Administration Selection dialog box, click on the administered medication that you want to edit, and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>. The Edit Med Log dialog box then displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you are about to edit an administration associated with an order that has a “Provider Hold” status, a warning message will display.</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>In the Admin Status field, select an action from the drop-down list box that reflects the correct status of the medication administration. The drop-down list will only display valid actions based on the current order type, the current action status, and the action status of other administrations for the same order (when applicable).</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If the administration status is Unknown, the Admin Status field will be blank, and the user must change the status to Given, Not Given, Held, or Refused. Administrations cannot be changed to a status of Missing.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select an Admin Status in the drop-down list box.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/581.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Example: Edit Med Log Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/582.png)</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Action Date/Time field, specify the actual date and time the action was taken. You can type a valid date@time entry (see formatting examples below) or click on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> to use the calendar.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to advance to the drop-down arrow, then <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to use the calendar.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Edit Med Log option does not allow entry of future dates or times.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/583.png)Example: Action Date/Time Status Field</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/584.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/585.png)</p></td>
<td><p>Date Formatting</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Nov 30, 2010, 30 NOV 10, 11/30/10, 113010</p></li>
<li><p>N (for NOW)</p></li>
<li><p>T (for Today), T-1 (Yesterday), T-3W (3 weeks ago)</p></li>
<li><p>Omitting the year assumes the current year.</p>
<p>Time Formatting</p></li>
<li><p>HH:MM or HHMM</p></li>
<li><p>Omitting the time assumes the current time</p>
<p>Date@Time Formatting Examples</p></li>
<li><p>T@11:20 (Today at 11:20 a.m.)</p></li>
<li><p>113010@1120 (November 30, 2010 at 11:20 a.m.)</p></li>
<li><p><strong>113010@1300 (November 30, 2010 at 1:00 p.m.)</strong></p></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/586.png)Example: Date/Time Selection Calendar</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>In the Injection Site drop-down list box, select the location on the patient where the medication was injected (if applicable).</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select an injection site in the drop-down list box.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/587.png)Example: Edit Med Log Dialog Box Injection Site Field</p>
<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>In the PRNs Reason drop-down list box, select one of the pre-defined reasons (if applicable).</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">arrow</span></strong> keys to locate and select a Reason in the drop-down list box.</p>
<p>Example: Edit Med Log Dialog Box PRN Reason Field</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/588.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>In the PRN Effectiveness comment field, enter an optional comment to describe the effectiveness of the medication given to the patient, up to 150 characters in length.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> PRN required pain scores are not supported by the Edit Med Log option. The preferred method for documenting PRN Effectiveness is via the BCMA Clinical Reminders marquee.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/589.png)Example: Edit Med Log Dialog Box PRN Effectiveness Field</p>
<p>The Dispensed Drugs area of the Edit Med Log dialog box shows a list of dispensed drugs, additives, and/or solutions, including the units ordered, units given, and units (TAB, CAP, etc.). You can only edit this area for Unit Dose orders. You can also add a dispensed drug (if necessary).</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When editing or adding Dispensed Drugs, the Name field is restricted to 50 characters, the Units Given must be a number less than 50, and the Units column must be 40 characters or less.</p>
<ol start="7" type="1">
<li><p>To edit a Dispensed Drug, perform the following actions as needed:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To edit the Dispensed Drug Name, right-click on the Name cell that you want to edit, and then select <strong><span class="smallcaps">edit</span></strong> from the drop-down menu. Enter a full or partial dispensed drug name and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> to display a list of drugs that matches the drug orderable item for the medication order. Select the appropriate drug from the list and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/590.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/591.png)</p></td>
<td><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To edit the Units Given, right-click on the Units Given cell that you want to edit and then select <strong><span class="smallcaps">edit</span></strong> from the drop-down menu. Enter the number of Units Given, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To edit the Units column, right-click on the Units cell you want to edit and then select <strong><span class="smallcaps">edit</span></strong> from the drop-down menu. Enter the new value for Units, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">ctrl-e</span></strong> to Edit a drug in the Dispensed Drugs area of the dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Edit Med Log Edit Dispensed Drug</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/592.png)</p>
<p>Example: Edit Med Log Dispensed Drugs Area – Drug Name Lookup</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/593.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="8" type="1">
<li><p>To add a Dispensed Drug, perform the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To add a dispensed drug, right-click anywhere in the Dispensed Drugs area, and then select the Add Dispensed Drug command from the drop-down menu. A new row displays for editing purposes, and the cursor is in the Dispensed Drug Name field.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>In the Dispensed Drug Name column, type a full or partial dispensed drug name and then press enter to display a list of dispensed drugs that matches the drug orderable item for the medication order. Select the appropriate drug from the list and then click ok.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Right-click in the Units Given cell that corresponds to the drug you just added, and then select edit from the drop-down menu. Enter the number of Units Given, and then press enter.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Right-click in the Units cell that corresponds to the drug you just added, and then select edit from the drop-down menu. Enter the value for Units, and then press enter.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">ctrl-a</span></strong> to add a drug in the Dispensed Drugs area of the dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Edit Med Log Add Dispensed Drug</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/594.png)</p></td>
</tr>

<colgroup>

<td>Using the Edit Med Log Option (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="9" type="1">
<li><p>Enter the reason the medication entry is being edited in the Comment field. This information displays on the Medication Log Report when a user selects the “Comments” option.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA will not save your changes to the Medication Log until you enter the required Comment.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/595.png)Example: Edit Med Log Dialog Box Comment Field</p>
<ol start="10" type="1">
<li><p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to save all changes made to the patient’s Medication Log, or <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> to cancel the changes.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Toc199860926" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 11: Viewing and Printing BCMA Reports

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 25%" />
<col style="width: 74%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-7" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></th>
<th>This chapter describes a variety of reports originating from BCMA that you can view and print on-screen via the BCMA VDL or via Tabs in CPRS. You can also use the reports to view patient demographic and allergy information.</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="p70_455" class="anchor"></span>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="enhancements-to-report-printing" class="Subheading-Style">Enhancements to Report Printing</h3></td>
<td><p>Here are the changes to the original report printing functionality in BCMA V. 3.0:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Removal times have been added where there are admin times for medications requiring removal (MRR).</p></li>
<li><p>Both “Removal” and “Given” administration information is available for reporting.</p></li>
<li><p>The new anatomic locations for MRRs are included in BCMA reports.</p></li>
<li><p>The word “Injection Site” has been replaced with “Body Site” in report column headers that could include both Dermal Sites for MRRs and Injection Sites for non-MRRs.</p></li>
<li><p>The word “Injection Site” has been replaced with “Dermal Site” when the orderable item for the medication order is an MRR for reports with one specific medication.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Mutually Exclusive and Combined reports added containing Inpatient as well as Clinic order data.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Medication Administration History (MAH) Report:</strong> The Date column lists three asterisks (*) to indicate that a medication is not due. This information is also noted in the Legend at the bottom of the MAH Report.</p></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>The report also includes information about when an order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” by a provider, and the order Start and Stop Date/Time for the medication.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Medication Variance Report:</strong> Provides “exceptions” (variances) to the medication administration process. It also lists “event” information within a selected date range, such as the type and number of events, and the total percentage of events that occurred. A variance preceded by a minus sign (such as –24) indicates the number of minutes that a medication was given before the administration time.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/596.png)Enhancements to Report Printing (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p><strong>Cumulative Vitals/Measurement Report:</strong> Lists a patient’s vitals from the Vitals package, along with their demographics and hospital location information. You cannot print this report by ward.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Ward-based Reports:</strong> Simply click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> at the Patient Lookup dialog box to access the Menu Bar — without opening a patient record — and print ward-based reports only, except for the Cumulative Vitals/Measurement Report. A patient’s file must be opened to access patient-specific reports.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>CHUI Missing Dose Report:</strong> Changed the line item “Dosage Schedule” on the BCMA CHUI Missing Dose Report to “Schedule” to coincide with the Missing Dose Email Notification change described on the next page.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Missed Medications Report:</strong> Indicates when a medication order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” in CPRS or Inpatient Medications V. 5.0. The Hold information is provided below the medication information on the report, and only applies to administrations due within the Hold timeframe.</p></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>The “Order Num” column on the report lists the actual order number and order type (i.e., Unit Dose or IV). This information is quite helpful when troubleshooting problems with BCMA.</p>
<p>Enhancements to the Missed Medications Report allow the user to selectively include or exclude Held and Refused orders in the report. A verified “Ver” column contains the initials of the nurse who verified the order or three asterisks (*) indicating the order was not nurse verified.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report:</strong> Displays and groups active, expired or discontinued, and future orders for the current patient or by selected patients on a ward. User specified criteria includes order status (Active, Future, Expired/DC’d), and whether to include actions and comments.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />
<col style="width: 70%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Enhancements to Report Printing (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p><strong>Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report:</strong> Displays and groups active, expired or discontinued, and future orders with a schedule type of PRN for the current patient or by selected patients on a ward. User specified criteria includes order status (Active, Future, Expired/DC’d), and whether to include actions and comments.</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report:</strong> Displays and groups IV bag information on active, expired, and discontinued orders for the current patient or by selected patients on a ward. User specified criteria includes order status (Infusing bags, Stopped bags, All others), and whether to include actions and comments.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Cover Sheet–Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders Report:</strong> Displays and groups expired and discontinued orders, as well as orders that will expire for the current patient or by selected patients on a ward. User specified criteria includes order status (Expired/DC’d, Expiring Today, Expiring Tomorrow), and whether to include actions and comments.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>Medication Therapy Report:</strong> Includes information similar to the Medication History Report but does not require a patient record to be open. The report can be run for the current patient or by selected patients on a ward. User can select medications by searching by VA Drug Class, Orderable Item, or Dispense Drug. Other user specified criteria includes date range, schedule types, and whether to include/exclude comments.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>IV Bag Status Report:</strong> Provides status on large volume IV bags, excluding available bags, by patient or selected patients on a ward. User can include/exclude by IV bag status: completed, infusing, stopped, missing dose, held, refused, and IV bags for which no action has been taken on the order. Other user specified criteria includes date range, order status (Active, DC’d, Expired), and whether to include/exclude comments.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="mutually-exclusive-reports" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/597.png)Mutually Exclusive Reports</h3></td>
<td><p>Since BCMA includes both Inpatient and Clinic order data, the reports are segregated into two different categories: “Mutually Exclusive” reports that separate Inpatient data from Clinic order data, and “Combined” reports that include both Inpatient data and Clinic order data. See chapter entitled, “Clinic Orders.”</p>
<p>Mutually Exclusive reports allow you to select either Inpatient or Clinic order data to be included in the report. When printed, the report header displays “Include Inpatient Orders Only” for reports that include only Inpatient order data or “Include Clinic Orders Only” for reports that include only Clinic order data. Mutually Exclusive reports include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Admin Times Report</p></li>
<li><p>Due List Report</p></li>
<li><p>Missed Meds Report</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet Reports</p></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If a patient record is open:</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>The report dialog Print by selection always defaults to “Patient.”</p></li>
<li><p>If you select the “Inpatient” order mode on the VDL, the report dialog Include Orders selection defaults to “Inpatient Orders.” The Print by selection defaults to “Patient,” Print by “Ward” is enabled, and Print by “Clinic” is disabled.</p></li>
<li><p>If you select the “Clinic” order mode on the VDL, the report dialog Include Orders selection defaults to “Clinic Orders.” The Print by selection defaults to “Patient,” Print by “Ward” is disabled, and Print by “Clinic” is enabled.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Mutually Exclusive Reports (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/598.png)Example: Clinic Orders/Default to Print by Patient</p>
<ul>
<li><p>If you change the report dialog Include Orders selection from “Inpatient Orders” to “Clinic Orders” (or vice versa), the dependent corresponding Print by option must also change.</p></li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If no patient record is open:</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>The report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward” or “Clinic,” based on user parameter that indicates the last mode that you selected, and Print by “Patient” is disabled.</p></li>
<li><p>If you choose “Inpatient Orders” for the Include Orders selection, the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward.”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Include Inpatient Orders/Default to Print by Ward</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/599.png)</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>

<td><ul>
<li><p>If you choose “Clinic Orders” for the Include Orders selection, the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Clinic.”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Include Clinic Orders/Default to Print by Clinic</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/601.png)</p></td>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="combined-reports" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/602.png)Combined Reports</h3></td>
<td><p>Combined reports automatically include both Inpatient and Clinic order data in the report. The inpatient nurse can see any IVs that were infused in Clinic that must be marked as completed. The clinic nurse can see any IVs that were infused in Inpatient that must be marked as completed.</p>
<p>Combined reports include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>MAH Report</p></li>
<li><p>Med Log Report</p></li>
<li><p>Med History Report</p></li>
<li><p>IV Bag Status Report</p></li>
<li><p>Med Therapy Report</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness Report</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The inpatient nurse can run a PRN Effectiveness report that combines both inpatient and clinic data for a single patient to help document PRN effectiveness for medications administered in the Clinic. The clinic nurse, likewise, can document PRN effectiveness for medications administered in the Ward.</p>
<p>Each report dialog contains the following message: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.”</p>
<p>The Print by “Clinic” option is disabled since selecting clinics is not allowed when printing these combined reports.</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If a patient record is open:</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>The Print by “Patient” option is enabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Patient.”</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Combined Reports (cont.)</th>
<th><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/603.png)Example: Default to Print by Patient</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>If no patient record is open:</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>The Print by “Patient” option is disabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward.”</p></li>
</ul>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/604.png)Example: Default to Print by Ward</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tbody>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
