<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-demographics-data" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/605.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/606.png)Viewing/Printing Demographics Data</h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Patient Demographics command (or button) to view or print personal, admission, eligibility, and appointment information about the patient whose orders are displayed on the BCMA VDL. This information was electronically documented when the patient was admitted to your medical center.</p>
<p>To view/print a patient’s demographics data</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Patient Demographics command from the View menu. The Patient Inquiry dialog box displays, with the patient’s demographics data.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+v</span></strong> to display the View menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">p</span></strong> to display the Patient Inquiry dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Patient Inquiry Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/607.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing Demographics Data (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Review the patient’s demographics data, and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> to return to the patient’s VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> to display the Printer dialog box. Proceed to step #3.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> and <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> buttons.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Select a printer from the drop-down list box that you want to use for outputting a report with the patient’s demographics data. Then click <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong>.</span></p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The printer that you select becomes the “default” printer for <em>all</em> reports printed from BCMA.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-allergy-and-adr-information" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/608.png)Viewing/Printing Allergy and ADR Information</h3></td>
<td><p>Clicking on the Allergies command (or button) displays allergy and adverse drug reaction (ADR) information documented about the patient in the Adverse Reaction Tracking (ART) package. This includes the causative agent, drug class, signs and symptoms, and whether the allergy/ADR was verified and observed. If the Allergies command/ button is grayed out, no allergies or adverse drug reactions were documented about the patient.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCMA only displays allergy information, not a drug “interaction” check.</p>
<p>To view/print a patient’s allergy and ADR information</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Allergies command from View menu. The Patient Allergy List dialog box displays, with the patient’s allergy and ADR information.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+v</span></strong> to display the View menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">a</span></strong> to display the Patient Allergy List dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Patient Allergy List Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/609.png)</p></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-an-order-from-medications-display-order" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/610.png)Viewing/Printing an Order from Medications (Display Order)</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA provides several ways for you to display (and print) the order details for Unit Dose and IV medication orders from Inpatient Medications V. 5.0. They include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Select a medication on the BCMA VDL, and then<br />
press <span class="smallcaps">f4</span></p></li>
<li><p>Double-click on an order displayed on the BCMA VDL</p></li>
<li><p>Use the Display Order command in the Due List menu</p></li>
<li><p>Use the Display Order command in the right-click drop-down menu (on VDL or Cover Sheet)</p></li>
</ul>
<p>Note: The Display Order detail report is especially useful for the nurse to view if CPRS Provider Override Reasons/Pharmacist Interventions are associated with an order, as indicated by a yellow highlighted cell in the verified “Ver” column.</p>
<p>To view/print an order from Inpatient Medications</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select a medication order on the patient’s VDL.</p></li>
<li><p>Select the Display Order command from the Due List menu. The Display Order dialog box displays, with the details of the medication order.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">f4</span></strong> to display the Display Order dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 29%" />

<td>Viewing/Printing an Order from Inpatient Medications (Display Order) (cont.)</td>
<td><p>This section provides examples of an IV Piggyback and IV medication order as they were entered using Inpatient Medications V. 5.0.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/612.png)Example: Display Order Dialog Box for IV Piggyback Medication Order</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/613.png)Example: Display Order Dialog Box for IV Medication Order</p></td>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing an Order from Inpatient Medications (Display Order) (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Review the patient’s medication order, and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> to return to the patient’s VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> to display the Printer dialog box. Proceed to step #4.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> and <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> buttons.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>Select a printer from the drop-down list box that you want to use for outputting a report, with the patient’s medication order. Then click <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong>.</span></p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The printer that you select becomes the “default” printer for <em>all</em> reports printed from BCMA.</p>
<p>Provider Override Reasons/Pharmacist Interventions</p>
<p>If CPRS Provider override reasons and/or Pharmacist interventions exist for an order, a summary of the order’s <u>current</u> CPRS Order Checks, Provider override reasons and Pharmacist intervention information will be included in the BCMA Order Detail report, below “Spec Inst.” The following pages show various examples of this report.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Viewing/Printing an Order from Inpatient Medications (Display Order) (cont.) | This section provides examples of BCMA Display Order Detail reports containing provider override and pharmacist intervention information. |

In the following example, both current CPRS Provider Overrides and current Pharmacist Interventions exist for a critical drug-drug interaction or an allergy/ADR associated with the order.

Example: Order Detail Report with Provider Override and Pharmacist Intervention

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-bcma-reports-with-special-instructions-other-print-info" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing BCMA Reports with Special Instructions / Other Print Info</h3></td>
<td><p>The following BCMA reports invoke a 74 character word wrap for Special Instructions and Other Print Info to accommodate unlimited text:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Medication Administration History (MAH) Report</p></li>
<li><p>Display Order Detail Report</p></li>
<li><p>Due List Report</p></li>
<li><p>IV Bag Status Report</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet Report – Medication Overview Report</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet Report – PRN Overview Report</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet Report – IV Overview</p></li>
<li><p>Cover Sheet Report – Expired/DC’d/Expiring Report</p></li>
</ul>
<p>When printing the MAH report to a printer the following applies:</p>
<p>If Special Instructions / Other Print Info need to flow to another printed page, a blank line with the message: “CONTINUED ON NEXT PAGE*” is printed before the page break. The message: “*CONTINUED FROM PREVIOUS PAGE *” and a blank line is printed on the subsequent page after the page headers.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-a-due-list-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/617.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/618.png)Viewing/Printing a Due List Report</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA lets you print and preview a Due List Report directly from the BCMA VDL. This report provides detailed information about active and future Unit Dose and IV Inpatient and Clinic medication orders that are “due” for administering to a patient — during a timeframe that you specify — within a 24-hour period.</p>
<p>The Due List Report includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADR information, plus detailed information about an order, such as whether (or not) the medication is a self-med; the medication type, schedule, dose, and route; Special Instructions; administration times; Last Given date and time; Start/Stop date and time; and the individual(s) who verified the order.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When including Clinic Orders in the Due List Report, parameters for Allowable Time Limits (Before Scheduled Admin Time and After Scheduled Admin Time) are ignored.</p>
<p>To view/print a Due List Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Due List command from the Reports menu. The Patient Due List dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">d</span></strong> to display the Patient Due List dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />

<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Date, and Start and Stop Times of the Due List Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Date for Report list box displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provides selections.</p></th>
</tr>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-a-medication-log-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/638.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/639.png)Viewing/Printing a Medication Log Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can print (and still view on-screen) a patient’s Medication Log Report (or Med Log Report), listing <em>every</em> action taken on an Inpatient or Clinic medication order within a user-specified date range. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data. The inpatient Ward name, where the medication was administered, displays above the Start Date for each medication administered in an inpatient ward. The Clinic name, where the medication was administered, displays above the Start Date for each medication administered in a clinic. You can choose to include/exclude Comments and Audits performed on the patient’s medication orders. Audits include “actions” taken on a medication.</p>
<p>The Medication Log Report also includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADR information, plus detailed information about the order, such as the drug/additive/solution; the orderable item dose, schedule, route, and injection site; Action date and time; Activity Start/Stop date and time; Unique Identifier Number for the bag; Unit ordered and given, and the clinician(s) who took an action on the medication.</p>
<p>Witness for High Risk/High Alert Drugs information also displays in the Medication Log Report, when applicable, if you select Include Comments on the Patient Medication Log Report Dialog box. Witness name, date, time and comments appear below the user comments and above audit areas in the report. If you choose to exclude comments from the report, the report will not display witness sign-on information or witness comments.</p>
<p>See <a href="#p70_334a">Example: Medication Log with Witness Information</a> at the end of this section.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Medication Log Report lists medications with a “Not Given” status in the Audit Trail section of the Log, not on the BCMA VDL. Administrations that were Cancelled are not listed on the Report.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />

</ol>

</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Date for Report list box displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provides selections.</p></th>

</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you choose to print selected patients, you must click <strong><span class="smallcaps">select patients</span></strong> and then select the patients you want to preview or print, then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong>.</p></td>

<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut</strong>: Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the <strong><span class="smallcaps">preview, print</span></strong> and <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> buttons.</p>
<p>Example: Print Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/645.png)</p>
<ol start="8" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one or more of the following actions, then click <span class="smallcaps"><strong>ok</strong>:</span></p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select a printer from the drop-down list box that you want to use for outputting the Medication Log Report.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Check the Queuing check box and enter the Date and Time you want the report to print. Click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> in the drop-down list box to display a choice of dates and times.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-an-mah-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing an MAH Report</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/649.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/650.png)</p></td>
<td><p>You can view on-screen and print a Medication Administration History (MAH) Report for Unit Dose and IV Inpatient and Clinic medication orders. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.” The word “INPATIENT” displays above the Order Start Date for each medication administered in an inpatient ward. All Inpatient orders are grouped together followed by all Clinic orders. With each group, orders are sorted according to existing MAH sort functionality.</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Date column lists three asterisks (*) to indicate that a medication is not due. This information is also noted in the Legend at the bottom of the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The report also includes information about when an order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” by a provider, and the order Start and Stop Date/Time for the medication.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>This report lists a clinician’s name and initials, and the exact time that an action was taken on an order (in a conventional MAR format). Each order is listed alphabetically by the orderable item. The Date column lists three asterisks (*) to indicate that a medication is not due. This information is also noted in the Legend at the bottom of the MAH Report.</p>
<p>An MAH Report includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADRs, plus detailed information about the order, such as the drug/additive/solution; the medication schedule, dose, route, and injection site; the actual administration times; the name and initials of the clinician who administered the medication; and the individuals who verified the order. It also includes information about when an order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” by a provider, and the order Start and Stop Date/Time for the medication.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If no parameter is defined in CPRS, the maximum date range defaults to a seven-date range. For example, a</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 32%" />
<col style="width: 67%" />

<p>To view/print an MAH Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Medication Admin History command from the Reports menu. The Medication Admin History dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">h</span></strong> to display the Medication Admin History dialog box.</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/651.png)Example: Medication Admin History Dialog Box</p>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-a-missed-medications-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing a Missed Medications Report</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA V. 3.0 lets you print a Missed Medications Report (or Missed Meds Report), for Continuous and One-Time Unit Dose and IV Piggyback Inpatient and Clinic medications that were not administered to a patient during a medication pass.</p>
<p>A Missed Medications Report includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADR information, plus detailed information about the order, such as the medication type; the administration date and time; and the order number. The report also includes a “Ver” column containing the initials of the nurse who verified the order or three asterisks (*) indicating the order was not nurse verified.</p>
<p>Users can specify a Start and Stop Date/Time for the report, defaulting to a 24-hour period but with a maximum limit based on a CPRS site parameter. The following items can also be included in the report:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Active, On Hold, DC’d, and Expired orders</p></li>
<li><p>Held and Refused administrations and missing doses</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Comments/ reasons</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Held, Refused and Comments/Reasons checkboxes will automatically be selected as a default when the report dialog initially displays. These settings will always be in effect when the report is executed. The Comments/Reasons checkbox will be selected regardless of parameter settings for Reports-Include Comments. Upon display of the dialog, you will be able to uncheck these checkboxes if desired.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Self-medications do not display on the Missed Medications Report.</p>
<p>To view/print a Missed Medications Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Missed Medications command from the Reports menu. The Patient Missed Medications dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>

<p>Example: Patient Missed Medications Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/660.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Start and Stop Dates, and Start and Stop Times for the Missed Medications Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Date for Report list box displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provide selections.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the different areas of the dialog box.</p></th>

The Hold information applies only to administrations due within the Hold timeframe. The “Order Num” column on the report lists the actual order number and order type (i.e., Unit Dose or IV). This information is quite helpful when troubleshooting problems with BCMA.</p></td>

<table>

</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-a-prn-effectiveness-list-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/674.png)Viewing/Printing a PRN Effectiveness List Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can view (and print) a PRN Effectiveness List Report using BCMA V. 3.0. This Report lists PRN Inpatient and Clinic medications administered to a patient that need Effectiveness comments. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.” It also includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADR information; plus the PRN medication, administration date and time; and the individual(s) who administered the order.</p>
<p>To view/print a PRN Effectiveness Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the PRN Effectiveness List command from the Reports menu. The PRN Effectiveness List dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">p</span></strong> to display the PRN Effectiveness List dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: PRN Effectiveness List Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/675.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Start and Stop Dates, and Start and Stop Times for the PRN Effectiveness List Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/676.png)Viewing/Printing a PRN Effectiveness List Report (cont.)</td>
<td><p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/677.png)To view/print a PRN Effectiveness List Report (cont.)</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Date for Report list box displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provides selections.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the different areas of the dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Print by area, select to print by Patient or Ward. The Inpatient nurse may print by Patient or Ward. The Clinic nurse may print by Patient, only. “Print by Clinic” is disabled.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Print by “Patient” option is enabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Patient.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>Example: PRN Effectiveness Report Dialog with Patient Record Open</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/678.png)</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If no patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Print by “Patient” option is disabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-an-administration-times-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing an Administration Times Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can print, and still view on-screen, an Administration Times Report. This report lists a patient’s Inpatient and Clinic Order medications by the scheduled administration time (from the earliest to the latest).</p>
<p>The Administration Times Report includes patient demographic data, allergies and ADR information, plus detailed information about the order, such as the medication type, dose, route, and the administration time.</p>
<p>To view/print an Administration Times Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Administration Times command from the Reports menu. The Patient Ward Administration Times dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">a</span></strong> to display the Patient Ward Administration Times dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Patient Ward Administration Times Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/682.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><ol start="2" type="1">

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconviewingprinting-a-medication-history-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/696.png)Viewing/Printing a Medication History Report</h3></td>
<td><p>BCMA provides two ways to access a patient’s Medication History Report (or Med History Report). They include the Med History command in the Due List menu and in the Right Click drop-down menu.</p>
<p>This Report lists the administration date and time, and orderable item of an Inpatient or Clinic medication selected on the BCMA VDL. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.” It also includes the medication status, schedule type, and dose; room location; and initials of the clinician who administered the medication.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> A Medication History Report is called an “Administration History Report” in CPRS. You can access it by selecting the Meds Tab in CPRS, and then right clicking on a medication.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Date column lists three asterisks (*) to indicate that a medication is not due. This information is also noted in the Legend at the bottom of the MAH Report.</p>
<p>The report also includes information about when an order is placed “On Hold” and taken “Off Hold” by a provider, and the order Start and Stop Date/Time for the medication.</p>
<p>To view/print a Medication History Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Med History command from the Due List menu. The Medication History dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+d</span></strong> to display the Due List menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">e</span></strong> to display the Medication History dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<colgroup>
<col style="width: 32%" />

</blockquote></li>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-a-medication-variance-log-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing a Medication Variance Log Report</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/699.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/700.png)</p></td>
<td><p>With GUI BCMA, you can print the Medication Variance Log Report by patient or by ward, using the Medication Variance Log in the Reports menu.</p>
<p>This Report lists “event” information within a selected date range, such as the type and number of events (i.e., Early/Late/PRN), and the total percentage of events that occurred. It also includes the medication type, date/time of the variance, and the initials of and comments by the clinician who administered the medication.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clinic orders are excluded from the Medication Variance Log report.</p>
<p>To view/print a Medication Variance Log Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Medication Variance Log command from the Reports menu. The Medication Variance Log dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">e</span></strong> to display the Medication Variance Log dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Medication Variance Log Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/701.png)</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/702.png)Viewing/Printing a Medication Variance Log Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Start and Stop Dates and Times of the Medication Variance Log Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Start/Stop Date list boxes displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provides selections.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the different areas of the dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the Print by area, select to print by Patient or Ward.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you choose to print the report by Patient, go to step 6.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you choose to print the report by Ward, make your selection from the Ward list box provided.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> to select the Ward, and then select a ward location from the drop-down list box.</p>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>To include Inactive Wards, click inside the check box to deselect the default “Exclude Inactive Wards.”</p></li>
<li><p>Select Sort by Patient (default), Sort by Room-Bed, or Print Selected Patients on Ward.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you choose to print selected patients, click <strong><span class="smallcaps">select patients</span></strong> and then select the patients’ orders you want to preview or print.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-the-patient-record-flag-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/708.png)Viewing/Printing the Patient Record Flag Report</h3>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/709.png)</p></td>
<td><p>The Patient Record Flag report displays all active PRF assignments associated with the patient. Applicable National (Category I) and Local (Category II) flag types are displayed. When the <strong><span class="smallcaps">flag</span></strong> button is enabled on the tool bar, it signifies that the current patient on the VDL has one or more active Patient Record Flags (PRFs). The PRF alerts VHA employees to patients whose behavior or characteristics may pose a threat either to their safety, the safety of other patients, or compromise the delivery of quality health care.</p>
<p>There are two ways to access the Patient Record Flag Report:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>From the VDL:</strong> Click the flag button (displayed in RED) on the tool bar to view and print the Patient Record Flag Report. A Patient Flag option is also available on the View menu.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>During the patient look-up process:</strong> Click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">details</span></strong> button on the Patient Confirmation dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If any active PRFs exist for a patient, it is strongly recommended that you run the Patient Record Flag report to view the active patient record flag details, especially for behavioral flags, to view information which may be critical to patient and employee safety.</p>
<p>In addition to patient demographic data, the following information is displayed on the Patient Record Flag Report:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Flag Name:</strong> The nationally or locally assigned name of patient record flag.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Flag Type:</strong> Identifies the usage classification of the Patient Record Flag, e.g., BEHAVIORAL, CLINICAL, OTHER, RESEARCH.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Flag Category</strong>: Category I Behavioral National PRFs are nationally approved and are to be used by all facilities. Category II Local PRFs may be locally</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Viewing/Printing the Patient Record Flag Report (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>established by individual Veterans Integrated Service Networks (VISNs) or facilities.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Assignment Status:</strong> Active or Inactive; only Active PRFs display on the PRF Report.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Initial Assigned Date:</strong> The date the PRF was initially assigned to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Approved by:</strong> The provider who approved the assignment.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Next Review Date:</strong> The date that the flag assignment is due for review to determine continuing appropriateness.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Owner Site:</strong> The current site that owns this patient flag assignment. Patient assignments may only be edited by the owner site. The owner site normally corresponds to the site providing primary care to the patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Originating Site:</strong> The site that initially assigned the patient record flag to this patient. The site that assigns the flag is not required to be the owner of the assignment.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p><strong>Assignment Narratives:</strong> Description of the incident or reason that generated the need for this patient record flag assignment. The description is followed by recommended actions that should be performed by a person working with this specific patient.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-an-unknown-actions-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing an Unknown Actions Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Unknown Actions Report to print a listing of administrations that have an unknown action status within a specified date range. When a user is in the process of documenting an administration in BCMA CHUI <em>Manual Medication Entry</em>, the administration status initially defaults to blank (null). If the order is not completed with a valid administration status, the Admin Status will be listed as unknown, and appear on the Unknown Actions Report.</p>
<p>The unknown (null) status can occur during <em>Manual Medication Entry</em> when the user’s network connection is broken, their terminal emulator software malfunctions, or if the user improperly exits out of the application.</p>
<p>Use the BCMA GUI Edit Med Log to correct the administration status of any entries found on this report.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> This report is only accessible to users with the PSB MANAGER security key.</p>
<p>The Unknown Actions Report includes information about the administration with the Unknown status, including patient name and ID, ward/bed, the order number, orderable item, schedule and scheduled administration time, who created the order, and the time the order was created.</p>
<p>To view/print an Unknown Actions Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Unknown Actions command from the Reports menu. The Unknown Actions dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">u</span></strong> to display the Unknown Actions dialog box.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-cover-sheet-reports" class="Subheading-Style"><br />
Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet Reports</h3></td>
<td><p>Cover Sheet Reports can be accessed from the BCMA GUI Reports menu and then previewed and/or printed. They include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Medication Overview</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>PRN Overview</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>IV Overview</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p>The Cover Sheet Reports mimic the Coversheet, which is patient based, so the reports are designed to be patient based as well, not ward based like the other reports. To print for a group of patients, you must select multiple patients. When selecting multiple patients, a single patient report is printed for each patient selected.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> When including Clinic Orders in the Cover Sheet Reports, parameters for Allowable Time Limits (Before Scheduled Admin Time and After Scheduled Admin Time) are ignored.</p>
<p>Example: Cover Sheet Reports Menu</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/718.png)</p>
<p>To view/print a Cover Sheet Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Cover Sheet command from the Reports menu and then select the Cover Sheet Report you want to see.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> It is not necessary to display the Cover Sheet in order to run a Cover Sheet Report. Cover Sheet reports can be run from the Reports Menu at any time.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet Reports (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>The appropriate report dialog box displays. Refer to the following sections for more information on each report dialog box.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">c</span></strong> to display the Cover Sheet dialog box.</p>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">e</span></strong> to display the Medication Overview dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Press r to display the PRN Overview dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Press o to display the IV Overview dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Press x to display the Expired/DC’d/Expiring dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-cover-sheetmedication-overview-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report</h3></td>
<td><p>The Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report displays and groups active, expired or discontinued, and future orders for the current patient and by ward. The total number of orders per group displays in brackets next to each group heading.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report can be accessed from the Reports menu and then previewed and/or printed.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report provides three levels of detail for each order displayed.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>The top level displays order and next administration data, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Order Status: the current status of the order (i.e., Active, Expired, Hold)</p></li>
<li><p>Type: the schedule type of the order (C for Continuous, O for One Time, OC for On Call, P for PRN)</p></li>
<li><p>Medication; Dosage, Route: the orderable item associated with the order; plus the dosage and route of the order separated by a comma</p></li>
<li><p>Schedule: the order schedule (i.e., Q2H, BID)</p></li>
<li><p>Next Action: one of the following:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>“DUE”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action taken for active orders that have defined administration times in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p><strong>“Missed”</strong> followed by the next scheduled administration time after the last action</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report (cont.)</th>
<th><p>taken if administration date/time exceeds the “After Scheduled Admin Time” site parameter in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format.</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>“Provider Hold”</strong> for active orders on provider hold</p></li>
<li><p>Blank for PRN, On Call, and One-Time orders</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p>Order Stop Date: the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against this specific order, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Actions whose activity dates exceed the “Med History Days Back” site parameter will not be displayed.</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: If the order is an IV order, then the Bag ID header and field displays, which is the unique identifier for the bag associated with this action.</p></li>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action, and the date/time of the action in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the status of the administration (i.e., Given, Held, Refused, Missing, etc.).</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–Medication Overview Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>If the order has a PRN schedule type, the following headers and fields will display:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>PRN Reason:</strong> the PRN reason associated with the action</p></li>
<li><p><strong>PRN Effectiveness:</strong> the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Comment By: the initials of the person that entered the comment and the date/time the comment was entered in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment</p></li>
</ul>
<p>To view/print a Cover Sheet Medication Overview Report</p>

</ol></td>

</blockquote></li>

<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-cover-sheetprn-overview-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report</h3></td>
<td><p>The Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report displays and groups active expired or discontinued and future orders with a schedule type of PRN for the current patient and by ward. The total number of orders per group displays in brackets next to each group heading. The Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report can be accessed from the Reports menu and then previewed and/or printed.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report provides three levels of detail for each order displayed.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>The top level displays order and next administration data, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Status: the current status of the order (i.e., Active, Expired, Hold)</p></li>
<li><p>Medication; Dosage, Route: the orderable item associated with the order, including multiple dispense drugs, additives, and solutions; plus the dosage and route of the order separated by a comma</p></li>
<li><p>Last Given: the last administration and the date/time the action was performed for the orderable item in ACTION MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Since Last Given: the number of hours and minutes since the last administration of the orderable item in ##d ##h ##m format (e.g., 1d 10h 23m)</p></li>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions associated with the order</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–PRN Overview Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Order Stop Date: the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against this specific order, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p>
<p>Note: Actions whose activity dates exceed the “Med History Days Back” site parameter will not be displayed.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: If the order is an IV order, then the Bag ID displays, which is the unique identifier for the bag associated with this action. The Bag ID header will not display unless the order type of the order is “IV.”</p></li>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action, and the date/time of the action in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the action that was performed.</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Reason: the PRN reason associated with the action</p></li>
<li><p>PRN Effectiveness: the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>The third level displays comments associated with the action and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Comment By: the initials of the person that entered the comment and the date/time the comment was entered in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment</p>
<p>The report header displays “Include Inpatient Orders Only” for reports that include only Inpatient order data.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="viewingprinting-cover-sheetiv-overview-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report</h3></th>
<th><p>The Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report displays and groups IV bag information on active, expired, and discontinued orders for the current patient and by ward. The total number of IV bags per group displays in brackets next to each group heading.</p>
<p>The Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report can be accessed from the Reports menu and then previewed and/or printed.</p>
<p>The groups display top down in the following order:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Infusing: any bag that is currently infusing on an active, expired, or discontinued order</p></li>
<li><p>Stopped: any bag that is currently stopped on an active, expired, or discontinued order</p></li>
<li><p>All Other: any bag that is not infusing or stopped on an active order</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report provides two levels of detail for each order displayed.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>The top level displays bag and order data, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: the unique identifier of the bag.</p></li>
<li><p>Order Status: the current status of the order to which the bag belongs</p></li>
<li><p>Bag Status: the current status of the bag (Infusing, Stopped, Available, Complete).</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Bag status is blank for active IV orders that have no bags associated with them.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Medication; Dosage, Route: the orderable item associated with the order, including additives and solutions; plus the dosage and route of the order separated by a comma.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–IV Overview Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ul>
<li><p>Infusion Rate: the infusion rate associated with the order.</p></li>
<li><p>Other Print Info: other print information associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Bag Info: “changed order” if the bag is associated with an order that has been edited</p></li>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Order Stop Date: the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays the bag history (actions and comments) and contains the following header and information&gt;</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> A maximum of four previous actions display at the second level. Actions with activity date exceeding the “Med History Days Back” site parameter do not display.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Date/Time: If the order is an IV order, then the Bag ID displays, which is the unique identifier for the bag associated with this action.</p></li>
<li><p>By: the initials of the person that performed the action or entered the comment.</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the action that was performed.</p></li>
<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment.</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</blockquote></li>

<p>If the selected Order Mode is “Clinic:”</p>
</blockquote></li>

</blockquote></li>

<p>If no patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>

</blockquote></li>

</ol>

<ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>In the Print by area, select to print by Patient or Ward.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The report dialog Print by selection always defaults to “Patient.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the “Inpatient” Order Mode is selected on the VDL, the report dialog Include Orders selection defaults to “Inpatient Orders” and Print by “Ward” is enabled, and Print by “Clinic” is disabled.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></td>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-cover-sheetexpireddcd-expiring-orders-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–Expired/DC’d/ Expiring Orders Report</h3></td>
<td><p>The Cover Sheet–Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders Report displays and groups expired and discontinued orders, as well as orders that will expire for the current patient and by ward. For each group, the total number of IV bags per group is displayed in brackets next to the group heading. The Cover Sheet– Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders Report can be accessed from the Reports menu and then previewed and/or printed.</p>
<p>The groups display top down in the following order:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Expired/DC’d: orders that have expired or discontinued within the last 24 hours.</p></li>
<li><p>Expiring Today: orders that have not yet expired, but will expire before midnight of the current day</p></li>
<li><p>Expiring Tomorrow: orders that expire after midnight of the current day but before midnight of the next day</p></li>
</ul>
<p>The Cover Sheet Expired/DC’d/Expiring Orders Report provides three levels of detail for each order displayed.</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>The top level displays order and next administration data, and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>VDL Tab: the name of the tab within BCMA where administrations are displayed.</p></li>
<li><p>Status: the current status of the order (i.e., Active, Expired, Hold)</p></li>
<li><p>Type: the schedule type of the order</p></li>
<li><p>Medication; Dosage, Route: the orderable item associated with the order, including multiple dispense drugs, additives, and solutions; plus the dosage and route of the order separated by a comma</p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Viewing/Printing Cover Sheet–Expired/DC’d/ Expiring Orders Report (cont.)</th>
<th><ul>
<li><p>Schedule: the order schedule (i.e., Q2H, BID).</p></li>
<li><p>Special Instructions: special instructions associated with the order</p></li>
<li><p>Order Start Date: the order’s start date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
<li><p>Order Stop Date: the order’s stop date/time displayed in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>The second level displays a maximum of four previous actions taken against the order and contains the following header and information:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Bag ID: if the order is an IV order, the Bag ID displays.</p></li>
<li><p>Action By: the initials of the person that performed the action and the date/time of the action in MM/DD/YYYY@HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p>Action: the action that was performed.</p></li>
<li><p>If the order has a PRN schedule type, the following headers and fields will display:</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>PRN Reason: the PRN reason associated with the action</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>PRN Effectiveness: the PRN Effectiveness comment for this action</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>The third level displays comments associated with the action and includes the following header and information in the order listed below.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><p>Comment By: the initials of the person that entered the comment and the date/time the comment was entered in MM/DD/YYYY@ HHMM format.</p></li>
<li><p>Comment: the text of the comment.</p></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-a-medication-therapy-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing a Medication Therapy Report</h3></td>
<td><p>The Medication Therapy Report is similar to the Medication History Report, but contains additional information and does not require a patient record to be open. If no patient record is open, it defaults to a ward-based report. If a patient record is open, the report searches the current patient’s administrations.</p>
<p>The Medication Therapy Report allows users to search by VA Drug Class, orderable item, or dispense drug on an Inpatient or Clinic medication order. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.” The report searches through all of currently admitted patients’ previous administrations that fall within the specified date range and match the specified schedule types and selected medications.</p>
<p>To view/print a Medication Therapy Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Medication Therapy command from the Reports menu. The Medication Therapy dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">t</span></strong> to display the Medication Therapy dialog box.</p></td>

<td>Viewing/Printing a Medication Therapy Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>In the Drug Search Category, click a category to choose the method by which you want to search for a medication. Choices include Dispensed Drugs, IV Medications, Orderable Item (default), and VA Drug Class. Regardless of the drug category you choose for searching, the search results will return Dispensed Drugs.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Currently, when searching by VA Drug Class, BCMA accepts only VA Drug Class Classification Text, not VA Drug Class Codes.</p>
<ol start="7" type="1">
<li><p>In the Search Criteria area, enter search text as applicable. If you are unsure of the spelling of an item, you can enter a partial name. Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">enter</span></strong> or click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">search</span></strong> button.</p></li>
<li><p>When Search Results display, select the medications you want on the report using one of the following methods:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To select only one medication, click its name and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">add</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To select all listed medications, click one and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">add all</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To remove a medication that was selected by mistake, click its name in the Selected Medications area and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">remove</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>To remove all medications in the Selected Medications area, click one name and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">remove all</span></strong>.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> To select medications from the Search Results or Selected Medications lists, use <strong><span class="smallcaps">ctl+click</span></strong> or <strong><span class="smallcaps">shift+click</span></strong> for each name. To select all medications in a list, use <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+a</span></strong>.</p></td>
</tr>

<li><p>In the Print by area, select to print by Patient or Ward. The Inpatient nurse and Clinic nurse will print by Patient.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If a patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The “Print by Patient” option is enabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Patient.”</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If no patient record is open:</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The “Print by Patient” option is disabled, and the report dialog Print by selection defaults to “Ward.” The nurse can select one patient on the Ward.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Print by Clinic is disabled.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If you choose to print the report by Patient, go to step 12.</p>
<ol start="11" type="1">
<li><p>If you choose to print the report by Ward, make your selection from the list box provided. Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Ward list box displays an alphabetical list of MAS wards and Nurse Units.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> After selecting a ward, you must select patients within that ward before running the report.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> To include Inactive Wards, click inside the check box to deselect the default “Exclude Inactive Wards.”</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> to select the Ward, and then select a ward location from the drop-down list box.</p></th>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-an-iv-bag-status-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing an IV Bag Status Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can print (and view) a patient’s IV Bag Status Report, which provides status on IV bags, excluding available bags, by patient or by selected patients on the ward for Inpatient or Clinic orders. The following message appears on each report dialog: “This report includes both Inpatient and Clinic Order data.” Users can include/exclude completed, infusing, stopped, missing, held, and refused IV bags, as well as bags for which no action has been taken on the order.</p>
<p>To view/print an IV Bag Status Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the IV Bag Status command from the Reports menu. The Medication Therapy dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">b</span></strong> to display the IV Bag Status dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: IV Bag Status Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/754.png)</p>

<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Start and Stop Dates of the IV Bag Status Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>

<td><h3 id="viewingprinting-an-unable-to-scan-detailed-report" class="Subheading-Style">Viewing/Printing an Unable to Scan (Detailed) Report</h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Unable to Scan (Detailed) Report to view/print detailed information for each scanning failure logged via Unable to Scan functionality. Report data for a wristband scanning failure is collected after you complete the Unable to Scan process and successfully select, confirm, and open the patient record. Report data for a medication scanning failure is collected after you complete the Unable to Scan process and complete all steps of the medication administration. Canceling out of the Unable to Scan process or canceling a medication administration at any point in the process will not log the Unable to Scan event. Only logged Unable to Scan events print on the Detailed report. It is not necessary to open a patient record in order to view/print this report.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> This report is only accessible to users with the PSB UNABLE TO SCAN security key. The report only includes data for Inpatient administrations.</p>
<p>To view/print an Unable to Scan (Detailed) Report</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icon-viewingprinting-an-unable-to-scan-summary-report" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/761.png)<br />
Viewing/Printing an Unable to Scan (Summary) Report </h3></td>
<td><p>You can use the Unable to Scan (Summary) Report to view/print the total number and percentages of wristbands scanned, wristbands by-passed, medications scanned, and medications by-passed. It is not necessary to open a patient record in order to view/print this report.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> This report is only accessible to users with the PSB UNABLE TO SCAN security key. The report only includes data for Inpatient administrations.</p>
<p>To view/print an Unable to Scan (Summary) Report</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the Unable to Scan (Summary) command from the Reports menu. The Unable to Scan (Summary) dialog box displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">alt+r</span></strong> to display the Reports menu, and then press <strong><span class="smallcaps">s</span></strong> to display the Unable to Scan (Summary) dialog box.</p>
<p>Example: Unable to Scan (Summary) Dialog Box</p>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/762.png)</p>
<ol start="2" type="1">
<li><p>Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within the list boxes, to select the Start and Stop Dates for the Unable to Scan (Summary) Report that you want to view on-screen or print.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Viewing/Printing an Unable to Scan (Summary) Report (cont.)</th>
<th><p><strong>Note:</strong> Clicking on the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong> on the Start Date and Stop Date list boxes displays a calendar. You can use the scroll arrows in the upper corners of the calendar to display a different month, and then click on a date to select it and close the calendar. Clicking inside the Start/Stop Time list boxes provides selections.</p>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the different areas of the dialog box.</p>
<ol start="3" type="1">
<li><p>In the For area, select the Entire Facility radio button, Nurse Unit/Location radio button, or the Ward radio button.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Entire Facility option prints a one page report containing grand totals and percentages for your entire Division. This option is filtered by the Division you selected when you logged into BCMA.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Nurse Unit/Location option prints a summary report page for each Nurse Unit in your Division (one unit per page). This option is filtered by the Division you selected when you logged into BCMA.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>The Ward option allows you print a summary report for a selected MAS Ward or Nurse Unit.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ol start="4" type="1">
<li><p>If you choose to print the report by Ward, make your selection from the list box provided. Clicking on the <strong>DOWN</strong> <strong>ARROW</strong> on the Ward list box displays an alphabetical list of MAS Wards and/or Nurse Units.</p></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> To include Inactive Wards in the list box, click inside the check box to deselect the default “Exclude Inactive Wards.”</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> To include MAS Wards in the list box, click inside the check box to deselect the default “Exclude MAS Wards.”</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Viewing/Printing an Unable to Scan (Summary) Report (cont.)</td>
<td><ol start="5" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>PREVIEW</strong> to display the report on screen.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> to display the Printer dialog box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Click <strong>CANCEL</strong> to return to the patient’s VDL.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Use <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the <strong>PREVIEW</strong>, <strong><span class="smallcaps">print</span></strong> and <strong><span class="smallcaps">cancel</span></strong> buttons.</p>
<ol start="6" type="1">
<li><p>Perform one or more of the following actions, then click <strong>OK</strong>:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select a printer from the drop-down list box that you want to use for ouputting the Unable to Scan (Summary) report.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Check the Queuing check box and enter the Date and Time you want the report to print. Click the DOWN ARROW in the drop-down list box to display a choice of dates and times.</p>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The printer that you select becomes the “default” printer for <em>all</em> reports printed from <strong>BCMA.</strong></p></li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

Example: Unable to Scan (Summary) Report

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/763.png)

<span id="_Toc3682571" class="anchor"></span>Chapter 12: Understanding the CPRS Med Order Button

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="benefits-of-this-chapter-8" class="Subheading-Style">Benefits of this Chapter</h3></th>
<th><p>This chapter describes the process for using the CPRS Med Order Button (or “Hot Button”) in BCMA V. 3.0. It describes the many benefits of this new enhancement, and the steps for using it — plus it provides a flow chart for you to discover the workflow using this button.</p>
<p>Note: At this time, Clinic Orders cannot be created using the CPRS Med Order Button. This functionality is scheduled to be implemented in a future release of CPRS.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 31%" />
<col style="width: 68%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-icontip-box-with-lightbulb-iconproviding-a-link-to-cprs" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/764.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/765.png)Providing a Link to CPRS</h3></th>
<th><p>BCMA V. 3.0 includes the CPRS Med Order Button, a “link” to CPRS for electronically ordering, documenting, reviewing, and signing verbal- and phone-type STAT and (One-Time) medication orders for Unit Dose and IV medications that you have already administered to patients. This feature is particularly beneficial in ICU-type environments, as it helps streamline the workflow in such a busy setting. For instance, this button provides a secure, seamless environment for interfacing with three VistA applications to electronically document the medication administration process. They include BCMA V. 3.0, CPRS V. 1.0, and Inpatient Medications V. 5.0.</p>
<p>How the CPRS Med Order Button Works</p>
<p>Using the “Hot Button” in BCMA is quick and easy. Simply click the CPRS Med Order button on the BCMA VDL Tool Bar to perform tasks using the BCMA Order Manager and CPRS Order dialog boxes. These order types are then passed to the Inpatient Medications V. 5.0 software application as “nurse-verified” expired orders with a priority of “Done.” A pharmacist must still verify these order types. The provider selected during the Ordering process will receive an “alert,” requesting their electronic signature on the order.</p>
<p>Verifying the Documentation Process</p>
<p>Order types documented with the CPRS Med Order button do not display on the BCMA VDL <em>unless</em> they are large-volume IV or non-intermittent syringe type orders administered over a period of time. In that case, they display on the BCMA VDL under the IV Medication Tab as “Infusing.”</p>
<p>You can, however, print the Medication Log and the MAH Reports from the Reports menu (or Tool Bar) within BCMA, or using the Reports Tab in CPRS, to verify that these orders were properly documented. On the Medication Log, the text titled “BCMA/CPRS Interface Entry,” displays opposite the order. You can edit these orders using the Edit Medication Log [PSB MED LOG EDIT] option in the CHUI version of BCMA.</p></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
</tbody>
</table>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="enabling-the-cprs-med-order-button-functionality" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/766.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/767.png)Enabling the CPRS Med Order Button Functionality</h3></td>
<td><p>You can enable the CPRS Med Order Button functionality, at your division, by performing the steps listed below.</p>
<p>To enable the CPRS Med Order Button functionality</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Select the “Enable CPRS Med Order Button” check box under the Parameters Tab of the GUI BCMA Site Parameters application.</p></li>
<li><p>Assign the secondary menus “PSB GUI CONTEXT – USER” and “OR BCMA ORDER COM” to each BCMA user.</p></li>
<li><p>Assign the PSB CPRS MED BUTTON security key to appropriate site personnel.</p></li>
<li><p>Verify that the user has been assigned the ORELSE security key associated with CPRS.</p></li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<span id="_Toc6549281" class="anchor"></span>

Workflow for CPRS Med Order Button

![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/768.png)

<span id="_Toc105057255" class="anchor"></span>Using the CPRS Med Order Button

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><h3 id="tip-box-with-lightbulb-iconordering-and-documenting-stat-or-now-orders" class="Subheading-Style">![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/769.png)![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/770.png)Ordering and Documenting STAT or NOW Orders</h3></td>
<td><p>Follow the instructions in this section to use the CPRS Med Order Button from the BCMA VDL. Once you activate the button, BCMA passes patient data from the BCMA Order Manager dialog box to CPRS, for ordering, documenting, reviewing, and signing STAT or NOW medication orders already administered to patients.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The patient that you are ordering and documenting orders about must have a status and location of “inpatient.”</p>
<p>To order/document STAT or NOW orders</p>
<ol type="1">
<li><p>Click the <strong><span class="smallcaps">cprs med order</span></strong> button on the Tool Bar of the BCMA VDL. The BCMA Order Manager Dialog box then displays.</p></li>
</ol>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/771.png)Example: BCMA Order Manager Dialog Box</p></td>

<td><ol start="12" type="1">
<li><p>Under the Order Type area of the dialog box, perform one of the following actions:</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select the Unit Dose Radio button if you want to order/document a STAT or NOW Unit Dose medication. Proceed to step #3.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Select the IV Radio button if you want to order/document a STAT or NOW IV medication. Then complete the IV’s area of the dialog box, and proceed to step #3.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>The fields that need completed under the IVs area of the dialog box relate to the IV Type selected.</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="13" type="1">
<li><p>Complete the Provider field, and then press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to move to the Injection Site field, and complete that field if applicable to the order.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If you enter the provider’s full last name and first name, BCMA finds an exact match.</p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>![](psb-3-155-bcma-gui-user-manual/773.png)<strong>If you enter the provider’s last name or a portion of their last name</strong> and then press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab,</strong></span> BCMA provides matches in a list box so you can select the correct provider for the order.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><p>The provider selected for this field will receive an “alert” notifying them that they need to sign the order.</p></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Keyboard Shortcut:</strong> Press <strong><span class="smallcaps">tab</span></strong> to move among the fields within the dialog box. Use the <strong><span class="smallcaps">down arrow</span></strong>, within a list box, to make your selection.</p></td>
</tr>

<table>
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 30%" />
<col style="width: 69%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Ordering and Documenting STAT or NOW Orders (cont.)</th>
<th><ol start="14" type="1">
<li><p>Complete the Action Date/Time field, and then press <span class="smallcaps"><strong>tab</strong></span> to display your date/time entry and continue with the order/document process.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>Enter the date and time when you administered the medication to the patient, using the VA FileMan Date/Time formatting guidelines listed below. Keep in mind that the system does not accept a date/time in the future.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul>
<h3 id="date-formatting-3">Date Formatting</h3>
<ul>
<li><p>May 1, 2010, 01 MAY 10, 5/01/10, 050110</p></li>
<li><p>N (for NOW)</p></li>
<li><p>T (for Today)</p></li>
<li><p>T-1 (for Yesterday)</p></li>
</ul>
<h3 id="time-formatting-3">Time Formatting</h3>
<ul>
<li><p>00:00 (For example, 14:00 for 2:00 p.m.)</p></li>
</ul>
<ol start="15" type="1">
<li><p>Scan the bar code number on the Unit Dose medication or IV Additive/Solution ordered for the patient. BCMA will process the scan, and then display the medication or additive/solution in the Medications and/or Solutions Scanned list box.</p></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If multiple drugs are available for the selected order, BCMA provides a list box with choices. Select the medication that you want to document/order, and then click <strong><span class="smallcaps">ok</span></strong> to enter your selection in the Medications and/or Solutions Scanned list box<span class="smallcaps">.</span></p>
</blockquote></li>
<li><blockquote>
<p>If the bar code is missing or unreadable, enter one or more alpha characters in the Scan Medication Bar Code field, and then press enter. BCMA will perform a look-up for you, and then display its findings. Select a drug name, and then click ok to enter your selection directly into the Medications and/or Solutions Scanned list box.</p>
</blockquote></li>
</ul></th>
</tr>
</thead>

</tr>
